Al-Hakim Abu Abd Allah: A Biographical Sketch
Ibn Asakir provides a brief biography of al-Hakim with name, teachers, and dates.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will know the basic biographical details of al-Hakim al-Naysaburi as recorded by Ibn Asakir.

Core Idea
Al-Hakim’s biography is a testament to his vast learning and early start in hadith.

Ibn Asakir presents a concise biographical notice of the renowned hadith scholar al-Hakim Abu Abd Allah. This passage gives us his full name, his status as a hafiz, his numerous teachers, and key dates. Let's examine the details.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Pay attention to the full name and lineage.
2
Identify key terms
Find the terms حافظ, روى عن ألف شيخ, and التصنيف. Understand what they mean in context.
حافظ refers to a master memorizer of hadith.
3
Analyze the dates
Note the birth year (321 AH), the start of compilation (337 AH), and the death year (405 AH). Calculate his age at these milestones.
4
Reflect on the significance of his teachers
Consider what it means to have narrated from over a thousand shaykhs. Why is this noteworthy?
This indicates extensive travel and dedication to hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الحسن عبد الغافر بن إسماعيل في كتابه قال : محمد بن عبد الله بن محمد بن حمدويه بن نعيم بن الحكم أبو عبد الله الحافظ روى عن ألف شيخ أو أكثر من أهل الحديث ولد في شهر ربيع الأول سنة إحدى وعشرين وثلاثمائة وأخذ في التصنيف سنة سبع وثلاثين وثلاثمائة وتوفى فى صفر يوم الثلاثاء الثالث منه سنة خمس وأربعمائة
Shaykh Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Ghafir ibn Isma'il informed us in his book, saying: Muhammad ibn Abd Allah ibn Muhammad ibn Hamdawayh ibn Nu'aym ibn al-Hakam, Abu Abd Allah al-Hafiz. He narrated from a thousand shaykhs or more of the people of hadith. He was born in the month of Rabi' al-Awwal, year 321 AH. He began compilation in the year 337 AH. And he died in Safar, on Tuesday, the third of it, year 405 AH.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is a concise biographical entry for al-Hakim Abu Abd Allah (the famous hadith scholar and author of al-Mustadrak). It provides his full name and lineage, his status as a hafiz (master memorizer of hadith), his immense number of teachers (over a thousand), his birth date (Rabi' al-Awwal 321 AH), his start of authorship (337 AH), and his death date (Safar 405 AH). This is a standard biographical notice in the Tabyin.

Key Terms
حافظ
روى عن ألف شيخ
التصنيف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which year did al-Hakim die?
A) 321 AH
B) 337 AH
C) 405 AH
D) 401 AH

Key Takeaway
Al-Hakim's biography highlights his exceptional teachers and early start in hadith scholarship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Hakim began compiling hadith at the age of 16. You are likely older than that right now. What are you doing today—this very week—to preserve or share the knowledge of this deen? Write one concrete action you will take before the next 7 days end.
?
He learned from over a thousand shaykhs. Are you humble enough to learn from those around you, even those younger or less known? Who is one person you have been neglecting to ask for knowledge? Commit today to seek one lesson from them.
?
Al-Hakim died leaving a legacy of compilation. If you were to die tonight, what would you leave behind for the Ummah in terms of knowledge or service? Be specific and honest—then take one step to fill that gap starting tomorrow.

Abu Nasr al-Isma'ili: Scholar and Son of a Scholar
Ibn Asakir details the life and teaching career of Abu Nasr al-Isma'ili.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and scholarly career of Abu Nasr al-Isma'ili, including his role as a teacher, his travels, and his death date.

Core Idea
A scholar who led and taught while his father still lived.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's work provides a detailed account of the life of Abu Nasr al-Isma'ili, a prominent hadith scholar from Jurjan. It traces his early leadership, his educational lineage, and his dedication to teaching. As you read, pay attention to the details of his academic career and the significance of his book al-'Aqd.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography carefully
Read through the Arabic and translation to get the full account of his life.
Notice the chain of transmission at the beginning.
2
Note the key events
Pay attention to his early leadership, his teachers, the mosques where he taught, and his death date.
3
Reflect on the chain of transmission
Observe how the information is transmitted through an isnad, a typical feature of Islamic biographical writing.
This shows the importance of oral transmission in Islamic scholarship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم أبو نصر بن أبي بكر الإسماعيلي الجرجاني ) • أخبرنا أبو القسم إسماعيل بن أحمد بن السمرقندى قال أنا أبو القسم إسماعيل بن مسعدة الجرجاني ، قال أنا أبو القسم حمزة بن يوسف السهمى إجازة أو سماعا في تاريخ جرجان قال : أبو نصر محمد ابن أحمد بن إبراهيم بن إسماعيل بن العباس الإسماعيلي ترأس في حياة والده أبي بكر الإسماعيلى وبعد وفاته إلى أن توفي وكان له جاه عظيم وقبول عند الخاص والعام في كثير من البلدان وتحل بكتابه العقد وكان كتب الحديث الكثير عن أبي يعقوب البحيرى وأبى العباس الأصم وبالعراق وبمكة وبالرى وهمذان وكان يعرف الحديث ويدرى وأول ما جلس للاملاء في حياة والده أبي بكر الإسماعيلي في سنة ست وستين في مسجد الصفارين إلى أن توفى والده ثم انتقل إلى المسجد الذي كان والده يملى فيه ويملى كل يوم سبت إلى أن توفى وكانت وفاته في يوم الأحد و دفن يوم الاثنين لثلاث بقين من شهر ربيع الآخر سنة خمس وأربعمائة وصلى عليه أبو معمر الإسماعيلي
And among them is Abu Nasr ibn Abi Bakr al-Isma'ili al-Jurjani. • Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi informed us, saying: Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Mas'ada al-Jurjani narrated to us, saying: Abu al-Qasim Hamza ibn Yusuf al-Sahmi narrated to us, by permission or hearing, in the History of Jurjan, saying: Abu Nasr Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-Abbas al-Isma'ili. He held leadership during the lifetime of his father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili and after his death until he himself died. He had great prestige and acceptance among the elite and commoners in many lands. He was adorned with his book al-'Aqd. He wrote many hadith from Abu Ya'qub al-Buhayri, Abu al-Abbas al-Asamm, in Iraq, Mecca, Rayy, and Hamadhan. He knew hadith and understood it. His first sitting for dictation was during the lifetime of his father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili in the year 366 in the mosque of the coppersmiths, until his father died. Then he moved to the mosque where his father used to dictate, and he dictated every Saturday until he died. His death was on Sunday, and he was buried on Monday, with three nights remaining in Rabi' al-Akhir, year 405 AH. Abu Mu'ammar al-Isma'ili prayed over him.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This is another biography in the series, introduced with 'wa minhum' (and among them). The author provides a chain of transmission (isnad) for the information. It describes Abu Nasr al-Isma'ili as the son of the famous Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili. He assumed leadership and had great influence. He authored a book called al-'Aqd. He traveled widely to collect hadith. He began teaching dictation in his father's lifetime and continued in his father's mosque after his death. His death date is given: Rabi' al-Akhir 405 AH.

Key Terms
الإسماعيلي
الإملاء
العقد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Where did Abu Nasr al-Isma'ili first dictate hadith?
A) In the mosque of the coppersmiths
B) In the Great Mosque of Jurjan
C) In the mosque of his father
D) In Baghdad

Key Takeaway
Abu Nasr al-Isma'ili was a respected hadith scholar who began teaching during his father's lifetime and continued until his death in 405 AH.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Abu Nasr began dictating hadith while his father, a renowned scholar, was still alive. What knowledge or skill do you have that you could begin sharing with others today, even before you feel 'fully ready'? What is holding you back?
?
He taught every Saturday until his death. What consistent act of service—whether teaching, helping, or learning—are you willing to commit to for the rest of your life? Write down one specific commitment.
?
His prestige and acceptance came from both elite and commoners. Are you more concerned with impressing those above you or serving those around you? How can you seek Allah's acceptance over human praise?

The Life and Legacy of Abu Bakr ibn Furak
Ibn Asakir recounts the life and scholarly activity of Abu Bakr ibn Furak, an Ash'ari theologian.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key events in the life of Abu Bakr ibn Furak, including his scholarly journey and role in reviving Sunni knowledge in Nishapur.

Core Idea
Ibn Furak's life shows how Ash'ari scholars overcame opposition to revive knowledge.

This passage from Tabyin Kidhb al-Muftari presents the biography of Abu Bakr ibn Furak, a prominent Ash'ari theologian. It traces his early studies in Iraq, his encounter with opposition in Rayy, and his eventual establishment in Nishapur, where he became a central figure in reviving Islamic sciences. The narrative also includes a curious anecdote about a fellow scholar's refusal to pray for him, hinting at deeper spiritual dimensions.

Guided Path
1
Read Ibn Furak's full name and titles
Notice the list of scholarly descriptors: literary scholar, theologian, legal theorist, preacher, grammarian. This sets the stage for his stature.
The Arabic 'al-adib al-mutakallim al-usuli al-wa'iz al-nahwi'.
2
Trace his geographical journey
Identify the cities: first Iraq, then Rayy, then Nishapur. Note the events at each stop.
3
Understand the opposition and support
In Rayy, the 'mubtadi'a' slandered him, but the Ahl al-Sunna rallied and arranged his move to Nishapur.
The term 'mubtadi'a' refers to those who deviate from Sunni orthodoxy.
4
Reflect on the anecdote about al-Daqqaq
The passage ends with Abu Ali al-Daqqaq being asked why he didn't pray for Ibn Furak. His cryptic answer suggests a special status.
The page cuts off here; the full story is not given.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم الأستاذ أبو بكر بن فورك الأصبهاني رحمه الله أخبرنا الشيخ أبو نصر عبد الرحيم بن عبد الكريم إجازة قال أنا أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين الحافظ قال أخبرنا أبو عبد الله محمد بن عبد الله الحافظ قال : محمد بن الحسن بن فورك الأديب المتكلم الأصولي الواعظ النحوى أبو بكر الأصبهاني أقام أولاً بالعراق إلى أن درس بها على مذهب الأشعرى ثم لما ورد الرى سعت به المبتدعة فعقد أبو محمد عبد محمد الثقفى مجلساً في مسجد رجا وجمع أهل السنة وتقدمنا إلى ناصر الدولة أبي الحسن محمد بن إبراهيم والتمسنا منه المراسلة في توجيهه إلى نیسابور ففعل، وورد نيسابور فبني له الدار والمدرسة من خانكاه أبى الحسن البوشنجى وأحـيـا الله تعالى به في بلدنا أنواعا من العلوم لما أستوطنها وظهرت بركته على جماعة من المتفقهة وتخرجوا به سمع عبد الأمير الله بن جعفر الأصبهاني وكثر سماعه بالبصرة وبغداد وحدث بنيسابور . أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الحسن عبد الغافر بن إسماعيل في كتابه إلى من نیسابور قال سمعت الشيخ أبا صالح أحمد بن عبد الملك المؤذن الحافظ يقول كان الأستاذ أوحد وقته أبو علي الحسن بن على الدقاق يعقد المجلس ويدعو للحاضرين والغائبين من أعيان البلد وأئمتهم فقيل له قد نسيت ابن فورك ولم تدع له فقال أبو على كيف ادعو له وكنت أقسم على الله البارحة
And among them is al-Ustadh Abu Bakr ibn Furak al-Isbahani, may Allah have mercy on him. Shaykh Abu Nasr Abd al-Rahim ibn Abd al-Karim informed us by permission, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Hafiz narrated to us, saying: Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Abd Allah al-Hafiz informed us, saying: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Furak, the literary scholar, theologian, legal theorist, preacher, grammarian, Abu Bakr al-Isbahani. He resided first in Iraq and studied there according to the Ash'ari school. Then when he came to Rayy, the innovators (mubtadi'a) slandered him. So Abu Muhammad Abd Muhammad al-Thaqafi held a gathering in the mosque of Raja and gathered the Ahl al-Sunna. We appealed to Nasir al-Dawla Abu al-Hasan Muhammad ibn Ibrahim and requested his correspondence to send him to Nishapur, so he did. He came to Nishapur, and a house and a school were built for him from the khanaqah of Abu al-Hasan al-Bushanji. Through him, Allah revived many types of knowledge in our land when he settled there, and his blessing appeared on a group of students of fiqh who graduated under him. He heard from Abd al-Amir Allah ibn Ja'far al-Isbahani, and his listening (hadith acquisition) was extensive in Basra and Baghdad, and he narrated in Nishapur. Shaykh Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Ghafir ibn Isma'il informed us in his book 'to from Nishapur'? He said: I heard Shaykh Abu Salih Ahmad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Mu'adhdhin al-Hafiz say: Al-Ustadh, the unique of his time, Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Ali al-Daqqaq used to hold sessions and pray for both those present and absent among the notables and imams of the city. It was said to him: You forgot Ibn Furak and did not pray for him. So Abu Ali said: How can I pray for him when I was swearing by Allah last night...
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a biography of Abu Bakr ibn Furak, a major Ash'ari theologian and scholar. It provides his full name and describes him as an adib, mutakallim, usuli, wa'iz, and nahwi. It recounts his academic journey: he first studied in Iraq according to the Ash'ari madhhab, then went to Rayy where he faced opposition from the mubtadi'a (innovators). The Ahl al-Sunna rallied and arranged for him to be invited to Nishapur, where a house and school were built. He revived many sciences there and trained many students. The passage ends with an anecdote from Abu Ali al-Daqqaq, who was asked why he didn't pray for Ibn Furak; his cryptic response indicates a special spiritual state. The biography is incomplete as the page ends here.

Key Terms

الأشعرى
المبتدعة
المدرسة

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr ibn Furak was a key Ash'ari theologian who revived Sunni knowledge in Nishapur despite opposition from innovators.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Ibn Furak was slandered by the mubtadi'a and then supported by the Ahl al-Sunna. When you face criticism for your faith, do you trust that Allah can turn it into a means of your growth, or do you become resentful? What is one step you can take this week to respond with patience and reliance on Him?
?
Ibn Furak mastered multiple sciences: theology, grammar, preaching, legal theory. Which of these areas is weakest in your own religious knowledge, and what is one concrete action you will take this week to strengthen it?
?
The scholar Abu Ali al-Daqqaq prayed for everyone except Ibn Furak because of a divine vision that showed Ibn Furak's high rank. Is there anyone you overlook in your duas—perhaps out of jealousy, pride, or neglect—whom you need to include? Will you commit to making dua for that person today?

Biography of al-Isma'ili: His Teaching and Death
Biography of al-Isma'ili, his teaching and death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and scholarly career of al-Isma'ili, including his lineage, his role in hadith transmission, and the circumstances of his death.

Core Idea
Al-Isma'ili continued his father's legacy as a respected hadith scholar and teacher.

Imam Ibn Asakir presents a brief biographical sketch of the scholar al-Isma'ili. This passage highlights his lineage, his early assumption of leadership, his widespread acceptance, and his dedication to teaching hadith. It also records the date and circumstances of his death, providing a complete portrait of a notable figure in Islamic scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing it. Then read the translation. Let the flow of the biography come through.
2
Identify key details about his life
Look for the following: his lineage, his assumption of leadership, his prestige, his teachers, his teaching schedule, and the date and manner of his death.
These details form the core of the biographical account.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why such biographical details are recorded. They show the continuity of scholarship from father to son and the importance of hadith dictation sessions.
This passage is not doctrinal but provides context for understanding the chain of transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ابن أحمد بن إبراهيم بن إسماعيل بن العباس الإسماعيلي ترأس في حياة والده أبي بكر الإسماعيلي وبعد وفاته إلى أن توفي وكان له جاه عظيم وقبول عند الخاص والعام في كثير من البلدان وتحل بكتابه العقد وكان كتب الحديث الكثير عن أبي يعقوب البحيرى وأبى العباس الأصم وبالعراق وبمكة وبالرى وهمذان وكان يعرف الحديث ويدرى وأول ما جلس للاملاء في حياة والده أبي بكر الإسماعيلي في سنة ست وستين في مسجد الصفارين إلى أن توفى والده ثم انتقل إلى المسجد الذي كان والده يملى فيه ويملى كل يوم سبت إلى أن توفى وكانت وفاته في يوم الأحد ودفن يوم الاثنين لثلاث بقين من شهر ربيع الآخر سنة خمس وأربعمائة وصلى عليه أبو معمر الإسماعيلي
Ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Ismail ibn al-Abbas al-Isma'ili assumed leadership during the lifetime of his father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili and after his death until he died. He had great prestige and acceptance among the elite and the common people in many lands. He authored the book 'al-'Iqd' and wrote much hadith from Abu Ya'qub al-Buhayri, Abu al-Abbas al-Asamm, in Iraq, Mecca, Rayy, and Hamadhan. He knew hadith and was knowledgeable. His first sitting for dictation was during the lifetime of his father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili in the year 366 in the Mosque of the Coppersmiths until his father died. Then he moved to the mosque where his father used to dictate and dictated every Saturday until he died. His death was on Sunday, and he was buried on Monday with three nights remaining in Rabi' al-Akhir in the year 405. Abu Mu'mar al-Isma'ili prayed over him.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage provides a biography of the scholar al-Isma'ili. It begins by identifying his lineage and then mentions that he assumed scholarly leadership during his father's lifetime and after his death. He had great prestige and acceptance among both the elite and common people in many lands. He authored a book called 'al-'Iqd' and collected many hadith from various teachers across different regions including Iraq, Mecca, Rayy, and Hamadhan. He was knowledgeable in hadith. The passage then details his teaching career: he first began dictating hadith in the Mosque of the Coppersmiths in the year 366 while his father was still alive. After his father's death, he moved to the mosque where his father used to dictate and continued dictating every Saturday until his own death. His death occurred on a Sunday, and he was buried on Monday with three days remaining in Rabi' al-Akhir of the year 405. Abu Mu'mar al-Isma'ili led his funeral prayer.

Key Terms

أبو بكر الإسماعيلي
العقد
الإملاء

Key Takeaway
Al-Isma'ili was a respected hadith scholar who began teaching in 366 AH and continued until his death in 405 AH.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Isma'ili taught every Saturday without fail until his death. What regular commitment to Allah's religion do you maintain with such consistency? How can you strengthen a weak habit today?
?
He enjoyed prestige among both elites and commoners. Are you more concerned with the approval of certain people than with the pleasure of Allah? What is one step you can take this week to purify your intention?
?
He began teaching while his father was still alive, not waiting for the 'right time'. Is there a good deed you are postponing? What would it cost you to start today, and what would it cost you not to?

Ibn Furak's Migration to Nishapur and Scholarly Impact
Ibn Furak's migration to Nishapur and the construction of his house and school.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Furak was supported by the Sunni community after facing opposition from innovators and how he revived sciences in Nishapur.

Core Idea
Ibn Furak's arrival revived Nishapur's sciences.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari narrates the migration of the Ash'ari scholar Ibn Furak from Rayy to Nishapur. It shows how the people of Sunnah rallied to support him against the innovators, and how his presence brought life to the sciences. Read on to see the details of this pivotal event in his life.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the chain of narration and the details of his migration.
Pay attention to the titles given to Ibn Furak.
2
Identify the opposition and response
The passage mentions 'al-mubtadi'a' (innovators) who slandered him. How did the Sunni community respond? What role did Nasir al-Dawla play?
3
Reflect on the construction of the school
A house and school were built for him. What does this indicate about the value placed on scholars?
Consider the phrase 'Ahya Allahu bihi' (God revived through him).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم الأستاذ أبو بكر بن فورك الأصبهاني رحمه الله أخبرنا الشيخ أبو نصر عبد الرحيم بن عبد الكريم إجازة قال أنا أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين الحافظ قال أخبرنا أبو عبد الله محمد بن عبد الله الحافظ قال : محمد بن الحسن بن فورك الأديب المتكلم الأصولي الواعظ النحوى أبو بكر الأصبهاني أقام أولاً بالعراق إلى أن درس بها على مذهب الأشعرى ثم لما ورد الرى سعت به المبتدعة فعقد أبو محمد عبد محمد الثقفى مجلساً في مسجد رجا وجمع أهل السنة وتقدمنا إلى ناصر الدولة أبي الحسن محمد بن إبراهيم والتمسنا منه المراسلة في توجيهه إلى نیسابور ففعل، وورد نيسابور فبني له الدار والمدرسة من خانكاه أبى الحسن البوشنجى وأحيا الله تعالى به في بلدنا أنواعا من العلوم لما أستوطنها وظهرت بركته على جماعة من المتفقهة وتخرجوا به سمع عبد الله بن جعفر الأصبهاني وكثر سماعه بالبصرة وبغداد وحدث بنيسابور . أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الحسن عبد الغافر بن إسماعيل في كتابه إلى من نیسابور قال سمعت الشيخ أبا صالح أحمد بن عبد الملك المؤذن الحافظ يقول كان الأستاذ أوحد وقته أبو علي الحسن بن على الدقاق يعقد المجلس ويدعو للحاضرين والغائبين من أعيان البلد وأئمتهم فقيل له قد نسيت ابن فورك ولم تدع له فقال أبو على كيف ادعو له وكنت أقسم على الله البارحة بأيمانه أن يشفى علتى وكان به وجع البطن تلك الليلة . قال عبد الغفار بن إسماعيل : محمد بن الحسن بن فورك أبو بكر بلغ تصانيفه في أصول الدين وأصول الفقه ومعاني القرآن قريبا من المائة ، توفى سنة ست وأربعمائة وكان قد دعى إلى غزنة وجرت له بها مناظرات وكان شديد الرد على أصحاب أبي عبد الله ولما عاد من غزنة سم في الطريق ومضى إلى رحمة الله ونقل إلى نيسابور ودفن بالحيرة ومشهده اليوم ظاهر يستشفى به ويجاب الدعاء عنده . أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم زاهر بن طاهر قال أنا أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين البيهقى الحافظ قال سمعت الأستاذ أبو القسم القشيري يقول سمعت الإمام أبا بكر بن فورك يقول حملت مقيداً إلى شيراز لفتنة في الدين فوافينا باب البلد مصبحا وكنت مهموم القلب فلما أسفر النهار وقع بصری علی محراب في مسجد على باب البلد مكتوب عليه ( أليس الله بكاف عبده ( وحصل لى تعريف من باطنى أنى أكفى عن قريب وكان كذلك وصرفونى بالعز
Among them is the master Abu Bakr ibn Furak al-Isbahani, may God have mercy on him. The sheikh Abu Nasr Abd al-Rahim ibn Abd al-Karim informed us by permission, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Hafiz told us, saying: Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Abd Allah al-Hafiz told us: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Furak, the literary scholar, theologian, legal methodologist, preacher, grammarian, Abu Bakr al-Isbahani. He first stayed in Iraq until he studied there according to the Ash'ari school. Then when he came to Rayy, the innovators maligned him, so Abu Muhammad Abd Muhammad al-Thaqafi held a gathering in the mosque of Raja and gathered the people of Sunnah. We appealed to Nasir al-Dawla Abu al-Hasan Muhammad ibn Ibrahim and asked him to send a letter to direct him to Nishapur, and he did. So he came to Nishapur, and a house and school were built for him from the hospice of Abu al-Hasan al-Bushanji. God revived through him in our city many types of sciences when he settled there, and his blessing appeared upon a group of jurisprudence students, and they graduated under him. He heard from Abd Allah ibn Ja'far al-Isbahani and heard much in Basra and Baghdad, and narrated hadith in Nishapur. The sheikh Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Ghafir ibn Ismail informed us in his letter to us from Nishapur, saying: I heard the sheikh Abu Salih Ahmad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Mu'adhdhin al-Hafiz say: The master, unique in his time, Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Ali al-Daqqaq used to hold gatherings and pray for the present and absent among the notable people of the city and their imams. It was said to him: You forgot Ibn Furak and did not pray for him. Abu Ali said: How can I pray for him? For I swore by God last night by His oaths that He should cure my illness, and he had stomach pain that night. Abd al-Ghaffar ibn Ismail said: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Furak Abu Bakr - his works in usul al-din, usul al-fiqh, and meanings of the Quran reached nearly one hundred. He died in the year 406. He was invited to Ghazna and debates occurred there, and he was severe in refuting the followers of Abu Abd Allah. When he returned from Ghazna, he was poisoned on the road and went to the mercy of God. He was transported to Nishapur and buried in al-Hira. His tomb today is well-known; people seek healing there and supplications are answered at it. The sheikh Abu al-Qasim Zahir ibn Tahir informed us, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Bayhaqi al-Hafiz told us, saying: I heard the master Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri say: I heard Imam Abu Bakr ibn Furak say: I was taken in chains to Shiraz due to a conflict in religion. We arrived at the gate of the city at dawn, and I was anxious. When the day brightened, my eyes fell upon a mihrab in a mosque at the city gate on which was written: 'Is not God sufficient for His servant?' [Quran 39:36] I received an inner intimation that I would be taken care of soon, and it was so, and they released me with honor.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed biography of Ibn Furak, a prominent Ash'ari theologian and scholar. It begins by listing his full name and titles: al-adib (literary scholar), al-mutakallim (theologian), al-usuli (legal methodologist), al-wa'iz (preacher), al-nahwi (grammarian). He first resided in Iraq and studied according to the Ash'ari school. When he went to Rayy, the innovators (mubtadi'a) slandered him, prompting the Sunnis to rally in his support. Through the efforts of Nasir al-Dawla, he was invited to Nishapur, where a house and school were built for him. His presence revived sciences there, and many students benefited from him. He studied under various teachers and narrated hadith. The passage then relates a story from Abd al-Ghafir al-Isma'ili about a miraculous healing: the famous ascetic Abu Ali al-Daqqaq, when asked why he did not pray for Ibn Furak, explained that he had sworn an oath to God for his own healing, implying that Ibn Furak's merit was such that his mere presence was a blessing. The biography continues with his scholarly output: nearly one hundred works in usul al-din, usul al-fiqh, and tafsir. He died in 406 AH. He was invited to Ghazna where he engaged in debates and strongly refuted the followers of Abu Abd Allah (likely the Mu'tazila or other sect). On his return, he was poisoned and died. His tomb in al-Hira became a place where people seek blessings. Finally, a personal anecdote from Ibn Furak himself: he was taken to Shiraz in chains due to a religious conflict, but upon seeing the verse 'Is not God sufficient for His servant?' inscribed on a mihrab, he received divine reassurance and was eventually released with honor.

Key Terms
ابن فورك
الأشعري
المبتدعة
نيسابور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why was Ibn Furak invited to Nishapur?
A) He was slandered by innovators in Rayy
B) He was born there
C) He requested a transfer
D) The caliph ordered it

Key Takeaway
Ibn Furak's migration to Nishapur was facilitated by the Sunni community to protect him from innovator opposition and resulted in the revival of sciences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Ibn Furak was maligned by innovators but did not retreat; instead, the community rallied to support him. When you face criticism for standing by the truth, do you withdraw or seek the support of like-minded believers? What would it take for you to trust the community's help as he did?
?
A hospice funded Ibn Furak's house and school, reviving sciences. What is one tangible sacrifice—time, money, or effort—you can make this week to support Islamic knowledge in your local community? Write down one specific action you will take.

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
4 min
The Status of Ibn Furak: A Story of Baraka
Ibn Furak's high status shown through Abu Ali al-Daqqaq's statement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the high spiritual station of Ibn Furak as evidenced by the story of Abu Ali al-Daqqaq.

Core Idea
Ibn Furak's presence itself was a blessing.

This passage recounts an anecdote from the biography of Ibn Furak that illustrates his lofty rank. The renowned ascetic Abu Ali al-Daqqaq, when questioned about not including Ibn Furak in his prayers, explained that he had sworn an oath for his own healing, implying that Ibn Furak's mere presence was a source of blessing. Read the story to grasp the subtle point.

Guided Path
1
Read the anecdote carefully
Pay attention to the dialogue between Abu Ali al-Daqqaq and those who questioned him.
2
Understand the implication
Why did Abu Ali say he could not pray for Ibn Furak? What does this reveal about Ibn Furak?
Consider the concept of baraka.
3
Reflect on baraka
Consider how this story shows the concept of baraka (blessing) associated with righteous scholars.

Why did Abu Ali al-Daqqaq not pray for Ibn Furak?
A) He forgot

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Who in your life do you consider so spiritually elevated that you assume they don't need your prayers? Is that a justification for neglect, or does it reveal a deeper connection?
?
When you pray for others, do you include those you secretly envy or resent? How does al-Daqqaq's spontaneous vow for Ibn Furak challenge you to examine your own heart?
?
If someone's mere presence is a blessing, are you actively seeking such company? What is one step you can take this week to draw closer to those who carry baraka?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir

Ibn Furak's Scholarly Legacy and Death
Ibn Furak's works, death, and tomb.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the extent of Ibn Furak's scholarly output and the circumstances of his death.

Core Idea
Ibn Furak authored nearly 100 works and died after being poisoned.

This passage details the scholarly productivity of Ibn Furak and the tragic end of his life. It mentions that his works in theology, jurisprudence, and Quranic exegesis neared one hundred. It also recounts his invitation to Ghazna, his debates there, his strong refutation of certain groups, his poisoning on the return journey, and the veneration of his tomb. Read on to learn about his legacy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Note the numbers and events mentioned.
2
Identify his fields of authorship
The passage mentions three fields: usul al-din, usul al-fiqh, and ma'ani al-Quran. What does each cover?
3
Understand his death
How did he die? What does the passage say about his tomb?
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why his tomb became a place of visitation and prayer.

Then when he came to Rayy, the innovators maligned him, so Abu Muhammad Abd Muhammad al-Thaqafi held a gathering in the mosque of Raja and gathered the people of Sunnah. We appealed to Nasir al-Dawla Abu al-Hasan Muhammad ibn Ibrahim and asked him to send a letter to direct him to Nishapur, and he did. So he came to Nishapur, and a house and school were built for him from the hospice of Abu al-Hasan al-Bushanji. God revived through him in our city many types of sciences when he settled there, and his blessing appeared upon a group of jurisprudence students, and they graduated under him. He heard from Abd Allah ibn Ja'far al-Isbahani and heard much in Basra and Baghdad, and narrated hadith in Nishapur. The sheikh Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Ghafir ibn Ismail informed us in his letter to us from Nishapur, saying: I heard the sheikh Abu Salih Ahmad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Mu'adhdhin al-Hafiz say: The master, unique in his time, Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Ali al-Daqqaq used to hold gatherings and pray for the present and absent among the notable people of the city and their imams. It was said to him: You forgot Ibn Furak and did not pray for him. Abu Ali said: How can I pray for him? For I swore by God last night by His oaths that He should cure my illness, and he had stomach pain that night. Abd al-Ghaffar ibn Ismail said: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Furak Abu Bakr - his works in usul al-din, usul al-fiqh, and meanings of the Quran reached nearly one hundred. He died in the year 406. He was invited to Ghazna and debates occurred there, and he was severe in refuting the followers of Abu Abd Allah. When he returned from Ghazna, he was poisoned on the road and went to the mercy of God. He was transported to Nishapur and buried in al-Hira. His tomb today is well-known; people seek healing there and supplications are answered at it. The sheikh Abu al-Qasim Zahir ibn Tahir informed us, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Bayhaqi al-Hafiz told us, saying: I heard the master Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri say: I heard Imam Abu Bakr ibn Furak say: I was taken in chains to Shiraz due to a conflict in religion. We arrived at the gate of the city at dawn, and I was anxious. When the day brightened, my eyes fell upon a mihrab in a mosque at the city gate on which was written: 'Is not God sufficient for His servant?' [Quran 39:36] I received an inner intimation that I would be taken care of soon, and it was so, and they released me with honor.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed biography of Ibn Furak, a prominent Ash'ari theologian and scholar. It begins by listing his full name and titles: al-adib (literary scholar), al-mutakallim (theologian), al-usuli (legal methodologist), al-wa'iz (preacher), al-nahwi (grammarian). He first resided in Iraq and studied according to the Ash'ari school. When he went to Rayy, the innovators (mubtadi'a) slandered him, prompting the Sunnis to rally in his support. Through the efforts of Nasir al-Dawla, he was invited to Nishapur, where a house and school were built for him. His presence revived sciences there, and many students benefited from him. He studied under various teachers and narrated hadith. The passage then relates a story from Abd al-Ghafir al-Isma'ili about a miraculous healing: the famous ascetic Abu Ali al-Daqqaq, when asked why he did not pray for Ibn Furak, explained that he had sworn an oath to God for his own healing, implying that Ibn Furak's merit was such that his mere presence was a blessing. The biography continues with his scholarly output: nearly one hundred works in usul al-din, usul al-fiqh, and tafsir. He died in 406 AH. He was invited to Ghazna where he engaged in debates and strongly refuted the followers of Abu Abd Allah (likely the Mu'tazila or other sect). On his return, he was poisoned and died. His tomb in al-Hira became a place where people seek blessings. Finally, a personal anecdote from Ibn Furak himself: he was taken to Shiraz in chains due to a religious conflict, but upon seeing the verse 'Is not God sufficient for His servant?' inscribed on a mihrab, he received divine reassurance and was eventually released with honor.

معاني القرآن

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
He was poisoned for his firm stance in refuting falsehood. Is there a truth you are avoiding because it might cost you comfort or reputation?
?
His tomb is a place where people seek healing and have their prayers answered. When was the last time you sincerely turned to Allah through the legacy of the righteous, or do you rely only on your own means?

Ibn Furak's Trial in Shiraz and Divine Assistance
Ibn Furak's imprisonment in Shiraz and divine reassurance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Furak's faith was tested during his imprisonment in Shiraz and how divine signs provided him comfort.

Core Idea
The Quranic verse 'Is not God sufficient?' gave Ibn Furak peace.

This final anecdote from the biography of Ibn Furak recounts a personal trial he faced. He was taken in chains to Shiraz due to a religious conflict. In his anxiety, he saw a mihrab inscribed with the Quranic verse 'Is not God sufficient for His servant?' which brought him inner reassurance. Eventually, he was released with honor. Read this story to see how Ibn Furak's reliance on God was rewarded.

Guided Path
1
Read the anecdote

2

The verse on the mihrab is key. Reflect on its meaning in this context.
The verse is Quran 39:36.
3
Understand the outcome
How did God fulfill the promise of that verse?

The Life of Abu Sa'd al-Kharkushi
Partial biography of Abu Sa'd al-Kharkushi, a preacher and ascetic

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the early life and scholarly journey of Abu Sa'd al-Kharkushi, a Shafi'i jurist and ascetic.

Core Idea
Abu Sa'd al-Kharkushi's life exemplifies the integration of jurisprudence, asceticism, and travel for knowledge.

This lesson presents a partial biography of Abu Sa'd al-Kharkushi, a preacher and ascetic from Nishapur. The passage traces his early study of jurisprudence, his adoption of asceticism, his teachers, and his travels to Iraq and the Hijaz. Though incomplete, it offers a glimpse into the life of a devoted scholar.

ومنهم أبو سعد بن أبي عثمان النيسابورى الخر كوشي الزاهد رحمه الله قرأت على الشيخ أبي القسم زاهر بن طاهر الشحامي عن أبي بكر أحمد بن الحسين البيهقى قال أنا أبو عبد الله محمد بن عبد الله الحافظ قال : عبد الملك بن محمد بن إبراهيم أبو سعد بن أبي عثمان الواعظ الزاهد تفقه في حداثة السن وتزهد وجالس الزهاد والمجردين إلى أن جعله الله خلفاً لجماعة من تقدمه من العباد المجتهدين والزهاد القانعين ، سمع بنيسابور أبا محمد يحيى بن منصور القاضى وأبا عمرو بن نجيدو أبا على الرفاء الهروى وأبا أحمد محمد بن محمد بن الحسن النسائى وأقرانهم ، وتفقه للشافعي على أبي الحسن الماسرجسى وسمع بالعراق بعد التسعين والثلاثمائة ثم خرج إلى الحجاز وجاوز حرم الله وأمنه مكة وصحب بها العباد الصالحين وسمع الحديث من أهلها والواردين وانصرف إلى وطنه بنيسابور وقد أنجز الله له موعوده على لسان نبيه المصطفى صلى الله عليه وسلم ( في حديث
Among them is Abu Sa'd ibn Abi Uthman al-Naysaburi al-Kharkushi the ascetic, may God have mercy on him. I read to the sheikh Abu al-Qasim Zahir ibn Tahir al-Shihami from Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Bayhaqi, who said: Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Abd Allah al-Hafiz told us: Abd al-Malik ibn Muhammad ibn Ibrahim Abu Sa'd ibn Abi Uthman, the preacher, the ascetic. He studied jurisprudence in his youth and became ascetic, and sat with ascetics and recluses until God made him a successor to a group of earlier devoted worshippers and contented ascetics. He heard in Nishapur from Abu Muhammad Yahya ibn Mansur al-Qadi, Abu Amr ibn Najidu, Abu Ali al-Rifa' al-Harawi, Abu Ahmad Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Nasa'i, and their peers. Then he went to the Hijaz and entered the sacred sanctuary of God and its secure place, Mecca, and accompanied there the righteous worshippers, and heard hadith from its people and visitors. He returned to his homeland Nishapur, and God fulfilled for him His promise on the tongue of His chosen Prophet, peace be upon him, in a hadith...
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage provides a partial biography of Abu Sa'd al-Kharkushi, an ascetic preacher. It begins with his name and title: al-wa'iz al-zahid (preacher and ascetic). He studied jurisprudence (tafaqqaha) in his youth and adopted asceticism, associating with ascetics and recluses. God made him a successor to earlier devoted worshippers and contented ascetics. He studied hadith in Nishapur from several teachers, including Abu Muhammad Yahya ibn Mansur al-Qadi and others. He studied Shafi'i jurisprudence under Abu al-Hasan al-Masarjisi. He heard hadith in Iraq after the year 390. Then he traveled to the Hijaz and entered Mecca, where he accompanied righteous worshippers and heard hadith from its inhabitants and visitors. He then returned to Nishapur. The passage ends abruptly mid-sentence, mentioning that God fulfilled His promise on the tongue of the Prophet in a hadith, which is incomplete due to the page break.

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir

Ibn Furak: Scholar and the Miracle of Divine Sufficiency
Biography of Ibn Furak with anecdote of his release from prison.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly legacy of Ibn Furak and the miraculous event that demonstrated Allah's sufficiency for His servant.

Core Idea
Allah's promise of sufficiency can manifest even in chains.

Ibn Furak was a towering Ash'ari scholar whose works spanned theology, jurisprudence, and Quranic exegesis. This passage from Ibn 'Asakir's Tabyin presents both his scholarly contributions and a personal anecdote of his miraculous release from imprisonment. The story illustrates how divine assurance can turn distress into honor.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical overview
Read the first part of the passage, which lists Ibn Furak's scholarly works, his invitation to Ghazna, his death, and his burial place. Notice the high output of nearly a hundred works and the mention of his tomb as a site of healing.
This section establishes Ibn Furak's prominent status in Islamic scholarship.
2
Analyze the miraculous release narrative
Read the anecdote transmitted through al-Qushayri. Identify the Quranic verse Ibn Furak saw and the inner assurance he received. Observe the outcome: he was released with honor.
The verse 'Is not God sufficient for His servant?' is key to the story.
3
Reflect on the core message
Consider how the anecdote demonstrates the principle of tawakkul (trust in God). Reflect on how divine sufficiency can manifest in difficult circumstances.
This connects the historical event to a universal spiritual lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال عبد الغفار بن إسماعيل : محمد بن الحسن بن فورك أبو بكر بلغ تصانيفه في أصول الدين وأصول الفقه ومعاني القرآن قريبا من المائة ، توفى سنة ست وأربعمائة وكان قد دعى إلى غزنة وجرت له بها مناظرات وكان شديد الرد على أصحاب أبي عبد الله ولما عاد من غزنة سم في الطريق ومضى إلى رحمة الله ونقل إلى نيسابور ودفن بالحيرة ومشهده اليوم ظاهر يستشفى به ويجاب الدعاء عنده .
أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم زاهر بن طاهر قال أنا أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين البيهقى الحافظ قال سمعت الأستاذ أبا القسم القشيري يقول سمعت الإمام أبا بكر بن فورك يقول حملت مقيداً إلى شيراز لفتنة في الدين فوافينا باب البلد مصبحا وكنت مهموم القلب فلما أسفر النهار وقع بصری علی محراب في مسجد على باب البلد مكتوب عليه ( أليس الله بكاف عبده ( وحصل لى تعريف من باطنى أنى أكفى عن قريب وكان كذلك وصرفونى بالعز .
Abd al-Ghaffar ibn Isma'il said: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Furak, Abu Bakr, his works in usul al-din (foundations of religion), usul al-fiqh (foundations of jurisprudence), and ma'ani al-Qur'an (meanings of the Qur'an) reached nearly a hundred. He died in the year 406 AH. He had been invited to Ghazna and held debates there, and he was severe in refuting the followers of Abu Abd Allah. When he returned from Ghazna, he was poisoned on the road and passed to the mercy of God. He was transferred to Nishapur and buried in al-Hira. His tomb today is visible, where people seek healing and prayers are answered. 
The shaykh Abu al-Qasim Zahir ibn Tahir informed us, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Bayhaqi the hafiz told us, saying: I heard the master Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri say: I heard Imam Abu Bakr ibn Furak say: I was taken in chains to Shiraz due to a religious trial. We arrived at the gate of the city in the morning, and my heart was distressed. When the day brightened, my eyes fell upon a mihrab in a mosque at the city gate, on which was written: "Is not God sufficient for His servant?" (Qur'an 39:36). An inner realization came to me that I would be released soon, and so it happened; they released me with honor.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage is a biography of the renowned Ash'ari theologian Ibn Furak. It first provides his full name and his scholarly output in theology, jurisprudence, and Quranic exegesis. It notes his death in 406 AH. The text highlights his debates in Ghazna and his strong refutation of the followers of Abu Abd Allah (likely the Mu'tazila or other opponents). Upon his return from Ghazna, he was poisoned, died, and was buried in Nishapur. The passage emphasizes that his tomb is a place where people seek healing and where supplications are answered, indicating veneration. 
Then follows a first-person anecdote from Ibn Furak himself, transmitted through a chain: al-Bayhaqi from al-Qushayri. Ibn Furak recounts being arrested and taken in chains to Shiraz for a religious controversy. As he arrived at the city gate, he noticed a Quranic verse inscribed in a mosque: 'Is not God sufficient for His servant?' He felt an inner assurance that he would be freed soon, and indeed he was released with honor. This story serves to demonstrate divine intervention and the efficacy of trust in God.

Key Terms
ابن فورك
أصول الدين
أصول الفقه
معاني القرآن
غزنة
نيسابور
الحيرة
استشفاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The passage justifies tomb worship or seeking healing directly from the deceased.
Correction: The text merely reports that people visit Ibn Furak's tomb for healing and prayer; it does not prescribe such acts as religious obligations or indicate that the dead grant requests.

Checkpoint
In what year did Ibn Furak die according to this passage?
A) 406 AH
B) 400 AH
C) 410 AH
D) 416 AH

Key Takeaway
Ibn Furak's life and release demonstrate that divine sufficiency can transform moments of distress into honor.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a trial that seems overwhelming, do you genuinely believe that Allah is sufficient for you, or do you rely on your own strategies and resources? What one concrete step can you take today to deepen your trust in His promise of sufficiency?
?
Ibn Furak found solace in a familiar verse inscribed in a mosque. Is there a verse or reminder from Allah that you have repeatedly encountered but ignored? Write it down and commit to meditating on it daily this week, asking Allah to grant you inner assurance.
?
His release was with honor despite being brought in chains. Are you willing to endure temporary humiliation or difficulty for the sake of your faith, trusting that Allah can turn your distress into honor? What fear of loss or shame holds you back from full reliance on Him?

Abu Sa'd al-Kharkushi: A Model of Asceticism and Service
Biography of Abu Sa'd al-Kharkushi including his life, charities, and hadith on divine love.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and virtues of Abu Sa'd al-Kharkushi, focusing on his asceticism, charitable works, and the hadith about divine love that shaped his mission.

Core Idea
Abu Sa'd al-Kharkushi turned divine love into a life of service.

This biography introduces a towering figure of Nishapur: Abu Sa'd al-Kharkushi, a scholar and ascetic whose life mirrored the hadith that when God loves a servant, acceptance spreads throughout heaven and earth. As you read, notice how his personal transformation led to vast charitable projects and lasting scholarly works.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography fully
Read the Arabic and English passages once to get a sense of his life journey from youth to legacy.
Pay attention to the hadith of Suhayl – it’s central to understanding his motivation.
2
Map his life stages
Identify the main phases: early study and asceticism, travels to Iraq and Mecca, return to Nishapur, and his charitable and scholarly works.
3
Analyze the hadith and its impact
Study the hadith about God’s love and how al-Kharkushi interpreted it as a call to action. Notice the chain of transmission and the emphasis on acceptance on earth.
The hadith is quoted directly; reflect on why the author includes it.
4
List his charitable contributions
Identify the specific institutions he built: mosques, cisterns, bridges, a hospital, and his care for the poor and sick.
Note the detail about appointing caregivers for the sick.
5
Reflect on his legacy
Consider how the author praises him as unmatched in knowledge, asceticism, humility, and guidance. What made him unique?
The passage ends with another chain of transmission confirming his identity.

ومنهم أبو سعد بن أبي عثمان النيسابورى الخر كوشی الزاهد
رحمه الله
قرأت على الشيخ أبي القسم زاهر بن طاهر الشحامي عن أبي بكر أحمد بن الحسين البيهقى قال أنا أبو عبد الله محمد بن عبد الله الحافظ قال : عبد الملك بن محمد بن إبراهيم أبو سعد بن أبي عثمان الواعظ الزاهد تفقه في حداثة السن وتزهد وجالس الزهاد والمجردين إلى أن جعله الله خلفاً لجماعة من تقدمه من العباد المجتهدين والزهاد القانعين ، سمع بنيسابور أبا محمد يحيى بن منصور القاضى وأبا عمرو بن نجيدو أبا على الرفاء الهروى وأبا أحمد محمد بن محمد بن الحسن النسائى وأقرانهم ، وتفقه للشافعي على أبي الحسن الماسرجسى وسمع بالعراق بعد التسعين والثلاثمائة ثم خرج إلى الحجاز وجاوز حرم الله وأمنه مكة وصحب بها العباد الصالحين وسمع الحديث من أهلها والواردين وانصرف إلى وطنه بنيسابور وقد أنجز الله له موعوده على لسان نبيه المصطفى صلى الله عليه وسلم ( في حديث سهيل عن أبيه عن أبي هريرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أن الله تعالى إذا أحب عبداً نادى جبريل أن الله قد أحب فلاناً فأحبه فينادي جبريل بذلك في السماء فيحبه أهل السماء ثم يوضع له القبول في الأرض ) فلزم منزله ومجلسه وبذل النفس والمال والجاه للمستوردين من الغرباء والفقراء المنقطع بهم حتى صار الفقراء في مجالسه كما حدثونا عن إبراهيم بن الحسين ثنا عمرو بن عون قال ثنا يحيى ابن اليمان قال كان الفقراء في مجلس سفيان كأمراء ، قد وفقه الله تعالى لعمارة المساجد والحياض والقناطر والدروب وكسوة الفقراء العراة من الغرباء والبلدية حتى بنى دارا للمرضى بعد أن خربت الدور القديمة لهم بنيسابور ووكل جماعة من أصحابه المستورين بتمريضهم وحمل مياههم إلى الأطباء ، وشراء الأدوية. ولقد أخبرني الثقة أن الله تعالى ذكره قد شفى جماعة منهم فكساهم وزودهم إلى الرجوع إلى أوطانهم وقد صنف في علوم الشريعة ودلائل النبوة وفي سير العباد والزهاد كتبا نسخها جماعة من أهل الحديث وسمعوها منه وسارت تلك المصنفات في بلاد المسلمين تاريخا لنيسابور وعلمائها الماضين منهم والباقين وكثيرا أقول أن لا يباهي بأجمع منه علما وزهدا وتواضعاً وإرشاداً إلى الله تعالى ذكره وإلى شريعة نبيه المصطفى صلى الله عليه وسلم وعلى آله وإلى الزاهدين في الدنيا الفانية والتزود منها للآخرة الباقية ، زاده الله توفيقاً وأسعدنا بأيامه ووفقنا للشكر الله تعالى ذكره بمكانه أنه خير معين و موفق .
وقد روى عنه الحاكم وهو أسند منه
أخبرنا الشيخان أبو الحسن على بن أحمد الغساني بدمشق وأبو منصور عبد الرحمن بن محمد الشيباني ببغداد قالا قال لنا أبو بكر أحمد ابن علی ثابت الخطيب : عبد الملك بن أبي عثمان واسم أبي عثمان محمد ابن إبراهيم ويكنى عبد الملك أبا سعد الواعظ من أهل نيسابور قدم بغداد حاجا وحدث بها عن يحيى بن منصور القاضي وحامد بن محمد الهروي ومحمد بن الحسن بن إسماعيل السراج وأبي عمرو بن مطر وإسماعيل بن نجيد وأبى أحمد محمد بن محمد بن الحسن النيسابوريين ومحمد بن عبد
And among them is Abu Sa'd ibn Abi Uthman al-Naysaburi al-Kharkushi al-Zahid (may God have mercy on him). I read to the shaykh Abu al-Qasim Zahir ibn Tahir al-Shihami from Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Bayhaqi, who said: Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Abd Allah al-Hafiz told us, saying: Abd al-Malik ibn Muhammad ibn Ibrahim, Abu Sa'd ibn Abi Uthman, the preacher and ascetic, studied jurisprudence in his youth, became ascetic, and associated with ascetics and devotees until God made him a successor to a group of preceding devout worshippers and contented ascetics. He heard (hadith) in Nishapur from Abu Muhammad Yahya ibn Mansur al-Qadi, Abu Amr ibn Najid, Abu Ali al-Rifa' al-Harawi, Abu Ahmad Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Nasa'i, and their peers. He studied Shafi'i jurisprudence under Abu al-Hasan al-Masarjisi and heard hadith in Iraq after 390 AH. Then he traveled to the Hijaz and entered the sacred sanctuary of God and its security, Mecca. There he accompanied righteous worshippers and heard hadith from its people and visitors. He returned to his homeland, Nishapur, and God fulfilled for him His promise on the tongue of His chosen Prophet (peace be upon him) in the hadith of Suhayl from his father from Abu Hurayra from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'When God loves a servant, He calls Jibril: God loves so-and-so, so love him. Then Jibril calls out in the heavens, and the inhabitants of the heavens love him, then acceptance is placed for him on earth.' So he stuck to his home and his gathering, and he devoted his soul, wealth, and status to those who came to him from strangers and the poor who were stranded, until the poor in his gatherings were like princes, as they narrated to us from Ibrahim ibn al-Husayn: Amr ibn Awn told us: Yahya ibn al-Yaman told us: The poor in the gathering of Sufyan were like princes. God facilitated for him the building of mosques, cisterns, bridges, and roads, and clothing the naked poor from strangers and locals, until he built a house for the sick after the old houses for them in Nishapur had fallen into ruin. He appointed a group of his trustworthy companions to nurse them, carry their water to the doctors, and buy medicines. A trustworthy person told me that God cured a group of them, so he clothed them and provided them with provisions until they returned to their homelands. He authored books on the sciences of the Sharia, proofs of prophethood, and the biographies of worshippers and ascetics. A group of hadith scholars copied them and heard them from him, and those works spread throughout the lands of the Muslims, a history of Nishapur and its past and present scholars. And I say much: that no one comparable to him can be found in knowledge, asceticism, humility, and guidance to God and to the Sharia of His chosen Prophet (peace be upon him and his family) and to the ascetics in the fleeting world and taking provision from it for the eternal afterlife. May God increase him in success, make us happy through his days, and grant us gratitude to God for his station, for He is the best Helper and Grantor of success. 
And al-Hakim narrated from him, and he is more reliable than him (or: he is a higher authority). The two shaykhs, Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad al-Ghassani in Damascus and Abu Mansur Abd al-Rahman ibn Muhammad al-Shaybani in Baghdad, told us, both saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali Thabit al-Khatib told us: Abd al-Malik ibn Abi Uthman – and the name of Abi Uthman is Muhammad ibn Ibrahim – and he is called Abd al-Malik Abu Sa'd the preacher, from the people of Nishapur. He came to Baghdad as a pilgrim and narrated there from Yahya ibn Mansur al-Qadi, Hamid ibn Muhammad al-Harawi, Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Isma'il al-Sarraj, Abu Amr ibn Matar, Isma'il ibn Najid, Abu Ahmad Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Naysaburiyyun, and Muhammad ibn Abd...
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage is a detailed biography of the ascetic and scholar Abu Sa'd al-Kharkushi. It begins by introducing his full name and his ascetic character. It then describes his early study of fiqh and his association with ascetics. He studied under prominent teachers in Nishapur and Iraq, and later traveled to Mecca, where he accompanied righteous worshippers. The biography emphasizes that God fulfilled for him a promise from the hadith of Suhayl, which narrates that when God loves a servant, He commands Jibril to love him, leading to acceptance on earth. 
After returning to Nishapur, Abu Sa'd devoted himself to charity: he spent his wealth on the poor and strangers, building mosques, cisterns, bridges, and even a hospital for the sick. He personally arranged for nursing and medicines. The text notes that many were healed and sent back to their homelands. 
He also authored books on Islamic sciences, proofs of prophethood, and biographies of ascetics. His works became widely known. The author praises him as unparalleled in knowledge, asceticism, humility, and guidance. 
Finally, another chain of transmission confirms his name and his hadith narrations, listing several of his teachers. The passage ends abruptly with 'Muhammad ibn Abd' as the page ends.

سير العباد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the hadith about God's love implies predestination — that if God loves someone, they have no free will.
Correction: The hadith describes the effects of God's love, not a deterministic compulsion. It emphasizes that divine love leads to acceptance on earth, inspiring action as seen in al-Kharkushi's life.

Key Takeaway
Abu Sa'd al-Kharkushi turned the hadith of divine love into a life of asceticism and extensive charitable service, including building a hospital and authoring lasting works.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's love for you truly leads to 'acceptance on earth' as the hadith says, what concrete evidence of that love would others see in your daily actions? Name one specific service you will undertake this week as a sign of that love.
?
Al-Kharkushi used his wealth, status, and time to build a hospital and clothe the poor. What resources—time, money, skills—are you holding back from serving others, and what is the fear that prevents you from giving them?
?
The poor in his gatherings were treated like princes. Who in your life is treated as less than a prince or princess? What one change will you make today to elevate their status, even if only in your heart and actions?

The Integrated Asceticism of Abu Sa'd al-Zahid
Multiple narratives detailing the life, virtues, and works of the ascetic scholar Abu Sa'd al-Zahid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the scholar 'Abd al-Malik al-Naysaburi combined deep piety, active charity, and lawful earning, redefining asceticism as social engagement.

Core Idea
True asceticism is not isolation but service to others while earning lawful livelihood.

This lesson presents the biography of a remarkable scholar who balanced inner piety with outward service. Through multiple accounts, we see how his love for Allah translated into building hospitals, teaching, and earning his own bread by making caps. The passage challenges the notion that asceticism means withdrawing from society, offering instead a model of engaged spirituality.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening hadith on divine love
Start with the hadith about Allah loving a servant. Notice how it sets the spiritual foundation for the entire biography: the scholar's actions flow from being loved by Allah.
This hadith is from Sahih Muslim and Bukhari.
2
Examine his charitable works
Identify the various projects he undertook: building mosques, water basins, bridges, and a hospital. Note how he organized nursing and medicine procurement.
His charity extended to strangers and locals alike.
3
Review his scholarly contributions
He authored books on Shari'a, proofs of prophethood, and biographies of ascetics. These works spread widely and served as a history of Nishapur.
He also built a school and a library.
4
Understand his personal lifestyle and death
He worked as a cap-maker to earn a lawful living, avoiding dependency. The biographical notices confirm his trustworthiness and give his death year. The rain prayer anecdote shows his spiritual station.
His death is recorded as 400 AH or 406 AH depending on the source.

Suhayl from his father from Abu Hurayra from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that Allah Almighty when He loves a servant calls Gabriel: 'Allah loves so-and-so, so love him.' Gabriel then calls out in heaven, and the inhabitants of heaven love him, then acceptance is placed for him on the earth. So he kept to his home and his gathering, and devoted his soul, wealth, and status to those who came from among the strangers and the poor who were cut off, until the poor in his gatherings became like princes, as they narrated to us from Ibrahim ibn al-Husayn who said: 'Amr ibn 'Awn narrated to us: Yahya ibn al-Yaman said: The poor in Sufyan's gathering were like princes.' Allah had granted him success in building mosques, water basins, bridges, and roads, and clothing the naked poor from among the strangers and locals, until he built a house for the sick after the old houses for them in Nishapur had fallen into ruin, and he appointed a group of his trustworthy companions to nurse them, carry their water to the physicians, and purchase medicines. A trustworthy person informed me that Allah (mentioned) cured a group of them, so he clothed them and provided them with provisions until they returned to their homelands. He authored books on the sciences of the Shari'a, proofs of prophethood, and the biographies of worshippers and ascetics; a group of hadith scholars copied them and heard them from him, and those works spread throughout the lands of the Muslims, a history of Nishapur and its scholars, past and present. I say much that no one can boast of a more complete person than him in knowledge, asceticism, humility, and guidance to Allah (mentioned) and to the Shari'a of His Chosen Prophet (peace be upon him and his family) and to the ascetics in the fleeting world and provision from it for the lasting Hereafter. May Allah increase him in success, make us happy with his days, and grant us gratitude to Allah (mentioned) for his sake; He is the best Helper and Giver of success. Al-Hakim narrated from him, and he is more reliable than him. The two shaykhs Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Ahmad al-Ghassani in Damascus and Abu Mansur 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Muhammad al-Shaybani in Baghdad informed us, both saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn 'Ali Thabit al-Khatib said: 'Abd al-Malik ibn Abi 'Uthman (the name of Abu 'Uthman is Muhammad ibn Ibrahim), and 'Abd al-Malik is known as Abu Sa'd al-Wa'iz from Nishapur. He came to Baghdad for pilgrimage and narrated there from Yahya ibn Mansur al-Qadi, Hamid ibn Muhammad al-Harawi, Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Isma'il al-Sarraj, Abu 'Amr ibn Matar, Isma'il ibn Najid, Abu Ahmad Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Naysaburi, Muhammad ibn 'Abd Allah ibn Jubayr al-Nasawi, Bishr ibn Ahmad al-Isfarayini, 'Ali ibn Bandar ibn al-Hasan al-Sufi, Abu Ishaq al-Muzakki, and Abu Sahl al-Sa'luqi. He was narrated from by Abu Muhammad al-Khallal, al-Azhari, 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Azaji, and al-Tanukhi. Al-Tanukhi said: Abu Sa'd al-Zahid came to us in Baghdad for pilgrimage in the year 393 AH and went to Mecca and stayed there as a neighbor. Abu Bakr al-Khatib said: He was trustworthy, righteous, and pious. Abu Mansur added: An ascetic. I asked Abu Salih Ahmad ibn 'Abd al-Malik al-Naysaburi about the death of Abu Sa'd, and he said: In the year 406 AH. The shaykh Abu al-Hasan 'Abd al-Ghafir ibn Isma'il informed us by permission, saying: 'Abd al-Malik ibn Abi 'Uthman Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Naysaburi, Abu Sa'd al-Zahid al-Kharkushi al-Wa'iz, the perfect master, one of the unique individuals of Khurasan in knowledge, asceticism, piety, fear, and way. He studied jurisprudence under Abu al-Hasan al-Masarjisi, then abandoned status and sat with the ascetics, adhered to action, performed pilgrimage, and stayed (in Mecca), then returned to Khurasan. He used to make caps and order them sold without it being known that they were his work, and he ate from the earnings of his own hands. He built a school and a hospital in his alley, endowed endowments for them, placed a library of books in the school, and authored many books. He died in Jumada al-Ula of the year 400 AH. 'Abd al-Ghafir said: I heard Abu al-Fadl Muhammad ibn 'Abd Allah al-Siram al-Zahid say: I saw the master praying for rain and saying: 'The dust. To You we have come, and You have brought us, and there is no Lord besides You to enrich us. Your door is wide, its courtyard is generous, the poor are sheltered at Your door.' Seven. Then he would supplicate and say: 'O Allah, give us rain.' He said: He did not complete it three times until we were given rain like the mouths of seven.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a composite biographical entry for the scholar 'Abd al-Malik ibn Abi 'Uthman al-Naysaburi (Abu Sa'd al-Zahid). It begins with a hadith about divine love for a servant, which sets a spiritual tone, and then applies it to the subject: because God loved him, he was devoted to serving the poor and strangers. The narrative proceeds chronologically: his charitable works (building mosques, bridges, a hospital), his authorship of books on Shari'a, proofs of prophethood, and ascetic biographies, and his widespread reputation. Then follows a formal biographical notice from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, listing his teachers, his pilgrimage visits, and his death date. A third account from 'Abd al-Ghafir adds details about his ascetic practice: he worked as a cap-maker to earn a lawful living, built a school and hospital, endowed them, and left many authored works. The entry closes with an anecdote of his prayer for rain, with a poetic supplication, showing his spiritual station.

Key Terms
عبد الملك بن أبي عثمان
أبو سعد الزاهد
الخركوشى
نيسابور
صاحب التصانيف
القلانس
دار المرضى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Asceticism means withdrawing from society and avoiding all worldly involvement.
Correction: This biography shows a model of asceticism that includes active social service, building hospitals and schools, teaching, and earning a lawful living through manual labor.

Checkpoint
What did 'Abd al-Malik al-Naysaburi do to earn a lawful living according to the biography?
A) He worked as a farmer.
B) He made caps and sold them anonymously.
C) He relied on endowments.
D) He taught for a salary.

Key Takeaway
'Abd al-Malik al-Naysaburi embodied an asceticism that was not withdrawal but active engagement in society, building institutions, teaching, and earning his own lawful livelihood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Abu Sa'd made caps and sold them without anyone knowing. What is one good deed you have done that no one knows about—and if you have none, what is stopping you from starting today?
?
He built a hospital, a school, endowed them, and wrote books. If you were to die tonight, what tangible, lasting contribution would you leave behind for the Ummah? Be honest.
?
When he prayed for rain, it poured. Is your dua so weak because your heart is still attached to the world? What one attachment must you break so that your words carry weight with Allah?

Beginning of al-Bistami's Biography
Ibn 'Asakir begins the biographical entry for al-Bistami with name, titles, and isnad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn 'Asakir introduces the scholar Muhammad al-Bistami, identifying his titles and the chain of transmission used to authenticate his biography.

Core Idea
Ibn 'Asakir establishes al-Bistami's scholarly credentials through his lineage and isnad.

This passage opens the biography of the jurist-theologian Muhammad al-Bistami. Ibn 'Asakir provides his full name and honorary titles, then traces the chain of transmission through which he received his knowledge. The entry sets the stage for al-Bistami's scholarly credentials and connections.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.

Identify the titles given to al-Bistami

The word 'البارغ' is unclear; possibly a place name or descriptor.
3
Trace the chain of transmission
Identify the narrators: al-Bistami wrote to al-Qushayri, who heard from al-Bayhaqi, who heard from al-Hakim. This isnad authenticates the information about al-Bistami.
This chain shows the care in preserving scholarly heritage.

Commentary
This passage begins a new biographical entry in the chain. The phrase 'among them' links it to the previous list of scholars. The entry gives the name and titles of Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Bistami, noting his roles as judge (قاضي), jurist (فقيه), theologian (متكلم), and preacher (واعظ). It provides the chain of transmission for the information: via a letter to al-Qushayri from al-Bayhaqi, who heard from al-Hakim al-Naysaburi. The entry is cut off at the mention of his teachers in Isfahan. The fragment thus serves as an introduction to the scholar's identity and his educational credentials.

Biography of Abu Sa'd al-Zahid al-Kharkushi
Ibn Asakir compiles two reports on Abu Sa'd al-Zahid's life and miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and spiritual station of Abu Sa'd al-Zahid al-Kharkushi, a renowned ascetic and scholar of Khurasan, as recorded by Ibn Asakir.

Core Idea
Abu Sa'd al-Zahid embodied knowledge, asceticism, and answered prayers.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari presents two reports on the life of Abu Sa'd al-Zahid al-Kharkushi. The first provides key dates of his pilgrimage and death; the second details his piety, self-sufficiency, charitable works, and a miraculous rain prayer. Together, they paint a portrait of a scholar who fully practiced what he preached.

Guided Path
1
Read the two reports
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the different chains of transmission (al-Tanukhi and Abd al-Ghafir) and how each report adds unique information.
The passage is a compilation of two separate accounts.
2
Identify key biographical details
List the important facts: his pilgrimage in 393 AH, his death around 406 AH, his teacher Abu al-Hasan al-Masarjisi, his trade as a cap-maker, and his founding of a school and hospital.
Pay attention to the clarity of the death year between the two reports.
3
Reflect on the rain prayer anecdote
Read the story of his prayer for rain. Consider what it reveals about his spiritual rank and the acceptance of his supplication.
This anecdote demonstrates his closeness to Allah.
4
Resolve the death year ambiguity
The second report says 'sana wa arba'ami'a' (year 400-something). Compare with the first report's clear '406 AH' to understand the intended meaning.
The phrase likely means 'the year 400-something', and the first report specifies 406.

الله بن بن جبير النسوى وبشر بن أحمد الاسفراينى وعلى بن بندار ابن الحسن الصوفي وأبى إسحق المزكى وأبى سهل الصعلوكي حدثنا عنه أبو محمد الخلال والأزهرى وعبد العزيز الأزجى والتنوخي وقال لى التنوخي قدم علينا أبو سعد الزاهد بغداد حاجا في سنة ثلاث وتسعين وثلاثماية وخرج إلى مكة فأقام بها مجاوراً قال أبو بكر الخطيب وكان ثقة صالحاً ورعاً زاد أبو منصور زاهدا ، سألت أبا صالح أحمد بن عبد الملك النيسابورى عن وفاة أبي سعد فقال فى سنة ست وأربعمائة . • أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الحسن عبد الغافر بن إسماعيل إجازة قال : عبد الملك بن أبي عثمان محمد بن إبراهيم النيسابوري أبو سعد الزاهد الخركوشى الواعظ الأستاذ الكامل أحد أفراد خراسان علماً وزهداً وورعاً وخشية وطريقة ، تفقه على أبى الحسن الماسرجسى ثم ترك الجاه وجالس الزهاد ولزم العمل وحج وجاور ثم رجع إلى خراسان وكان يعمل القلانس ويأمر ببيعها بحيث لا يدرى أنها من صنعته ويأكل من كسب يده وبنى في سكته المدرسة ودار المرضى ووقف أوقافاً عليها ووضع في المدرسة خزانة للكتب وصنف أعداداً من الكتب وتوفى فى جمادى الأولى سنة وأربعمائة . وقال عبد الغافر سمعت أبا الفضل محمد بن عبد الله الصرام الزاهد يقول رأيت الأستاذ يستسقى ويقول : الترب . إليك جئنا وأنت جئت بنا ولیس رب سواك يغنينا بابك رحب فناؤه كرم تؤوى إلى بابك المساكينا ثم يدعو ويقول : اللهم اسقنا قال فما اتم ثلاثاً حتى سقينا كأفواه السبع
Allah ibn ibn Jubayr al-Nasawi and Bishr ibn Ahmad al-Isfara'ini and Ali ibn Bandar ibn al-Hasan al-Sufi and Abu Ishaq al-Muzakki and Abu Sahl al-Sa'luki — Abu Muhammad al-Khallal and al-Azhari and Abd al-Aziz al-Azji and al-Tanukhi narrated from him. And al-Tanukhi said to me: Abu Sa'd al-Zahid came to us in Baghdad as a pilgrim in the year 393 AH, and he left to Mecca and resided there as a neighbor. Abu Bakr al-Khatib said: He was trustworthy, righteous, devout — Abu Mansur added: ascetic. I asked Abu Salih Ahmad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Naysaburi about the death of Abu Sa'd, and he said: In the year 406 AH. • The Shaykh Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Ghafir ibn Isma'il informed us by permission, saying: Abd al-Malik ibn Abi Uthman Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Naysaburi, Abu Sa'd al-Zahid al-Kharkushi, the preacher, the complete master, one of the unique individuals of Khurasan in knowledge, asceticism, piety, fear, and way. He studied jurisprudence under Abu al-Hasan al-Masarjisi, then he abandoned status and sat with ascetics, adhered to action, performed pilgrimage, resided, then returned to Khurasan. He used to make caps and order them to be sold such that it was not known they were his handiwork, and he ate from the earnings of his hands. He built in his lane a school and a hospital, endowed properties for them, placed in the school a library of books, and authored numerous books. He died in Jumada al-Ula of the year 400-something AH. And Abd al-Ghafir said: I heard Abu al-Fadl Muhammad ibn Abd Allah al-Siram al-Zahid say: I saw the master praying for rain, saying: 'O dust! To You we have come, and You have brought us; no lord besides You suffices us. Your gate is spacious, its courtyard is generous; the poor are sheltered at Your gate.' Then he supplicated and said: 'O Allah, give us rain.' He said: He did not complete three times until we were watered like mouths of seven.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry comprising two separate reports on the life of Abu Sa'd al-Zahid al-Kharkushi, a famous ascetic and scholar of Khurasan. The first report, transmitted by al-Tanukhi via a chain that includes several narrators, notes that Abu Sa'd visited Baghdad as a pilgrim in 393 AH, then went to Mecca and resided there. Al-Khatib confirms his trustworthiness and piety, and his death year is reported as 406 AH. The second report, from Abd al-Ghafir ibn Isma'il, provides more detail: Abu Sa'd studied jurisprudence under Abu al-Hasan al-Masarjisi, then abandoned worldly status to sit with ascetics. He was a cap-maker and sold his own work anonymously to eat from his own earnings. He built a school and a hospital, endowed them, and stocked the school with books. He wrote many books and died in Jumada al-Ula of 400 AH (the exact decade is ambiguous: 'sana wa arba'ami'a' likely means 400-something, but the earlier report specifies 406). The passage concludes with an anecdote: he prayed for rain with a poem and supplication, and rain came immediately. This illustrates his spiritual station and the acceptance of his prayers.

عبد الملك بن أبي عثمان

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The phrase 'سنة وأربعمائة' in the second report is interpreted as exactly 400 AH.
Correction: The first report clarifies that 'سنة وأربعمائة' means 'the year 400-something' (i.e., 406 AH), not precisely 400.

Key Takeaway
Abu Sa'd al-Zahid was a scholar-ascetic whose life exemplified self-reliance, charity, and spiritual authority, as evidenced by his answered prayer for rain.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When he prayed for rain, he turned to Allah with humility and a poem acknowledging his need. In your current trials, do you turn to Allah with the same desperate reliance, or do you rely on your own resources? What is one specific thing you can only ask from Allah?

The Travels and Appointment of al-Qadi Abu 'Umar al-Bistami
Ibn Asakir details his teachers, travels, and judgeship charter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the early life, scholarly travels, and the event of his appointment as judge of Nishapur.

Core Idea
A judge's journey from student to courtroom begins with travel and a royal charter.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's biographical dictionary introduces us to a key Shafi'i figure, al-Qadi Abu 'Umar al-Bistami. Through a chain of narrators, we learn of his extensive travels in search of knowledge and his formal appointment as judge of Nishapur in 388 AH.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about his travels and appointment

This is a typical biographical entry in a historical work.
2
Identify the places he studied

These travels show his dedication to gathering knowledge.
3
Note the date and manner of his appointment

The joy of the hadith scholars indicates his respected status.
4
Understand the reaction of the scholars
The people of hadith showed immense joy, scattering gifts. The author mentions writing thanks to the Sultan. Reflect on the communal celebration.
This highlights the importance of judicial appointments in that era.
