ومنهم القاضي أبو عمر محمد بن الحسين البسطامی رحمه الله كتب إلى الشيخ الإمام أبو نصر القشيري قال أنا أبو بكر البيهقى قال أخبرنا أبو عبد الله محمد بن عبد الله الحافظ الحاكم قال : محمد بن الحسين بن محمد بن يحيى الفقيه المتكلم البارغ الواعظ أبو عمر بن أبي سعد البسطامي سمع باصبهان أبا القسم سليمان بن أحمد اللخمي وأقرانه وبالعراق أبا بكر بن مالك وأبا محمد بن ماسى وأقرانهما وسمع بالبصرة والأهواز وورد له العهد بقضاء نيسابور وقرئ علينا العهد غداة الخميس الثالث من ذي القعدة سنة ثمان وثمانين وثلاثمائة وأجلسه في مجلس القضاء في مسجد رجا في تلك الساعة وأظهر أهل الحديث من الفرح والاستبشار والنثار ما يطول شرحه وكتبنا بالدعاء والشكر إلى السلطان أيده الله وإلى أوليائه حدثني الشيخ أبو بكر يحيى بن إبراهيم بن أحمد بن محمد السلماسي بدمشق عن أبيه القاضي أبي طاهر بن أبي بكر قال قال أبو علي الحسن بن نصر بن كاكا المرندى الفقيه في ذكر الأستاذ أبي عثمان إسماعيل بن عبد الرحمن الصابونى قال وذكر القاضي أبا عمر البسطامي فقال كان منفرداً بلطائف السيادة معتمداً لمواقف الوفادة سفر بين السلطان المعظم وبين مجلس الخلافة أيام القادر بالله فافتن أهل بغداد بلسانه وإحسانه ويزهم في إيراده وإصداره بصحة إتقانه ونكث في ذلك المشهد النبوى . والمحفل الأمامي أشياء أعجب بها كفاته وسلم الفضل له فيها حماته وقالوا مثله فليكن نائباً عن ذلك السلطان المؤيد بالتوفيق والنصرة وافداً على مثل هذه الحضرة حتى صدر وحقائبه مملوءة من أصناف الإكرام وسهامه فائزة بأقصى المرام ثم كان شافعى العلم شريحى الحكم سحبانی البیان سحار اللسان أخبرنا الشريف أبو القسم على بن إبراهيم بن العباس والـفـقـيـه أبو الحسن على بن أحمد بن منصور وأبو منصور محمد بن عبد الملك المقرى قالوا قال لنا أبو بكر أحمد بن على بن ثابت الخطيب : محمد ابن الحسين ابن محمد بن الهيثم أبو عمر البسطامي الواعظ الفقيه على مذهب الشافعي ولی قضاء نيسابور وقدم بغداد وحدث بها عن أحمد بن عبد الرحمن ابن الجارود الرقى وسليمان بن أحمد الطبراني وأبي بكر القباب الأصبهاني وأحمد بن محمود بن خرزاد الأهوازى حدثني عنه الحسن بن محمد الخلال وذكر لى أنه قدم بغداد في حياة أبي حامد الاسفراینی قال وكان إماماً نظاراً وكان أبو حامد يعظمه ويحله
And among them is the judge Abu 'Umar Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Bistami, may Allah have mercy on him. He wrote to the Imam Abu Nasr al-Qushayri, saying: Abu Bakr al-Bayhaqi told us, saying: Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Abd Allah al-Hafiz al-Hakim informed us, saying: Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn Muhammad ibn Yahya, the jurist, the theologian, the brilliant, the preacher, Abu 'Umar ibn Abi Sa'd al-Bistami. He heard in Isfahan from Abu al-Qasim Sulayman ibn Ahmad al-Lakhmi and his peers, and in Iraq from Abu Bakr ibn Malik and Abu Muhammad ibn Masi and their peers, and he heard in Basra and Ahwaz. The charter for the judgeship of Nishapur arrived for him, and the charter was read to us on the morning of Thursday, the third of Dhu al-Qa'dah of the year 388 AH. He was seated in the council of judgment in the Mosque of Raja at that hour, and the people of hadith showed joy, gladness, and scattering that would take long to describe. We wrote with supplication and thanks to the Sultan, may Allah support him, and to his clients. The Shaykh Abu Bakr Yahya ibn Ibrahim ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Salamasi narrated to me in Damascus from his father, the judge Abu Tahir ibn Abi Bakr, who said: Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Nasr ibn Kaka al-Marandi, the jurist, said in mentioning the master Abu Uthman Isma'il ibn Abd al-Rahman al-Sabuni: He mentioned the judge Abu 'Umar al-Bistami and said: He was unique in the subtleties of leadership, relying on the stations of deputation. He traveled between the exalted Sultan and the council of the Caliphate during the days of al-Qadir bi'llah. The people of Baghdad were captivated by his tongue and his beneficence, and he excelled in his presentations and dispatches with the correctness of his proficiency. He broke in that prophetic assembly and the imam's gathering things that amazed his peers, and his protectors conceded excellence to him, and they said: 'Might such a one be a deputy for that Sultan, supported by divine guidance and victory, an envoy to such a presence.' Until he issued forth, his baggage filled with varieties of honor, and his arrows winning the utmost goal. Then he was Shafi'i in knowledge, Shurayhi in judgment, Sahbani in eloquence, enchanting of tongue. The noble Abu al-Qasim Ali ibn Ibrahim ibn al-Abbas and the jurist Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Mansur and Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Muqri informed us, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Khatib said to us: Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn Muhammad ibn al-Haytham Abu 'Umar al-Bistami, the preacher, the jurist according to the Shafi'i school, was appointed to the judgeship of Nishapur. He came to Baghdad and narrated there from Ahmad ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Jarud al-Raqqi, Sulayman ibn Ahmad al-Tabarani, Abu Bakr al-Qabad al-Isbahani, and Ahmad ibn Mahmud ibn Khurzadh al-Ahwazi. Al-Hasan ibn Muhammad al-Khallal narrated to me from him, and he mentioned that he came to Baghdad during the lifetime of Abu Hamid al-Isfara'ini. He said: He was a leading scholar of kalam, and Abu Hamid used to venerate and honor him.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is a composite biographical entry for al-Qadi Abu 'Umar al-Bistami, a Shafi'i jurist, theologian, and preacher. It is presented through multiple chains of transmission. The first chain goes through al-Bayhaqi and al-Hakim, stating that Abu 'Umar studied in Isfahan, Iraq, Basra, and Ahwaz. His appointment as judge of Nishapur occurred in 388 AH, and the reading of the charter was a joyous event. The second chain, via al-Salamasi, quotes a description of Abu 'Umar's role as an envoy between the Sultan and the Caliph al-Qadir bi'llah, emphasizing his eloquence and diplomatic skill. The description likens him to Shurayh in judgment and Sahban in eloquence, and notes that he was a Shafi'i in fiqh. The final chain, via al-Khatib, confirms his Shafi'i adherence, his teachers, and his visit to Baghdad during the time of Abu Hamid al-Isfara'ini, who held him in high esteem. The passage thus presents Abu 'Umar as a man of multiple talents: judge, preacher, envoy, and theologian.

Key Terms
القاضي أبو عمر البسطامي
محمد بن الحسين
قضاء نيسابور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The word 'البارغ' means 'the arrow'.
Correction: It is likely a misspelling of 'البارع' meaning 'the brilliant', which fits the context of describing his scholarly abilities.

Checkpoint

B) 393 AH
C) 400 AH
D) 406 AH

Key Takeaway
Al-Qadi Abu 'Umar al-Bistami was a well-traveled scholar appointed as judge of Nishapur in 388 AH, bringing joy to the hadith scholars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have read about al-Bistami's extensive travels to learn from various teachers. Where are you in your own journey of seeking knowledge? Have you sacrificed comfort to learn from those who carry authentic knowledge, or are you content with what is easy? What step will you take this week to prioritize seeking beneficial knowledge over your current routine?
?
The people of hadith rejoiced at the appointment of a righteous judge. When was the last time you felt genuine joy at seeing a person of faith placed in a position of authority? Does your heart celebrate the rise of the pious, or are you indifferent? Ask yourself: if a scholar you respect were appointed as a leader tomorrow, would you respond with the same exuberance as the hadith scholars of Nishapur?
?
Consider the chain of narrators in this lesson: it took multiple trustworthy individuals to transmit this single account to us. Your faith today is built on the sacrifices of scholars who traveled, verified, and taught. How does this realization affect your relationship with the knowledge you have? Do you treat it as a trust (amana) to pass on, or as a collection of facts? Write down one concrete way you will honor these transmitters by sharing what you learn.

The Eloquence and Diplomatic Role of al-Qadi Abu 'Umar al-Bistami
The author describes his role as envoy and his scholarly attributes through multiple chains.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Abu 'Umar al-Bistami served as an envoy between the Sultan and the Caliph, and his reputation for eloquence and knowledge.

Core Idea
A judge's tongue can move between sultan and caliph, captivating all with his speech.

The second part of Ibn Asakir's biography shifts from his appointment to a vivid description of Abu 'Umar's role as a diplomat. Through a chain of reporters, including a jurist's tribute, we see him as a unique figure who could represent the Sultan before the Caliph, and whose eloquence was compared to legendary figures.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of his diplomatic role

This part comes from a different narrator than the first.
2

The description uses terms like 'Sahbani al-bayan', 'Shuraihi al-hukm', and 'sahhar al-lisan'. Understand these as high praise for his speech and judgment.
Sahban was famous for eloquence; Shurayh for judicial wisdom.
3
Understand the context of his diplomatic mission
He traveled between the Sultan and the Caliph al-Qadir bi'llah, captivating Baghdad with his tongue and beneficence.
He returned with honors and his arrows hitting the mark.
4

The final chain confirms his Shafi'i school and that Abu Hamid, a leading scholar, venerated him.
This shows his high status among contemporary scholars.

And among them is the judge Abu 'Umar Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Bistami, may Allah have mercy on him. Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner

Biography of Abu Umar al-Bastami
Ibn Asakir relates the biography of Abu Umar al-Bastami through multiple chains.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the biography of Abu Umar al-Bastami as recorded by Ibn Asakir, including his appointment as judge, his scholarly status, and his connections.

Core Idea
Abu Umar al-Bastami was a Shafi'i judge and scholar who bridged the worlds of hadith, fiqh, and diplomacy.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's Tabyin Kidhb al-Muftari presents a multi-sourced biography of Abu Umar al-Bastami, a prominent Shafi'i judge and preacher. Through several chains of narration, we learn about his appointment as Qadi of Nishapur, his eloquence and diplomatic missions, his veneration by leading scholars like Abu Hamid al-Isfara'ini, and the various reports of his death. The entry exemplifies how classical biographers compiled information from multiple eyewitnesses.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage overview
Read the full Arabic passage and its translation to get a sense of the biographical flow. Note the different sections introduced by different chains.
The passage contains multiple isnads, so look for phrases like 'حدثني', 'أخبرنا', etc.
2
Focus on the appointment report
Notice the detailed description of his appointment as judge of Nishapur in 388 AH, including the date, location, and the joy of the hadith scholars.
This is a vivid historical account showing the public celebration.
3
Examine the praise from contemporaries
Read the laudatory description that praises his eloquence, judgment, and diplomatic role. Notice the similes: 'Shafi'i in knowledge, Shurayhi in judgment, Sahbani in eloquence'.
These comparisons highlight his excellence in multiple fields.
4
Analyze the scholarly details and death reports
Review the information from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi about his teachers, his veneration by Abu Hamid al-Isfara'ini, and the two death dates (407 and 408 AH). Note his sons al-Muwaffaq and al-Mu'ayyad.
The multiple death reports show the diversity of sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالعراق أبا بكر بن مالك وأبا محمد بن ماسى وأقرانهما وسمع بالبصرة والأهواز وورد له العهد بقضاء نيسابور وقرئ علينا العهد غداة الخميس الثالث من ذي القعدة سنة ثمان وثمانين وثلاثمائة وأجلسه في مجلس القضاء في مسجد رجا في تلك الساعة وأظهر أهل الحديث من الفرح والاستبشار والنثار ما يطول شرحه وكتبنا بالدعاء والشكر إلى السلطان أيده الله وإلى أوليائه حدثني الشيخ أبو بكر يحيى بن إبراهيم بن أحمد بن محمد السلماسي بدمشق عن أبيه القاضي أبي طاهر بن أبي بكر قال قال أبو علي الحسن بن نصر بن كاكا المرندى الفقيه في ذكر الأستاذ أبي عثمان إسماعيل بن عبد الرحمن الصابونى قال وذكر القاضي أبا عمر البسطامي فقال كان منفرداً بلطائف السيادة معتمداً لمواقف الوفادة سفر بين السلطان المعظم وبين مجلس الخلافة أيام القادر بالله فافتن أهل بغداد بلسانه وإحسانه ويزهم في إيراده وإصداره بصحة إتقانه ونكث في ذلك المشهد النبوي والمحفل الأمامي أشياء أعجب بها كفاته وسلم الفضل له فيها حماته وقالوا مثله فليكن نائباً عن ذلك السلطان المؤيد بالتوفيق والنصرة وافداً على مثل هذه الحضرة حتى صدر وحقائبه مملوءة من أصناف الإكرام وسهامه فائزة بأقصى المرام ثم كان شافعى العلم شريحى الحكم سحبانى البيان سحار اللسان أخبرنا الشريف أبو القسم على بن إبراهيم بن العباس والفقيه أبو الحسن على بن أحمد بن منصور وأبو منصور محمد بن عبد الملك المقرى قالوا قال لنا أبو بكر أحمد بن على بن ثابت الخطيب : محمد ابن الحسين ابن محمد بن الهيثم أبو عمر البسطامي الواعظ الفقيه على مذهب الشافعي ولی قضاء نيسابور وقدم بغداد وحدث بها عن أحمد بن عبد الرحمن ابن الجارود الرقى وسليمان بن أحمد الطبراني وأبي بكر القباب الأصبهاني وأحمد بن محمود بن خرزاد الأهوازى حدثني عنه الحسن بن محمد الخلال وذكر لى أنه قدم بغداد في حياة أبي حامد الاسفراینی قال وكان إماماً نظاراً وكان أبو حامد يعظمه ويجله حدثنى أبو صالح أحمد بن عبد الملك المؤذن وأبو بكر محمد ابن يحيى بن إبراهيم النيسابوريان قالا توفى أبو عمر البسطامي بنيسابور في سبع وأربعمائة . كتب إلى الشيخ أبو الحسن عبد الغافر بن إسماعيل . قال : محمد بن الحسين بن محمد بن الهيثم بن القسم بن مالك أبو عمر البسطامي القاضى الإمام توفى سنة ثمان وأربعمائة وأعقب الموفق والمؤيد .
And in Iraq, Abu Bakr ibn Malik and Abu Muhammad ibn Masa and their peers, and he heard (hadith) in Basra and Ahwaz. His appointment as judge of Nishapur arrived, and the appointment was read to us on the morning of Thursday, the third of Dhu al-Qi'dah in the year 388 AH, and he was seated in the seat of judgment in the mosque of Raja at that hour. The people of hadith showed joy and rejoicing and scattering (of coins) whose description would be lengthy. And we wrote with supplication and thanks to the Sultan, may God support him, and to his supporters. The shaykh Abu Bakr Yahya ibn Ibrahim ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Salmasii related to me in Damascus, from his father, the judge Abu Tahir ibn Abi Bakr, who said: Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Nasr ibn Kaka al-Muradi al-Faqih said, mentioning the master Abu Uthman Ismail ibn Abd al-Rahman al-Sabuni, who said: He mentioned the judge Abu Umar al-Bastami, saying: He was uniquely possessed of the subtleties of lordship, relying on positions of delegation. He traveled between the great Sultan and the caliphal court during the days of al-Qadir bi'llah. The people of Baghdad were captivated by his speech and beneficence, and he excelled in presenting and issuing with the soundness of his mastery. He exhibited, in that prophetic assembly and the imamite gathering, things that amazed his peers, and the guardians conceded excellence to him. They said: 'Someone like him should serve as deputy for that Sultan, supported by divine guidance and victory, and as a delegate to such a court.' Until he returned, his saddlebags filled with various kinds of honor, and his arrows (i.e., endeavors) achieving the utmost aspiration. Then he was a Shafi'i in knowledge, a Shurayhi in judgment, a Sihbani in eloquence, a sorcerer of the tongue. The sharif Abu al-Qasim Ali ibn Ibrahim ibn al-Abbas, the faqih Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Mansur, and Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Muqri informed us, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Khatib said to us: Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn Muhammad ibn al-Haytham Abu Umar al-Bastami, the preacher, the faqih according to the Shafi'i madhhab, was appointed judge of Nishapur. He came to Baghdad and narrated there from Ahmad ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Jarud al-Raqqi, Sulayman ibn Ahmad al-Tabarani, Abu Bakr al-Qabab al-Isbahani, and Ahmad ibn Mahmud ibn Khurzad al-Ahwazi. Al-Hasan ibn Muhammad al-Khallal narrated to me from him, and he mentioned to me that he came to Baghdad during the lifetime of Abu Hamid al-Isfara'ini. He said: He was a leading scholar and a debater, and Abu Hamid used to venerate him and honor him. Abu Salih Ahmad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Mu'adhdhin and Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Yahya ibn Ibrahim al-Naysaburiyan narrated to me, saying: Abu Umar al-Bastami died in Nishapur in 407 AH. And the shaykh Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Ghafir ibn Ismail wrote to me, saying: Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn Muhammad ibn al-Haytham ibn al-Qasim ibn Malik Abu Umar al-Bastami, the judge, the imam, died in 408 AH, and he left behind al-Muwaffaq and al-Mu'ayyad.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry (tarjama) for Abu Umar al-Bastami, compiled by Ibn Asakir through multiple chains of transmission. It begins with an account of his appointment as judge of Nishapur in 388 AH, describing the joy of the hadith scholars. Then it presents a laudatory description from a group of scholars, praising his eloquence, judgment, and diplomatic role between the Sultan and the Caliph. Next, Ibn Asakir cites al-Khatib al-Baghdadi's biographical notice, giving his full name, his Shafi'i affiliation, his teachers, and his veneration by Abu Hamid al-Isfara'ini. Finally, two reports about his death are given: one in 407 AH and another in 408 AH, with mention of his sons al-Muwaffaq and al-Mu'ayyad. The entry highlights his scholarly and political status.

?
He traveled between the Sultan and the Caliph as a trusted mediator. In your life, you often mediate between people. Are you known as a peacemaker? Commit to a specific conflict you will help resolve this week.

The Biography of Abu al-Qasim al-Bajali: A Shafi'i-Ash'ari Judge
Ibn Asakir relates the biography of Abu al-Qasim al-Bajali, a Shafi'i-Ash'ari judge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and scholarly credentials of Abu al-Qasim al-Bajali, a prominent Shafi'i-Ash'ari judge and theologian.

Core Idea
Al-Bajali was a trustworthy judge, Shafi'i jurist, and Ash'ari theologian who authored works in usul.

This lesson presents a biographical entry from Ibn Asakir's Tabyin Kidhb al-Muftari, detailing the life of Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi Amr al-Bajali. The passage traces his teachers, judicial appointments, madhhab affiliation, and death date, highlighting his status as a faqih, usuli, and mutakallim. By examining this entry, we gain insight into the transmission of Ash'ari-Shafi'i scholarship in 5th-century Baghdad.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get an overview of al-Bajali's biography.
Notice the isnad (chain of transmission) at the beginning.
2
Identify key details
Note his teachers, judicial appointments, madhhab, and his lineage tracing back to a Companion.
3
Understand his scholarly identity
The passage describes him as 'faqih usuli mutakallim' and 'Shafi'i Ash'ari'. Reflect on what these terms imply about his expertise.
4
Consider the isnad and sources
Notice the multiple chains of transmission (Ibn Asakir via al-Khatib and al-Shirazi). This shows how biographical information was preserved and verified.
5
Reflect on the significance
Why would Ibn Asakir include this biography? It affirms the Ash'ari affiliation and scholarly credibility of al-Bajali.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخبرنا الشيخان أبو الحسن بن قبيس وأبو منصور بن زريق قالا قال أنا أبو بكر أحمد بن على بن ثابت الخطيب : عبد الواحد بن محمد بن عثمان أبو القسم بن أبي عمرو البجلي ، سمع أحمد بن سلمان النجاد وجعفر الخلدى والحسن بن محمد بن موسى بن إسحق الأنصارى ومحمد ابن الحسن ابن زياد النقاش ، وهبة الله بن محمد بن حبش الفراء وجعفر بن محمد بن الحكم المؤدب ومحمد بن على بن علون المقرى كتبنا عنه وكان ثقة ، تقلد القضاء من قبل أبى على التنوخي على دقوقا وخانجان ومن قبل أبي الحسن الجزري على جازر ثم ولى قضاء عكبرا من قبل أبي الحسن بن أبي محمد بن معروف وكان ينتحل في الفقه مذهب الشافعي ويعرف أصول الفقه وسمعته أملى على نسبه فقال أنى محمد بن عثمان بن إبراهيم ابن محمد بن خالد بن إسحق بن الزبرقان بن خالد ابن عبد الملك بن جرير ابن عبد الله البجلی صاحب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، توفى ابن أبي عمرو في اليوم الذي مات فيه ابن مهدى وهو يوم الاثنين الرابع عشر من رجب سنة عشر وأربعمائة ودفن من الغد في مقبره باب حرب أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم بن السمرقندى قال ثنا أبو إسحق إبراهيم بن على الشيرازي لفظا قال : أبو القسم عبد الواحد بن عثمان بن البجلي ويعرف بابن أبي عمرو ومات سنة عشر وأربعمائة وكان فقيهاً أصولياً متكلما له مصنفات حسنة في الأصول وذكره أبو الفضل بن خبرون في الوفيات فقال الفقيه الشافعى الأشعرى .
The two shaykhs, Abu al-Hasan ibn Qubays and Abu Mansur ibn Zurayq, informed us, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Khatib narrated to us: Abd al-Wahid ibn Muhammad ibn Uthman Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi Amr al-Bajali. He heard from Ahmad ibn Salman al-Najjad, Ja'far al-Khalidi, al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn Musa ibn Ishaq al-Ansari, Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Ziyad al-Naqqash, Hibatullah ibn Muhammad ibn Habash al-Farra', Ja'far ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hakam al-Mu'addib, and Muhammad ibn Ali ibn Ulwan al-Muqri. We wrote from him, and he was trustworthy. He held the position of judge under Abu Ali al-Tanukhi over Duquqa and Khanjan, and under Abu al-Hasan al-Jazari over Jazar, then he was appointed judge of Ukbara under Abu al-Hasan ibn Abi Muhammad ibn Ma'ruf. He professed the Shafi'i madhhab in fiqh and knew the principles of fiqh (usul al-fiqh). I heard him dictating his lineage, saying: I am Muhammad ibn Uthman ibn Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Khalid ibn Ishaq ibn al-Zubayrqan ibn Khalid ibn Abd al-Malik ibn Jarir ibn Abd Allah al-Bajali, the Companion of the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace. Ibn Abi Amr died on the same day that Ibn Mahdi died, which is Monday, the fourteenth of Rajab in the year 410 AH, and he was buried the next day in the cemetery of Bab Harb. The shaykh Abu al-Qasim ibn al-Samarqandi informed us, saying: Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Ali al-Shirazi narrated to us orally, saying: Abu al-Qasim Abd al-Wahid ibn Uthman al-Bajali, known as Ibn Abi Amr, died in 410 AH. He was a faqih, an usuli, a mutakallim, and he authored excellent works in usul. Abu al-Fadl ibn Khayrun mentioned him in the Obituaries, saying: The Shafi'i, the Ash'ari.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Abd al-Wahid ibn Muhammad al-Bajali, known as Ibn Abi Amr. It begins with an isnad from Ibn Asakir through al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, then lists his teachers, confirming his reliability as a hadith transmitter. It details his judicial appointments in various towns, his Shafi'i jurisprudence, and his knowledge of usul al-fiqh. His full lineage is given, tracing back to a Companion. The date of his death is recorded as Monday, 14 Rajab 410 AH. A second chain from al-Shirazi adds that he was a faqih, usuli, mutakallim, and authored works in usul. Finally, Ibn Khayrun's obituary identifies him as Shafi'i-Ash'ari. The entry thus highlights his scholarly credentials and his theological affiliation with Ash'arism.

قضاء
الشافعي
أصول الفقه
الأشعري
فقيه أصولي متكلم

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think al-Bajali was merely a judge without theological expertise.
Correction: But the passage confirms he was a mutakallim (theologian) and authored works in usul al-fiqh.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage emphasizes his lineage back to a Companion of the Prophet (ﷺ). Do you ever think about your own spiritual lineage—who you learned from, who influenced your faith? Are you taking steps to be a trustworthy link in that chain for those after you, or are you neglecting that responsibility? What will you do today to honor that trust?

Abu al-Qasim al-Bajali: A Shafi'i Judge and Ash'ari Theologian
Biography of Abu al-Qasim al-Bajali with emphasis on his Ash'ari and Shafi'i identity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a biographical entry from Ibn 'Asakir's Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari establishes the Ash'ari affiliation of a Shafi'i judge, demonstrating the integration of Ash'ari theology with mainstream fiqh and qada.

Core Idea
Ash'ari scholars were not just theologians; they were judges and jurists.

This biography from Ibn 'Asakir's work presents the life of Abu al-Qasim al-Bajali, a Shafi'i qadi who was also a mutakallim. The passage demonstrates how Ash'ari identity was not a separate sect but a theological stance embraced by leading Shafi'i scholars. It also provides a chain of transmission, showing how such biographical knowledge was preserved and validated.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the translation. Notice the chain of narrators at the beginning.
The passage begins with a chain from two shaykhs to al-Khatib al-Baghdadi.
2
Identify key roles
Identify the roles mentioned for al-Bajali: qadi, faqih, usuli, mutakallim. Note the explicit labels 'Shafi'i' and 'Ash'ari'.
He was a judge in multiple cities and authored works on usul al-fiqh.
3
Connect to context
Reflect on the significance of a Shafi'i judge being described as Ash'ari. What does this tell about the acceptance of Ash'ari theology in mainstream Shafi'i circles?
The Ash'ari school was often associated with Shafi'i fiqh.
4
Analyze the biographical method
Notice how the biography uses multiple chains of transmission and witnesses to establish credibility. Consider why this method is important for historical theology.
The second witness, al-Shirazi, confirms the death date and adds the description 'faqih usuli mutakallim'.
5
Reflect on misconceptions
Think about the common misunderstanding that Ash'ari scholars were only theologians. This biography shows a scholar who was also a judge and jurist.
The passage counters the idea that Ash'aris were isolated from legal practice.

Among them is Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi 'Amr al-Bajali al-Baghdadi, may Allah have mercy on him. Both shaykhs Abu al-Hasan ibn Qubays and Abu Mansur ibn Zuraiq reported to us, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn 'Ali ibn Thabit al-Khatib informed us: 'Abd al-Wahid ibn Muhammad ibn 'Uthman Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi 'Amr al-Bajali heard from Ahmad ibn Salman al-Najjad, Ja'far al-Khalidi, al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn Musa ibn Ishaq al-Ansari, Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Ziyad al-Naqqash, Hibat Allah ibn Muhammad ibn Habsh al-Farra', Ja'far ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hakam al-Mu'addib, and Muhammad ibn 'Ali ibn 'Alun al-Muqri'. We wrote from him, and he was trustworthy. He assumed the position of judge on behalf of Abu 'Ali al-Tanukhi over Duquqa and Khanjan, and on behalf of Abu al-Hasan al-Jazari over Jazar, then he assumed the qada' of 'Ukbara on behalf of Abu al-Hasan ibn Abi Muhammad ibn Ma'ruf. He adopted in fiqh the madhhab of al-Shafi'i and knew usul al-fiqh. I heard him dictating his lineage, saying: I am Muhammad ibn 'Uthman ibn Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Khalid ibn Ishaq ibn al-Zubayrqan ibn Khalid ibn 'Abd al-Malik ibn Jarir ibn 'Abd Allah al-Bajali, the Companion of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him. Ibn Abi 'Amr died on the same day that Ibn Mahdi died, which was Monday, the fourteenth of Rajab in the year four hundred and ten [AH], and was buried the next day in the cemetery of Bab Harb. Abu al-Qasim ibn al-Samarqandi reported to us, saying: Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn 'Ali al-Shirazi narrated to us orally, saying: Abu al-Qasim 'Abd al-Wahid ibn 'Uthman al-Bajali, known as Ibn Abi 'Amr, died in the year four hundred and ten [AH]. He was a faqih, usuli, mutakallim, and he authored excellent works on usul. Abu al-Fadl ibn Khabrun mentioned him in his death notices, saying: He was a Shafi'i Ash'ari faqih.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry about Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi 'Amr al-Bajali, an influential scholar with explicit Ash'ari affiliation. It begins with a chain of narration from two shaykhs who heard from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, who provides details: his teachers (including well-known figures from Baghdad), his trustworthiness, his judicial appointments in several towns, and his Shafi'i fiqh and knowledge of usul al-fiqh. His lineage is traced back to a Companion, showing noble ancestry. His death date is given relative to Ibn Mahdi. A second witness from al-Shirazi confirms his death in the same year and adds that he was a faqih, usuli, mutakallim with good works. Finally, Ibn Khabrun explicitly states that he was a Shafi'i Ash'ari. This entry documents the Ash'ari presence among Shafi'i scholars and judges.

A Noble Ash'ari: The Biography of al-Sharif Abu Talib
Biographical entry confirming a Sharif's Ash'arism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Ash'ari theology was embraced by noble lineages like the Hashimites, as exemplified by al-Sharif Abu Talib.

Core Idea
Even a Sharif followed the Ash'ari madhhab.

This brief biography from Ibn 'Asakir records the death of a Damascene Sharif and his theological affiliation. It may seem like a simple notice, but its inclusion in this work carries weight: it shows that Ash'arism was not a marginal movement but was adopted even by those with noble Hashimi lineage. Let's examine how this single entry refutes later misconceptions.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical notice
Read the Arabic and translation to get the facts: name, death, teachers, and theological madhhab.
2
Notice the chain of transmission
Ibn 'Asakir uses a chain from al-Akfani to al-Kittani to the subject. This reminds us that biography was a serious science.
3
Reflect on the significance of the statement
The final phrase 'yadhhabu ila madhhab Abi al-Hasan al-Ash'ari' is the punchline. Why would Ibn 'Asakir include this detail? Understand the apologetic value.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم الشريف أبو طالب بن المهتدى الهاشمي الدمشقی رحمه الله ) أخبرنا الشيخ الأمين أبو محمد هبة الله بن أحمد الأكفاني قال حدثنا أبو محمد عبد العزيز بن أحمد الكتاني قال توفى شيخنا الشريف أبو طالب عبد الوهاب بن عبد الملك بن المهتدى بالله الفقيه يوم الاثنين العاشر من شهر رمضان سنة خمس عشرة وأربعمائة حدث عن أبي عبد بن إبراهيم بن مروان وغيره بشئ يسير وكان فقيهاً حافظاً للفقه يذهب إلى مذهب أبي الحسن الأشعري رحمه الله
Among them is al-Sharif Abu Talib ibn al-Muhtadi al-Hashimi al-Dimashqi, may Allah have mercy on him. The trustworthy shaykh Abu Muhammad Hibat Allah ibn Ahmad al-Akfani reported to us, saying: Abu Muhammad 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Ahmad al-Kittani narrated to us, saying: Our shaykh al-Sharif Abu Talib 'Abd al-Wahhab ibn 'Abd al-Malik ibn al-Muhtadi billah, the faqih, died on Monday, the tenth of Ramadan in the year four hundred and fifteen [AH]. He narrated from Abu 'Abd [Allah] ibn Ibrahim ibn Marwan and others a small amount. He was a faqih, a memorizer of fiqh, and he followed the madhhab of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is a brief biographical notice of al-Sharif Abu Talib, a Hashemite noble (sharif) from Damascus. The chain includes al-Akfani and al-Kittani. The notice gives his death date, his limited hadith transmission from a few teachers, and his expertise as a faqih and hafiz of fiqh. Crucially, it concludes by stating that he 'yadhhabu ila madhhab Abi al-Hasan al-Ash'ari' (he went to the madhhab of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari). This explicit statement is significant for showing that Ash'ari doctrine was adopted even by descendants of the Prophet, countering claims that Ash'arism was a bid'a or contrary to the sunna.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Biography of Abu al-Hasan ibn Ma Shadha al-Isbahani
Biographical entry on a scholar who opposed anthropomorphism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and stance of Abu al-Hasan ibn Ma Shadha al-Isbahani, a scholar who opposed anthropomorphism and corruptions in Sufism.

Core Idea
A scholar who combined outer and inner knowledge and fearlessly corrected misguided Sufis.

This passage introduces us to a remarkable figure from early Islamic history: Abu al-Hasan ibn Ma Shadha al-Isbahani. He was both a jurist and a Sufi, but he did not shy away from criticizing those who deviated into anthropomorphism and license. Through his biography, we see the importance of balancing exoteric and esoteric knowledge, and the courage required to speak truth.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to get the full meaning.
Pay attention to the chain of transmission at the beginning.
2
Note his scholarly credentials
Identify that he was a jurist, a prominent Sufi, and combined outward knowledge (ẓāhir) with inward knowledge (bāṭin).
He surpassed others in character and endurance.
3
Identify the heresies he condemned
The passage lists three specific heresies: ḥulūl (incarnation), ibāḥa (licentiousness), and tashbīh (anthropomorphism). These are what he denounced among the anthropomorphist Sufis.
4
Understand the reaction to his criticism
Notice that people turned away from him out of ignorance and stubbornness, not because he was wrong.
This shows the challenge of calling to truth.

ومنهم أبو الحسن بن ما شاذة الأصبهاني رحمه الله له حدثني الشيخ أبو مسعود عبد الرحيم بن على بن أحمد المعدل بأصبهان قال أنا أبو على الحسن بن أحمد بن الحسن المقرى وأجازه لى أبو على قال قال لنا أبو نعيم أحمد بن عبد الله الحافظ : علی بن محمد بن أحمد بن ميلة أبو الحسن يعرف محمد بما شاذه كان من شيوخ الفقهاء أحد أعلام الصوفية صحب أبا بكر عبد الله بن إبراهيم بن واضح وأبا جعفر محمد بن الحسن بن منصور وغيرهما وزاد عليهما في طريقتهما خلقاً وفترة جمع بين علم الظاهر والباطن لا تأخذه في الله لومة لائم كان ينكر على مشبهة الصوفية وغيرهم من الجهال فساد مقالتهم في الحلول والإباحة والتشبيه وغير ذلك من جميع أخلاقهم وقبح أفعالهم وأقوالهم فعدلوا عنه لما دعاهم إلى الحق جهلا وعنادا انفرد فى وقته بالرواية عن محمد بن محمد ابن يونس الأبهرى وأبي عمرو بن حكيم المصاحفى والأسواري وغيرهم ، توفى يوم الفطر ضحوة يوم الأربعاء سنة أربع عشرة وأربعمائة ودفن من يومه رحمة الله عليه ورضوانه
And among them is Abu al-Hasan ibn Ma Shadha al-Isbahani, may God have mercy on him. [Let me?] the sheikh Abu Mas'ud 'Abd al-Rahim ibn 'Ali ibn Ahmad al-Mu'addil in Isfahan narrated to me, saying: Abu 'Ali al-Hasan ibn Ahmad ibn al-Hasan al-Muqri' informed us, and Abu 'Ali authorized me, saying: Abu Nu'aym Ahmad ibn 'Abd Allah al-Hafiz said to us: 'Ali ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Mayla, Abu al-Hasan, known as Muhammad ibn Ma Shadha, was among the senior jurists, one of the prominent Sufis. He accompanied Abu Bakr 'Abd Allah ibn Ibrahim ibn Wadih and Abu Ja'far Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Mansur and others, and he surpassed them in their path in character and endurance. He combined exoteric and esoteric knowledge; no blamer's reproach in God affected him. He used to denounce the anthropomorphists among the Sufis and other ignorant ones for the corruption of their doctrine of incarnation, licentiousness, anthropomorphism, and other such things, and all their [evil] traits and ugly deeds and statements. So they turned away from him because he called them to the truth out of ignorance and obstinacy. He was unique in his time in narrating from Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Yunus al-Abhari, Abu 'Amr ibn Hakim al-Masahifi, al-Isfisari [?], and others. He died on the day of Fitr in the forenoon of Wednesday, the year 414 AH, and was buried the same day. May God's mercy and pleasure be upon him.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry on Abu al-Hasan ibn Ma Shadha al-Isbahani. It begins by listing his chain of transmission to the author, then describes his scholarly and spiritual credentials. He was a jurist and a prominent Sufi who combined outward religious sciences (ʿilm al-ẓāhir) with inward spiritual knowledge (ʿilm al-bāṭin). He was fearless in criticizing anthropomorphists (al-mushabbiha) among the Sufis and others for their erroneous beliefs in incarnation (ḥulūl), libertinism (ibāḥa), and anthropomorphism (tashbīh). Because of his strong opposition, they turned against him out of ignorance and stubbornness. He was unique in his time in transmitting from certain scholars. The entry concludes with his date of death: the morning of Eid al-Fitr, Wednesday, 414 AH, and burial the same day.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: He was just a simple Sufi without strong theological stances.
Correction: He was actually a rigorous critic who denounced anthropomorphism and licentiousness among Sufis.

Key Takeaway
Abu al-Hasan ibn Ma Shadha exemplified the integration of outward knowledge and inward spirituality, and fearlessly opposed deviations in Sufism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Ibn Ma Shadha combined outward knowledge and inward spirituality. Which of these two are you neglecting? What concrete step can you take this week to strengthen the weaker side?

Biographical entry on a Damascene Ash'ari jurist.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the biographical details of al-Sharif Abu Talib al-Hashimi and his significance as an early Ash'ari jurist in Damascus.

Core Idea
Al-Sharif Abu Talib's biography shows the spread of Ash'arism in 5th-century Damascus.

This lesson introduces a brief biographical entry from Ibn 'Asakir's Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari. The entry records the death and scholarly profile of al-Sharif Abu Talib, a Damascene jurist. While the details are simple, the mention of his adherence to the Ash'ari school is a valuable historical marker. Let's examine the text to see what it reveals about early Ash'ari presence in Damascus.

List the full name, death date, teachers, and scholarly description. What do we learn about his education and expertise?
He narrated little, but was a jurist and memorizer of fiqh.

This is a direct attestation of Ash'ari affiliation in a biographical dictionary.
4
Consider historical context

Damascus was a center of traditionalist scholarship; this shows Ash'arism was present there early.

The key detail for kalam history is that he adhered to the school of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, which confirms the spread of Ash'arism in Damascus during the 5th century AH.

Life of Abu Mu'ammar al-Jurjani
Biographical entry on a Hadith scholar and judge from Jurjan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and scholarly achievements of Abu Mu'ammar al-Jurjani, including his early education, travels, and role as a judge.

Core Idea
A young prodigy who memorized the Quran at seven and later became a judge.

This lesson presents the biography of Abu Mu'ammar al-Jurjani, a scholar from Jurjan. The passage details his noble lineage, early education under his father, travels to Baghdad and Mecca, and his eventual appointment as a judge. It highlights his remarkable intellectual ability from a young age.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the chain of narration and the biographical details.
This is a traditional biographical entry from a historical work.
2
Identify key life events
Look for events: his birth lineage, study with his grandfather, travel to Baghdad and Mecca, hearing from scholars like al-Daraqutni, and his father's testimony of his abilities.
3
Note the anecdote about his childhood
His father states he memorized the Quran at seven, learned inheritance law, and corrected a judge's error. This shows his early genius.
4
Understand his role as a judge
After his father's death, he assumed the position of judge. Consider how his early learning prepared him for this role.
His judicial career is mentioned at the end.

And among them is Abu Mu'ammar ibn Abi Sa'd ibn Abi Bakr al-Jurjani. Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Ahmad ibn 'Umar informed us, saying: Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Mas'ada ibn Isma'il ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim al-Jurjani informed us, saying: Abu al-Qasim Hamza ibn Yusuf ibn Ibrahim al-Sahmi informed us by hearing or by permission in the book Tarikh Jurjan which he authored, saying: Abu Mu'ammar al-Fadl ibn Isma'il ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-'Abbas al-Isma'ili, the imam, narrated from his grandfather, the imam Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ibrahim al-Isma'ili, many books, and he heard from him his book al-Jami' on the Sahih of Bukhari and other collections, compilations, [names of] sheikhs, and dictations. His father, the imam Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili, preserved his hearing and carried him to Baghdad and Mecca in the year 384 AH, and he stayed there until he performed Hajj in 385, and returned in 386 to Jurjan. He had heard in Baghdad from Abu al-Hasan al-Daraqutni most of his books and writings, and wrote from Abu Hafs ibn Shahin and Abu al-Hasan al-Jabali and others, and in Mecca from Yusuf ibn al-Dukhayl and Abu Zur'a al-Janbi al-Jurjani and a group. He sat for dictation after the death of his uncle Abu Nasr al-Isma'ili. [I heard?] Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili say: 'This son of mine, Abu Mu'ammar, at seven years old he memorized the Quran and learned the laws of inheritance (fara'id), and he answered a question in which one of our judges erred.' And he had granted him what he had from Muhammad ibn 'Uthman ibn Abi Shayba, which he did not read to anyone after that. The last thing he narrated was heard by Abu Mu'ammar and Abu al-'Ala', then no one was able to [hear] all of it except for hadiths he extracted in places. And he became a judge after the death of his father, the imam Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is a detailed biography of Abu Mu'ammar al-Jurjani. It provides his full lineage and notes that he was an imam. He narrated many books from his grandfather, Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili, and heard his Jami'. His father took him to Baghdad and Mecca for study. He heard from major scholars like al-Daraqutni. After his uncle's death, he began dictating hadith. A striking anecdote from his father praises his precocious intelligence: at age seven he memorized the Quran, learned inheritance law, and corrected a judge's error. He was entrusted with his father's books from Muhammad ibn 'Uthman ibn Abi Shayba. Finally, he served as judge after his father's death.

The lineage traces back to 'Abd Allah ibn Mas'ud, a prominent Companion.

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner

The Life and Scholarship of Abu Hazim al-Abdawi
Biography of Abu Hazim al-Abdawi with isnad and death accounts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life, scholarly network, and dedication of the hadith scholar Abu Hazim al-Abdawi al-Naysaburi as recorded by Ibn Asakir.

Core Idea
Abu Hazim's life exemplifies the vast transmission and writing culture of classical hadith scholarship.

Abu Hazim al-Abdawi, a hadith master from Nishapur, is introduced through a chain of transmission reaching back to his own teachers. The passage details his extensive scholarly network, his credibility, and his remarkable claim of writing ten thousand parts from ten teachers. It also records his sudden death and burial led by a prominent scholar.

Guided Path
1
Trace the chain of transmission
Notice how Ibn Asakir cites his own sources for this biography: two shaykhs who heard from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi. This shows the isnad culture surrounding biographical literature.
The chain is: Ibn Asakir ← two shaykhs ← al-Khatib al-Baghdadi ← ...
2
Identify Abu Hazim's lineage
Read his full name: Umar ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim... ibn Abdullah ibn Utbah ibn Masud. Note the final link to the companion Ibn Masud.
The nisbah 'al-Abdawi' comes from his grandfather Abdawayh.
3
List his teachers and students
The passage lists many teachers, including Abu Bakr al-Ismaili, and students like Abu Ishaq al-Tabari. Observe the geographic spread from Nishapur to Baghdad and Herat.
The text says 'and many others' indicating his network was vast.
4
Reflect on the anecdote about writing
Abu Hazim claimed to have written ten thousand parts from ten teachers, a thousand each. This illustrates the immense effort of hadith transmission.
He also purchased books, showing multiple methods of acquisition.

And among them is Abu Hazim al-Abdawi al-Naysaburi the hafiz, may God have mercy on him. The two shaykhs informed us: Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik ibn al-Hasan ibn Khayrun in Baghdad and Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn al-Hasan in Damascus, they said: the shaykh Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Hafiz narrated to us: Umar ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Abdawayh ibn Sadus ibn Ali ibn Abd Allah ibn Ubayd Allah ibn Abd Allah ibn Utbah ibn Masud, Abu Hazim al-Hudhali al-Abdawi al-Araj, from the people of Nishapur. He heard from Ismail ibn Najid al-Sulami, Muhammad ibn Abd Allah al-Sulayti, Muhammad ibn Jaafar ibn Matar, Abu Bakr al-Ismaili, Muhammad ibn Ismail al-Muqri, Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ali al-Qaffal, Ibrahim ibn Muhammad al-Nasrabadhi, Ali ibn Bandar al-Sayrafi, Ismail ibn Abd Allah ibn Mikal, Muhammad ibn Abd Allah ibn Ali al-Samadhi, Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Abd al-Aziz al-Jurjani, Bishr ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ali ibn Ziyad, and many others whose mention spreads from al-Isfarayini and Abd Allah ibn M [؟] the people of Nishapur, Herat, and elsewhere. And he came to Baghdad long ago and narrated there, so from him heard Abu Ishaq al-Tabari al-Muqri, Muhammad ibn Abi al-Fawaris, Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Abnusi, Abu Abd Allah ibn al-Katib, and others. And al-Tanukhi and Abu Yala Ahmad ibn Abd al-Wahid narrated from us. And Abu Hazim remained alive until I met him in Nishapur and wrote much from him. He was trustworthy, truthful, knowledgeable, a hafiz, people would listen to his instruction and write from his selections. Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Ali al-Wakhshi wrote to me from Nishapur mentioning that Abu Hazim died on the day of Eid al-Fitr of the year 417 AH. The shaykh Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Ghafir ibn Ismail ibn Abd al-Ghafir al-Farisi wrote to me, saying: Umar ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Abdawayh—then he traced his lineage as before—and said: I heard the shaykh Abu Salih Ahmad ibn Abd al-Malik say: I heard Abu Hazim say: I wrote in my own hand from ten of my teachers ten thousand parts, from each teacher a thousand parts, besides what I purchased. He mentioned among them the Imam Abu Bakr al-Ismaili, Abu al-Hasan al-Hajjaji al-Hafiz, and al-Hakim Abu Ahmad al-Hafiz. Abd al-Ghafir said: al-Hakim Abu Abd Allah selected from him and narrated from him, and his benefits spread in the horizons. And he died suddenly on the night of Wednesday, the second of Shawwal of the year 417 AH, and the master Imam al-Isfarayini, may God have mercy on him, prayed over him.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is a biography of Abu Hazim al-Abdawi al-Naysaburi, a prominent hadith scholar. It begins with an isnad (chain of transmission) for the biography itself, showing the author's sources: the two shaykhs Abu Mansur and Abu al-Hasan, who heard from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi (Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit). The biography proper starts with his full name and lineage, tracing back to Ibn Masud, a companion. It then lists many of his teachers, including well-known figures like Abu Bakr al-Ismaili and al-Qaffal. The list ends with 'and many others whose mention spreads from al-Isfarayini and Abd Allah ibn M... the people of Nishapur, Herat, and elsewhere,' indicating the wide geographical range of his teachers. Next, it mentions his travels: he came to Baghdad and narrated there, and a list of his students is given, including Abu Ishaq al-Tabari and others. The author (Ibn Asakir) mentions that he met Abu Hazim in Nishapur and wrote much from him, praising him as trustworthy, truthful, knowledgeable, and a hafiz. Then two reports about his death: one from Abu Ali al-Wakhshi stating he died on Eid al-Fitr 417 AH, and another from Abd al-Ghafir al-Farisi providing a more detailed account. In that account, Abu Hazim is quoted as saying he wrote ten thousand parts from ten teachers, a thousand from each, besides purchased books. He names three of those teachers: Abu Bakr al-Ismaili, Abu al-Hasan al-Hajjaji, and al-Hakim Abu Ahmad. The passage concludes with details of his sudden death on the night of the second of Shawwal 417 AH, with the funeral prayer led by the master Imam al-Isfarayini.

Biography of Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini through an isnad, highlighting his scholarship and his school.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini was a pioneering scholar and founder of an unparalleled school.

This lesson introduces the biography of Imam Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini, a leading jurist, theologian, and ascetic. His reputation spanned Iraq and Khurasan, and he established a remarkable school in Nishapur. The passage provides a glimpse into his scholarly legacy through an isnad-linked report.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage carefully, then follow with the literal English translation. Notice the isnad chain and the descriptions of the scholar.
The passage is a biographical entry from a historical work, so the isnad establishes authenticity.

Being foremost in these sciences indicates mastery.

The shaykh Abu Nasr Abd al-Rahim ibn Abd al-Karim ibn Hawazin wrote to me, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Bayhaqi narrated to us, saying: al-Hakim Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Allah al-Hafiz narrated to us, saying: Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Ibrahim, the jurist, the usuli, the theologian, the foremost in these sciences, Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini, the ascetic, he departed from Iraq after residing there, and the people of knowledge in Iraq and Khurasan acknowledged his precedence and virtue. He heard in Khurasan from the shaykh Abu Bakr.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is a biography of Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini, introduced through an isnad from al-Bayhaqi to al-Hakim al-Naysaburi. It describes him as a jurist (faqih), a scholar of usul (usuli), a theologian (mutakallim), and the foremost in these sciences. He was an ascetic (zahid). He had resided in Iraq but then departed after acknowledgment from scholars of Iraq and Khurasan of his precedence and virtue. He chose his homeland initially but later went to Nishapur, where he built a school that was unparalleled in its excellence. He taught and narrated hadith there. The passage ends mid-sentence, mentioning that he heard in Khurasan from the shaykh Abu Bakr (likely Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili or similar, but the text is incomplete).

The Life and Works of Abu Hazim al-Abdawi
Biography of Abu Hazim al-Abdawi with details of his scholarship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the biography and scholarly work of the hadith memorizer Abu Hazim al-Abdawi, including his travels, teachers, students, and death date.

Core Idea
Abu Hazim al-Abdawi wrote ten thousand parts of hadith from ten teachers.

Ibn Asakir presents a brief biography of the hadith scholar Abu Hazim al-Abdawi, highlighting his travels to major centers of learning, his vast output in writing hadith, and the scholars who transmitted from him. This account includes a remarkable claim about his writing productivity. Let's explore his life and legacy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get a sense of the narrative flow. Note the mention of travels, teachers, and the claim about writing ten thousand parts.
The passage includes two reports about his death; compare them.
2
Identify key achievements
List Abu Hazim's travels (Nishapur, Herat, Baghdad), teachers he narrated from, students who heard from him, and his personal statement about his written output.
He claimed to have written ten thousand parts from ten teachers, each a thousand parts.
3
Examine the death reports
Two different dates are mentioned: one report says he died on Eid al-Fitr 417 AH, another says on the 2nd of Shawwal 417 AH. Note the consistency (same year) and the slight difference in day.
Both reports agree on the year 417 AH.
4
Consider the significance
Reflect on why Ibn Asakir included this biography. It demonstrates the vast scale of hadith transmission and the dedication of scholars like Abu Hazim.

أهل نيسابور وهراة وغيرهما وقدم بغداد قديماً وحدث بها فسمع منه أبو إسحق الطبرى المقرى ومحمد بن أبى الفوارس وأحمد بن محمد الأبنوسي، وأبو عبد الله بن الكاتب في آخرين ، وحدثنا عنه التنوخي وأبو يعلى أحمد بن عبد الواحد وبقى أبو حازم حياً حتى لقيته بنيسابور وكتبت عنه الكثير ، وكان ثقة صادقاً عارفاً حافظاً يسمع الناس بافادته ويكتبون بانتخابه • كتب إلى أبو على الحسن بن على الوخشى من نيسابور يذكر أن • أبا حازم مات في يوم عيد الفطر من سنة سبع عشرة وأربعمائة كتب إلى الشيخ أبو الحسن عبد الغافر ابن إسماعيل بن عبد الغافر الفارسي قال : عمر بن أحمد بن إبراهيم بن عبدويه ثم ساق نسبه كما تقدم وقال سمعت الشيخ أبا صالح أحمد بن عبد الملك يقول سمعت أبا حازم يقول كتبت بخطى عن عشرة من شيوخي عشرة آلاف جزء عن كل شيخ ألف جزء سوى ما أشتريته فذكر منهم الإمام أبا بكر الإسماعيلي وأبا الحسن الحجاجي الحافظ والحاكم أبا أحمد الحافظ قال عبد الغافر انتخب عليه الحاكم أبو عبد الله وحدث عنه وانتشرت فوائده في الآفاق وتوفي فجأة ليلة الأربعاء الثانى من شوال سنة سبع عشرة وأربعمائة وصلى عليه الأستاذ الإمام الاسفرايني رحمه الله
The people of Nishapur, Herat, and other places, and he (Abu Hazim) came to Baghdad long ago and narrated hadith there. Abu Ishaq al-Tabari al-Muqri', Muhammad ibn Abi al-Fawaris, Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Abnusi, and Abu Abdullah ibn al-Katib among others heard from him. Al-Tanukhi and Abu Ya'la Ahmad ibn Abd al-Wahid narrated from us about him. Abu Hazim remained alive until I met him in Nishapur and wrote a great deal from him. He was trustworthy, truthful, knowledgeable, a memorizer (hafiz); people would listen to his dictation and write from his selection (intikhab). Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Ali al-Wakhshi wrote to me from Nishapur mentioning that Abu Hazim died on the day of Eid al-Fitr in the year 417 AH. The Sheikh Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Ghafir ibn Isma'il ibn Abd al-Ghafir al-Farisi wrote to me saying: 'Umar ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Abdawayh — then he traced his lineage as mentioned earlier — and he said: I heard Sheikh Abu Salih Ahmad ibn Abd al-Malik say: I heard Abu Hazim say: I wrote with my own hand from ten of my teachers ten thousand parts (juz'), from each teacher a thousand parts, apart from what I purchased. He mentioned among them: Imam Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili, Abu al-Hasan al-Hajjaji al-Hafiz, and al-Hakim Abu Ahmad al-Hafiz. Abd al-Ghafir said: Al-Hakim Abu Abdullah selected (intakhaba) from him and narrated from him, and his benefits (fawa'id) spread throughout the horizons. He died suddenly on the night of Wednesday, the second of Shawwal, year 417 AH. The master Imam al-Isfarayini, may Allah have mercy on him, prayed over him.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is a biography of the hadith scholar Abu Hazim al-Abdawi. It begins by mentioning his travels to Nishapur, Herat, and Baghdad, and lists several scholars who heard from him. The author (Ibn Asakir) notes that he met Abu Hazim in Nishapur and wrote much from him, praising him as trustworthy and a hafiz. A letter from Abu Ali al-Wakhshi reports his death on Eid al-Fitr 417 AH. Then a second report from Abd al-Ghafir al-Farisi gives a fuller account: Abu Hazim claimed to have written ten thousand parts (juz') from ten teachers, each teacher a thousand parts, not counting what he purchased. He named three teachers: Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili, Abu al-Hasan al-Hajjaji, and al-Hakim Abu Ahmad. The passage concludes with his death date (2 Shawwal 417 AH) and that al-Isfarayini led his funeral prayer. This biography highlights Abu Hazim's massive output and his role as a transmitter of hadith.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Abu Hazim wrote hadith from every scholar he encountered.
Correction: His statement clarifies he wrote from ten specific teachers, each a thousand parts, totaling ten thousand parts. He did not claim to write from all scholars.

كتب إلى الشيخ أبو نصر عبد الرحيم بن عبد الكريم بن هوازن قال أنا أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين البيهقى قال أنا الحاكم أبو عبد الله محمد بن الله الحافظ قال : إبراهيم بن محمد بن إبراهيم الفقيه الأصولي المتكلم المقدم في هذه العلوم أبو إسحق الاسفراينى الزاهد انصرف من العراق بعد المقام بها ، وقد أقر له أهل العلم بالعراق وخراسان بالتقدم والفضل فاختار الوطن إلى أن خرج بعد الجهد إلى نيسابور وبنى له المدرسة التي لم يبن بنيسابور قبلها مثلها ، ودرس فيها وحدث ، سمع بخراسان الشيخ أبا بكر الإسماعيلى وأقرانه وبالعراق أبا بكر محمد بن عبد الله الشافعي وأبا محمد دعلج بن أحمد السجزى وأقرانهما أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم إسماعيل بن أحمد ، قال ثنا الشيخ الإمام أبو إسحق إبراهيم بن على بن يوسف الفيروز اباذي من لفظه قال : أبو إسحق إبراهيم بن محمد الاسفراينى وكان فقيهاً متكلماً أصولياً وعليه درس شيخنا القاضى أبو الطيب أصول الفقه باسفراين وعنه أخذ الكلام والأصول عامة شيوخ نيسابور . أحد الإمامة كتب إلى الشيخ أبو الحسن عبد الغافر بن إسماعيل الفارسي قال : إبراهيم بن محمد بن إبراهيم بن مهران الأستاذ الإمام أبو إسحق الاسفرايني من بلغ حد الاجتهاد من العلماء لتبحره فى العلوم واستجماعه شرائط من العربية والفقه والكلام والأصول ومعرفة الكتاب والسنة ، وكان من المجتهدين في العبادة المبالغين في الورع والتحرج ذكره الحاكم في التاريخ لعلو منزلته وكمال فضله وذكر أنه حمل إلى نيسابور استدعاء واكراها للاحتجاج إليه وانتخب عليه الحاكم أبو عبد الله عشرة أجزاء ، وقال أبو صالح المؤذن سمعت أبا حازم العبدوى الحافظ يقول كان الإمام يقول لى . بعد ما رجع من اسفراين أشتهي أن يكون موتى بنيسابور حتى يصلى على جمع نيسابور فتوفى بعد هذا الكلام بنحو من خمسة أشهر يوم عاشوراء سنة ثمان عشرة وأربعمائة وصلى عليه الإمام الموفق ، وحكى له من أثق به. أن الصاحب ابن عباد كان إذا انتهى إلى ذكر الباقلاني وابن فورك والاسفراينى وكانوا متعاصرين من أصحاب الاشعرى قال لأصحابه ابن الباقلاني بحر مغرق وابن فورك صل مطرق والاسفراینی نار تحرق ، وكان روح القدس نفث فى روعه حيث أخبر عن حال هؤلاء الثلاثة بما هو الحال فيهم وفوائد هذا الإمام وفضائله وأحاديثه وتصانيفه أكثر وأشهر من أن تستوعب فى مجلدات فضلا عن أطباق وأوراق.
The Sheikh Abu Nasr Abd al-Rahim ibn Abd al-Karim ibn Hawazan wrote to me, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Bayhaqi informed us, saying: Al-Hakim Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Allah al-Hafiz informed us, saying: Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Ibrahim, the jurist, the usuli, the mutakallim, the foremost in these sciences, Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini, the ascetic, departed from Iraq after residing there. The people of knowledge in Iraq and Khurasan acknowledged his precedence and virtue. He chose his homeland until, after effort, he went out to Nishapur, and a school (madrasa) was built for him, the like of which had not been built in Nishapur before. He taught and narrated hadith there. He heard in Khurasan from Sheikh Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili and his peers, and in Iraq from Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Shafi'i and Abu Muhammad Da'laj ibn Ahmad al-Sijzi and their peers. The Sheikh Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Ahmad informed us, saying: The Imam Sheikh Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Ali ibn Yusuf al-Firuzabadi narrated to us from his dictation, saying: Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Muhammad al-Isfarayini was a jurist, mutakallim, and usuli, and our teacher the Qadi Abu al-Tayyib studied usul al-fiqh under him in Isfarayin, and from him the general body of scholars of Nishapur took kalam and usul. One of the Imams. The Sheikh Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Ghafir ibn Isma'il al-Farisi wrote to me, saying: Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Ibrahim ibn Mihran, the master Imam Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini, reached the level of ijtihad among scholars due to his deep knowledge in the sciences and his fulfillment of the conditions in Arabic, fiqh, kalam, usul, and knowledge of the Book and Sunnah. He was among the diligent in worship, extreme in abstinence and cautiousness. Al-Hakim mentioned him in the history (book) for his high station and complete virtue, and mentioned that he was brought to Nishapur by request and reluctantly, out of need for him (to debate). Al-Hakim Abu Abdullah selected (intakhaba) from him ten parts. Abu Salih the mu'adhdhin said: I heard Abu Hazim al-Abdawi al-Hafiz say: The Imam used to say to me, after he returned from Isfarayin: 'I wish that my death would be in Nishapur so that the congregation of Nishapur would pray over me.' He died after this speech by about five months on the day of Ashura, year 418 AH, and al-Muwaffaq prayed over him. It was narrated to me by someone I trust that the vizier Ibn Abbad, when he came to mention al-Baqillani, Ibn Furak, and al-Isfarayini — and they were contemporaries among the followers of al-Ash'ari — said to his companions: 'Ibn al-Baqillani is a drowning sea, Ibn Furak is a hard striking rock, and al-Isfarayini is a burning fire.' And the Holy Spirit (Jibril) breathed into his heart, as he informed about the condition of these three with what is indeed their condition. The benefits, virtues, hadiths, and writings of this Imam are more numerous and famous than can be contained in volumes, let alone pages and sheets.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is a detailed biography of Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini, a prominent Ash'ari theologian and jurist. It begins with a chain of transmission from al-Bayhaqi to al-Hakim, describing al-Isfarayini as a leading jurist, usuli (scholar of legal methodology), and mutakallim (theologian), and an ascetic. After residing in Iraq, he returned to Khurasan and eventually settled in Nishapur, where a uniquely fine madrasa was built for him. His teachers included Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili in Khurasan and Abu Bakr al-Shafi'i and Da'laj in Iraq. The passage then quotes al-Firuzabadi stating that al-Isfarayini taught Qadi Abu al-Tayyib usul al-fiqh, and that most Nishapur scholars took kalam and usul from him. Abd al-Ghafir al-Farisi reports that he reached ijtihad, being a scholar of Arabic, fiqh, kalam, usul, and Qur'an and Sunnah, and was extremely devout. Al-Hakim selected ten parts from him. A death story is related: al-Isfarayini wished to die in Nishapur so its congregation would pray over him, and he died on Ashura 418 AH. Finally, a famous comparison by Ibn Abbad is quoted: al-Baqillani is a drowning sea, Ibn Furak a hard rock, and al-Isfarayini a burning fire. The passage concludes that his works and virtues are too vast to be contained in volumes. This biography highlights his status as a master theologian and the respect he commanded.

الأصول

Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini was a versatile scholar whose madrasa in Nishapur became a hub for Ash'ari learning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just read that Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini combined deep knowledge with asceticism and teaching. Which of these three—knowledge, piety, or service to others—is weakest in your life right now? What is one concrete action you will take this week to strengthen it?
?
The passage says his madrasa was unlike any before it. What kind of 'madrasa' are you building in your home, your community, or your heart? Are you investing in a legacy of learning that outlasts you, or are you content to just consume knowledge?
?
Al-Isfarayini studied under many teachers and then taught many students. Who are you currently learning from? And who are you deliberately teaching? If your answer is 'no one' for either, what is holding you back from being part of a chain of transmission?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
4 min
The Death and Legacy of Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini
Death story and comparative metaphor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the circumstances of Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini's death, his wish to be buried in Nishapur, and the famous comparison by Ibn Abbad that highlights his intellectual style.

Core Idea
Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini's death in Nishapur fulfilled his wish, and Ibn Abbad described him as a 'burning fire' for his intense debating style.

The second part of the biography narrates al-Isfarayini's longing to die in Nishapur and his actual death on Ashura 418 AH. It also recounts a vivid comparison made by the vizier Ibn Abbad, who likened al-Isfarayini to a burning fire, contrasting him with al-Baqillani (a drowning sea) and Ibn Furak (a hard rock). This metaphor captures his forceful and passionate arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the account of his wish
Notice the tradition from Abu Hazim al-Abdawi: the Imam said he wished to die in Nishapur so its congregation would pray over him.
2
Verify the fulfillment
He died about five months later on Ashura. Who prayed over him? Al-Muwaffaq.
3
Examine Ibn Abbad's comparison
The vizier described three contemporaries: al-Baqillani as a sea, Ibn Furak as a rock, and al-Isfarayini as a fire. What do these metaphors suggest?
4
Understand the spiritual insight
The text adds that 'the Holy Spirit breathed into his heart' regarding their true qualities. Reflect on this endorsement.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ibn Abbad's comparison was negative, implying al-Isfarayini was destructive.

Introduction to Abu Ali ibn Shadhan al-Baghdadi
Ibn Asakir begins a biography with a name and chain.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how classical biographers like Ibn Asakir introduce a scholar and begin a chain of transmission.

Core Idea
A biographical entry opens with the subject and the chain of narration.

This passage gives us a glimpse into the method of classical biographical writing. Ibn Asakir begins by naming the scholar, noting his late death, and then immediately provides the chain of narrators through whom he received information about him. This chain is the backbone of historical reliability.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic carefully, noting the structure: name, comment, then chain.
The passage is incomplete; the chain cuts off at 'ibn Thabit'.
2
Identify the chain
The chain includes two sheikhs who both report from Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit (likely al-Khatib al-Baghdadi).
This chain connects Ibn Asakir to the earlier scholar.
3
Reflect on the incomplete chain
The passage cuts off; consider why chains are important in Islamic historiography.
Biographies often continue with more details about the subject.

ومنهم أبو على بن شاذان البغدادى تأخرت وفاته رحمه الله أخبرنا الشيخ أبو منصور محمد بن عبد الملك المقرى وأبو الحسن على بن الحسن بن سعيد قالا قال لنا أبو بكر أحمد بن علی بن ثابت
And among them is Abu Ali ibn Shadhan al-Baghdadi, whose death was delayed (late), may Allah have mercy on him. The Sheikh Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Muqri' and Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn al-Hasan ibn Sa'id informed us, both saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit told us...

Commentary
This very brief passage introduces Abu Ali ibn Shadhan al-Baghdadi, noting that his death occurred later. It then begins a chain of transmission involving two narrators who report from Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit (likely al-Khatib al-Baghdadi). The passage is incomplete because the page ends, so we only have the beginning of this biography. It appears to be a standard biographical entry listing narrators and sources.

The Scholarly and Spiritual Stature of Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini
Ibn Asakir narrates the first part of al-Isfarayini's biography, focusing on his qualifications and piety.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the breadth of Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini's scholarly achievements and his exemplary piety as depicted by Ibn Asakir.

Core Idea
Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini combined deep ijtihad with intense worship.

This lesson introduces one of the great Ash'ari scholars of the 5th/11th century. Through Ibn Asakir's narration, we learn not only of his mastery in jurisprudence, theology, and principles but also of his deep piety and even his final wish to die in Nishapur. This biography sets the stage for understanding his influence.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening chain and introduction
Read the Arabic passage from the beginning up to the description of his ijtihad. Notice the chain of transmission and how al-Isfarayini is introduced as a jurist, theologian, and usuli.
The chain shows the authority of the narration.
2
Examine the list of sciences he mastered
The letter from al-Farsi lists the sciences: Arabic, jurisprudence, theology, principles, knowledge of Book and Sunnah. Reflect on what 'reaching ijtihad' means.
Ijtihad requires mastery of many disciplines.
3
Understand his piety and the death story
He was a mujtahid in worship, extreme in wara'. His wish to die in Nishapur shows his attachment to the community. Note that he died within five months of that wish.
This illustrates his sincerity and the respect he held.

أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم إسماعيل بن أحمد ، قال ثنا الشيخ الإمام أبو إسحق إبراهيم بن على بن يوسف الفيروز اباذي من لفظه قال : أبو إسحق إبراهيم بن محمد الاسفراينى وكان فقيهاً متكلماً أصولياً وعليه درس شيخنا القاضى أبو الطيب أصول الفقه باسفراين وعنه أخذ الكلام والأصول عامة شيوخ نيسابور .
كتب إلى الشيخ أبو الحسن عبد الغافر بن إسماعيل الفارسي قال : إبراهيم بن محمد بن إبراهيم بن مهران الأستاذ الإمام أبو إسحق الاسفرايني من بلغ حد الاجتهاد من العلماء لتبحره فى العلوم واستجماعه شرائط من العربية والفقه والكلام والأصول ومعرفة الكتاب والسنة ، وكان من المجتهدين في العبادة المبالغين في الورع والتحرج ذكره الحاكم في التاريخ لعلو منزلته وكمال فضله وذكر أنه حمل إلى نيسابور استدعاء واكراها للاحتجاج إليه وانتخب عليه الحاكم أبو عبد الله عشرة أجزاء ، وقال أبو صالح المؤذن سمعت أبا حازم العبدوى الحافظ يقول كان الإمام يقول لى . بعد ما رجع من اسفراين أشتهي أن يكون موتى بنيسابور حتى يصلى على جمع نيسابور فتوفى بعد هذا الكلام بنحو من خمسة أشهر يوم عاشوراء سنة ثمان عشرة وأربعمائة وصلى عليه الإمام الموفق ، وحكى له من أثق به. أن الصاحب ابن عباد كان إذا انتهى إلى ذكر الباقلاني وابن فورك والاسفراينى وكانوا متعاصرين من أصحاب الاشعرى قال لأصحابه ابن الباقلاني بحر مغرق وابن فورك صل مطرق والاسفراینی نار تحرق ، وكان روح القدس نفث فى روعه حيث أخبر عن حال هؤلاء الثلاثة بما هو الحال فيهم وفوائد هذا الإمام وفضائله وأحاديثه وتصانيفه أكثر وأشهر من أن تستوعب فى مجلدات فضلا عن أطباق وأوراق.
Our shaykh Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Ahmad informed us, he said: our shaykh the Imam Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Ali ibn Yusuf al-Firuzabadi narrated to us from his dictation, he said: Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Muhammad al-Isfarayini — he was a jurist, a theologian, a specialist in principles (usuli). And from him our shaykh al-Qadi Abu al-Tayyib studied principles of jurisprudence (usul al-fiqh) in Isfarayin, and from him most of the shaykhs of Nishapur took theology (kalam) and principles (usul).
The shaykh Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Ghafir ibn Isma'il al-Farsi wrote to me, saying: Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Ibrahim ibn Mahran, the master imam Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini — he reached the level of ijtihad among scholars due to his deep knowledge of the sciences and his possession of the conditions (of ijtihad) in Arabic language, jurisprudence, theology, principles, and knowledge of the Book and the Sunnah. He was among those who strive hard in worship, who go to extremes in scrupulousness (wara') and cautious avoidance of sin (taharruj). Al-Hakim mentioned him in the History for his high station and the perfection of his virtue, and he mentioned that he was brought to Nishapur by summons and coercion out of need for him, and al-Hakim Abu Abd Allah selected ten parts (ajza') from his narrations. Abu Salih al-Mu'adhdhin said: I heard Abu Hazim al-Abdawi al-Hafiz say: The Imam used to say to me, after he returned from Isfarayin: 'I desire that my death be in Nishapur so that the congregation of Nishapur may pray over me.' He died about five months after this speech on the day of Ashura in the year 418 AH, and al-Imam al-Muwaffaq prayed over him. A trustworthy person related to me that al-Sahib ibn Abbad, when he came to mention al-Baqillani, Ibn Furak, and al-Isfarayini — and they were contemporaries among the followers of al-Ash'ari — said to his companions: 'Ibn al-Baqillani is a deep sea, Ibn Furak is a file that abrades, and al-Isfarayini is a fire that burns.' And it was as if the Holy Spirit breathed into his heart, for he informed about the state of these three as it actually was. The benefits of this Imam, his virtues, his hadiths, and his works are too many and too famous to be contained in volumes, let alone in quires and sheets.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini, a prominent Ash'ari theologian and jurist. It begins with a chain of transmission: the author heard from Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Ahmad, who heard from al-Firuzabadi, who describes al-Isfarayini as a jurist, theologian, and specialist in principles. It then quotes a letter from Abd al-Ghafir al-Farsi, who praises al-Isfarayini as reaching the level of ijtihad due to his mastery of various sciences, including Arabic, jurisprudence, theology, principles, and knowledge of Quran and Sunnah. His piety and asceticism are highlighted. Al-Hakim al-Naysaburi mentioned him in his history, noting that he was brought to Nishapur under duress because of the need for his knowledge, and al-Hakim selected ten juz' from him. A story follows about his wish to die in Nishapur so that its people would pray over him; he died five months later on Ashura 418 AH. Then a key anecdote: the vizier al-Sahib ibn Abbad, when comparing three contemporary Ash'ari scholars—al-Baqillani, Ibn Furak, and al-Isfarayini—described al-Baqillani as a deep sea (vast knowledge), Ibn Furak as a file that abrades (sharp critic), and al-Isfarayini as a fire that burns (forceful debater). The author affirms that this characterization was accurate. The passage concludes by stating that al-Isfarayini's merits and works are too extensive to be fully recorded even in volumes.

Key Terms
إسفراييني
اجتهاد
ورع
أصول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think his forced relocation to Nishapur was due to some fault or weakness on his part.
Correction: The passage states he was brought 'out of need for him' (للاحتجاج إليه), meaning his knowledge was so valuable that they compelled him to come; it reflects his high station, not any deficiency.

Checkpoint
What event occurred about five months after al-Isfarayini expressed his wish to die in Nishapur?
A) He moved to another city
B) He died on Ashura 418 AH
C) He became a teacher in Isfarayin
D) He led a public debate

Key Takeaway
Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini was a scholar of ijtihad, a master of multiple sciences, and a deeply pious man who wished to die among the people of Nishapur.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have read that al-Isfarayini was extreme in wara' and taharruj. In what area of your life are you still making excuses for what you know is wrong? What one step can you take today to increase your scrupulousness?
?
The imam wished to die in Nishapur so that the righteous people would pray over him. Do you truly desire to be in the company of the righteous, or do you avoid their gatherings because it exposes your shortcomings? How will you change that starting today?
?
Al-Isfarayini mastered multiple sciences and was a mujtahid, yet his piety was not separate from his scholarship. In your pursuit of knowledge, have you neglected the heart? What concrete action will you take this week to combine learning with worship?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir

Al-Isfarayini as a Burning Fire: A Scholar's Legacy
Ibn Asakir records al-Sahib ibn Abbad's famous comparison of al-Baqillani, Ibn Furak, and al-Isfarayini.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will appreciate the distinctive characterization of al-Isfarayini by al-Sahib ibn Abbad and understand why his scholarly impact was likened to a burning fire.

Core Idea
Al-Isfarayini's scholarship was forceful and impactful, like a fire that burns.

In this lesson, we examine a famous anecdote where the vizier al-Sahib ibn Abbad compares three contemporary Ash'ari scholars: al-Baqillani, Ibn Furak, and al-Isfarayini. Each is given a unique metaphor that captures his style. Al-Isfarayini is called a 'fire that burns,' reflecting his intense and penetrating scholarship. The passage ends by noting that his merits are too numerous to fully document.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage of the comparison
Read the Arabic from 'وحكى له من أثق به' to the end. Notice the chain and the direct quote from al-Sahib ibn Abbad.
The narrator is trustworthy but unnamed.
2
Analyze each metaphor
Al-Baqillani is a deep sea (vast knowledge), Ibn Furak is a file that abrades (sharp critic), and al-Isfarayini is a fire that burns (forceful debater). Consider what each says about their scholarly style.
The metaphors are vivid and memorable.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
The author says al-Isfarayini's works are too many to contain in volumes. This emphasizes his prolific output and lasting legacy.
The passage ends with a praise of his extensive contributions.

?
