The Scholarly Reputation of Abu Ali ibn Shadhan
Ibn Asakir presents personal and scholarly details along with praise for Ibn Shadhan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Abu Ali ibn Shadhan's credentials as a trustworthy hadith scholar and Ash'ari theologian based on the biographical entry by Ibn Asakir.

Core Idea
Ibn Shadhan was a trustworthy hadith scholar and Ash'ari theologian praised by peers.

This lesson examines the first part of Ibn Asakir's biography of Abu Ali ibn Shadhan, focusing on his birth, his scholarly description, and the testimonials of his trustworthiness. The passage establishes his reliability as a narrator and his adherence to the Ash'ari school of theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical details
Read the Arabic passage and translation, noting the full name, birth date, and the chain of transmission by which this biography is reported.
The chain shows the scholarly rigor in preserving biographies.
2
Identify how he is described
Look for the terms 'saduq' and 'sahih al-kitab', and note that he understood kalam according to the Ash'ari school.
These terms indicate his reliability and theological leaning.
3
Review the list of scholars
Notice the names of scholars who wrote from him, including well-known figures like al-Barqani and al-Khallal.
This list shows his acceptance among leading hadith scholars.
4
Examine the testimonials
Read the statements of Ibn Rizqawayh and al-Azhari, who explicitly declare his trustworthiness and preference for his narrations.
These testimonials reinforce his reliability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم أبو على بن شاذان البغدادى تأخرت وفاته رحمه الله أخبرنا الشيخ أبو منصور محمد بن عبد الملك المقرى وأبو الحسن على بن الحسن بن سعيد قالا قال لنا أبو بكر أحمد بن علی بن ثابت الحافظ : الحسن بن أحمد بن إبراهيم بن الحسن بن محمد بن حرب بن مهران أبو على البزاز ولد فى ليلة الخميس لاثنتى عشرة ليلة خلت من شهر ربيع الأول سنة تسع وثلاثين وثلاثماية كذلك قرأت بخط بن أحمد الدقاق وأحمد بن سليمان العباداني وأحمد ابن سليمان النجاد وخلقاً غيرهم يطول ذكرهم كتبنا عنه وكان صدوقا صحيح الكتاب وكان يفهم الكلام علي مذهب الأشعرى وكتب عنه جماعة من شيوخنا كأبي بكر البرقاني ومحمد بن طلحة وأبي محمد الخلال وأبى القسم الأزهرى وعبد العزيز الأزجي وغيرهم ، سمعت أبا الحسن بن رزقويه يقول أبو على بن شاذان ثقة وسمعت الأزهرى يقول أبو علی ابن شاذان من أوثق من برأ الله في الحديث وسماعي منه أحب إلى من السماع من غيره أو كما قال : وقال أبو بكر الخطيب حدثني محمد بن يحيى الكرماني قال كنا يوماً بحضرة أبى على بن شاذان فدخل علينا رجل شاب لا يعرفه منا أحد فسلم ثم قال أيكم أبو على بن شاذان فأشرنا له إليه، فقال له أيها الشيخ رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في المنام فقال لى سل عن أبي على بن شاذان فإذا لقيته فأقرئه منى السلام ، ثم أنصرف الشاب فيكي أبو على وقال ما أعرف لى عملاً أستحق به هذا اللهم إلا أن يكون صبرى على قراءة الحديث وتكرير الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كلما جاء ذكره ، قال الكرماني ولم يلبث أبو على بعد ذلك ألا شهرين أو ثلاثة حتى مات ، قال أبو بكر توفى ابن شاذان في ليلة السبت مستهل المحرم من سنة ست وعشرين وأربعماية بعد صلاة العتمة ودفن من الغد وحضرت الصلاة على جنازته قلت وكان حنيفي الفروع
And among them is Abu Ali ibn Shadhan al-Baghdadi, his death occurred later, may Allah have mercy on him. Our shaykh Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Muqri' and Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn al-Hasan ibn Sa'id informed us, they said: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Hafiz narrated to us: al-Hasan ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn Harb ibn Mahran, Abu Ali al-Bazzaz was born on the night of Thursday, the twelfth night remaining from the month of Rabi' al-Awwal in the year 339 AH. Likewise I read in the handwriting of Ibn Ahmad al-Daqqaq, and Ahmad ibn Sulayman al-Abbadani, and Ahmad ibn Sulayman al-Najjad, and many others whose mention would be lengthy. We wrote from him, and he was truthful (saduq), correct in his book (sahih al-kitab), and he understood theology (kalam) according to the school of al-Ash'ari. A group of our shaykhs wrote from him, such as Abu Bakr al-Barqani, Muhammad ibn Talha, Abu Muhammad al-Khallal, Abu al-Qasim al-Azhari, Abd al-Aziz al-Azaji, and others. I heard Abu al-Hasan ibn Rizqawayh say: Abu Ali ibn Shadhan is trustworthy (thiqa). And I heard al-Azhari say: Abu Ali ibn Shadhan is among the most trustworthy of those created by Allah in hadith, and my hearing from him is more beloved to me than hearing from others — or as he said. And Abu Bakr al-Khatib said: Muhammad ibn Yahya al-Karmani narrated to me, he said: One day we were in the presence of Abu Ali ibn Shadhan when a young man entered upon us whom none of us knew. He greeted and then said: 'Which of you is Abu Ali ibn Shadhan?' We pointed to him. He said to him: 'O shaykh, I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) in a dream, and he said to me: Ask about Abu Ali ibn Shadhan, and if you meet him, convey my greeting to him.' Then the young man left. Abu Ali wept and said: 'I do not know of any deed by which I deserve this, except that it may be my patience in reading hadith and repeating blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) every time he is mentioned.' Al-Karmani said: Abu Ali did not remain after that except two or three months until he died. Abu Bakr said: Ibn Shadhan died on the night of Saturday, the beginning of Muharram in the year 426 AH, after the night prayer, and was buried the next day. I attended the prayer over his funeral. He (the author) said: He was Hanafi in branches (furu').
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Abu Ali ibn Shadhan, a notable hadith scholar and Ash'ari theologian. It begins with a chain of transmission: from the author through two shaykhs, to al-Khatib al-Baghdadi (Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit), who gives the biography. Ibn Shadhan's full name and birth date (339 AH) are given. He is described as 'saduq' (truthful) and 'sahih al-kitab' (having a correct book), and he understood kalam according to the Ash'ari school. A list of scholars who wrote from him is provided, including well-known figures. Two testimonials emphasize his trustworthiness: Ibn Rizqawayh calls him 'thiqa', and al-Azhari says he is among the most trustworthy in hadith, preferring his narration over others. Then a striking anecdote is narrated by al-Karmani: a young man came to Ibn Shadhan and reported a dream in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) asked about Ibn Shadhan and sent his greeting. Ibn Shadhan wept humbly, attributing this honor possibly to his patience in teaching hadith and his constant prayer upon the Prophet. He died shortly after, in 426 AH. The author notes that Ibn Shadhan was Hanafi in furu' (positive law), indicating his madhhab in jurisprudence.

ابن شاذان
صدوق
ثقة
أشعري

A) Ash'ari

D) Shafi'i

Key Takeaway
Abu Ali ibn Shadhan was a trustworthy hadith scholar and Ash'ari theologian, praised by contemporary scholars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Azhari said that hearing from Ibn Shadhan was more beloved to him than hearing from others. Is there anyone in your life whose company you cherish because of their integrity? What can you do today to become the kind of person others desire to be around?
?
Ibn Shadhan was described as 'truthful' and 'most trustworthy'. If your closest companions were asked to describe your character in one word, what would they say? What step can you take this week to align your reputation with what pleases Allah?

A Dream of the Prophet's Greeting
Ibn Asakir narrates a dream story and Ibn Shadhan's death with his madhhab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of a dream in which the Prophet Muhammad sent greetings to Abu Ali ibn Shadhan and how Ibn Shadhan humbly interpreted this honor.

Core Idea
A dream showed the Prophet honoring Ibn Shadhan, who attributed it to his devotion to hadith.

This second lesson covers a remarkable dream story from the biography of Ibn Shadhan, in which a young man saw the Prophet in a dream and was instructed to convey greetings to Ibn Shadhan. Ibn Shadhan's humble reaction and his subsequent death are also recounted, along with a note on his legal madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Read the dream narrative
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully, following the story: the young man's arrival, the dream report, and the Prophet's greeting.
Notice the detailed chain of transmission for this story.
2
Observe Ibn Shadhan's reaction
Ibn Shadhan wept and humbly expressed that he did not know of any deed deserving this except his patience in reading hadith and sending blessings on the Prophet.
This shows his humility and devotion.
3
Learn about his death
The passage notes that he died two to three months after the dream, and provides the exact date and burial details.
The timing adds a spiritual dimension.
4
Note his madhhab in furu'
The author concludes by stating that Ibn Shadhan was Hanafi in branches (furu'), despite his Ash'ari theology.
This shows the compatibility of Ash'ari theology with Hanafi jurisprudence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم أبو على بن شاذان البغدادى تأخرت وفاته رحمه الله أخبرنا الشيخ أبو منصور محمد بن عبد الملك المقرى وأبو الحسن على بن الحسن بن سعيد قالا قال لنا أبو بكر أحمد بن علی بن ثابت الحافظ : الحسن بن أحمد بن إبراهيم بن الحسن بن محمد بن حرب بن مهران أبو على البزاز ولد فى ليلة الخميس لاثنتى عشرة ليلة خلت من شهر ربيع الأول سنة تسع وثلاثين وثلاثماية كذلك قرأت بخط بن أحمد الدقاق وأحمد بن سليمان العباداني وأحمد ابن سليمان النجاد وخلقاً غيرهم يطول ذكرهم كتبنا عنه وكان صدوقا صحيح الكتاب وكان يفهم الكلام علي مذهب الأشعرى وكتب عنه جماعة من شيوخنا كأبي بكر البرقاني ومحمد بن طلحة وأبي محمد الخلال وأبى القسم الأزهرى وعبد العزيز الأزجي وغيرهم ، سمعت أبا الحسن بن رزقويه يقول أبو على بن شاذان ثقة وسمعت الأزهرى يقول أبو علی ابن شاذان من أوثق من برأ الله في الحديث وسماعي منه أحب إلى من السماع من غيره أو كما قال : وقال أبو بكر الخطيب حدثني محمد بن يحيى الكرماني قال كنا يوماً بحضرة أبى على بن شاذان فدخل علينا رجل شاب لا يعرفه منا أحد فسلم ثم قال أيكم أبو على بن شاذان فأشرنا له إليه، فقال له أيها الشيخ رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في المنام فقال لى سل عن أبي على بن شاذان فإذا لقيته فأقرئه منى السلام ، ثم أنصرف الشاب فيكي أبو على وقال ما أعرف لى عملاً أستحق به هذا اللهم إلا أن يكون صبرى على قراءة الحديث وتكرير الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كلما جاء ذكره ، قال الكرماني ولم يلبث أبو على بعد ذلك ألا شهرين أو ثلاثة حتى مات ، قال أبو بكر توفى ابن شاذان في ليلة السبت مستهل المحرم من سنة ست وعشرين وأربعماية بعد صلاة العتمة ودفن من الغد وحضرت الصلاة على جنازته قلت وكان حنيفي الفروع
And among them is Abu Ali ibn Shadhan al-Baghdadi, his death occurred later, may Allah have mercy on him. Our shaykh Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Muqri' and Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn al-Hasan ibn Sa'id informed us, they said: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Hafiz narrated to us: al-Hasan ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn Harb ibn Mahran, Abu Ali al-Bazzaz was born on the night of Thursday, the twelfth night remaining from the month of Rabi' al-Awwal in the year 339 AH. Likewise I read in the handwriting of Ibn Ahmad al-Daqqaq, and Ahmad ibn Sulayman al-Abbadani, and Ahmad ibn Sulayman al-Najjad, and many others whose mention would be lengthy. We wrote from him, and he was truthful (saduq), correct in his book (sahih al-kitab), and he understood theology (kalam) according to the school of al-Ash'ari. A group of our shaykhs wrote from him, such as Abu Bakr al-Barqani, Muhammad ibn Talha, Abu Muhammad al-Khallal, Abu al-Qasim al-Azhari, Abd al-Aziz al-Azaji, and others. I heard Abu al-Hasan ibn Rizqawayh say: Abu Ali ibn Shadhan is trustworthy (thiqa). And I heard al-Azhari say: Abu Ali ibn Shadhan is among the most trustworthy of those created by Allah in hadith, and my hearing from him is more beloved to me than hearing from others — or as he said. And Abu Bakr al-Khatib said: Muhammad ibn Yahya al-Karmani narrated to me, he said: One day we were in the presence of Abu Ali ibn Shadhan when a young man entered upon us whom none of us knew. He greeted and then said: 'Which of you is Abu Ali ibn Shadhan?' We pointed to him. He said to him: 'O shaykh, I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) in a dream, and he said to me: Ask about Abu Ali ibn Shadhan, and if you meet him, convey my greeting to him.' Then the young man left. Abu Ali wept and said: 'I do not know of any deed by which I deserve this, except that it may be my patience in reading hadith and repeating blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) every time he is mentioned.' Al-Karmani said: Abu Ali did not remain after that except two or three months until he died. Abu Bakr said: Ibn Shadhan died on the night of Saturday, the beginning of Muharram in the year 426 AH, after the night prayer, and was buried the next day. I attended the prayer over his funeral. He (the author) said: He was Hanafi in branches (furu').
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Abu Ali ibn Shadhan, a notable hadith scholar and Ash'ari theologian. It begins with a chain of transmission: from the author through two shaykhs, to al-Khatib al-Baghdadi (Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit), who gives the biography. Ibn Shadhan's full name and birth date (339 AH) are given. He is described as 'saduq' (truthful) and 'sahih al-kitab' (having a correct book), and he understood kalam according to the Ash'ari school. A list of scholars who wrote from him is provided, including well-known figures. Two testimonials emphasize his trustworthiness: Ibn Rizqawayh calls him 'thiqa', and al-Azhari says he is among the most trustworthy in hadith, preferring his narration over others. Then a striking anecdote is narrated by al-Karmani: a young man came to Ibn Shadhan and reported a dream in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) asked about Ibn Shadhan and sent his greeting. Ibn Shadhan wept humbly, attributing this honor possibly to his patience in teaching hadith and his constant prayer upon the Prophet. He died shortly after, in 426 AH. The author notes that Ibn Shadhan was Hanafi in furu' (positive law), indicating his madhhab in jurisprudence.

Key Terms

أشعري
حنيفي
فروع

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the dream proves Ibn Shadhan's infallibility or absoluteness in every aspect.
Correction: The passage shows Ibn Shadhan himself did not consider it a proof of perfection; he attributed it to his patience in hadith study and blessings on the Prophet, not to any innate sinlessness.

C) Study hadith with him

Key Takeaway
Ibn Shadhan was honored by a dream in which the Prophet sent him greetings, which he humbly attributed to his dedication to hadith and blessings on the Prophet.

?
Ibn Shadhan wept in humility when he heard the Prophet's greeting. When is the last time you felt genuinely unworthy of a blessing you received? How can you cultivate that humility starting today?
?
He attributed the greeting to patience in reading hadith and sending blessings. What is one concrete change you will make this week to consistently recite salawat when you hear the Prophet's name?

Biography of Abu Nu'aym al-Isfahani
Ibn 'Asakir narrates the biography and karama of Abu Nu'aym.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life, scholarly achievements, and the miraculous protection (karama) of Abu Nu'aym al-Isfahani as narrated by Ibn 'Asakir.

Core Idea
Abu Nu'aym's life shows how divine favor protects the righteous from harm.

Ibn 'Asakir presents a concise biography of the great hadith scholar Abu Nu'aym al-Isfahani, highlighting his virtues, famous works, and a remarkable event demonstrating his karama. This passage offers both historical information and a lesson in how Allah safeguards His saints.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the translation to grasp the full biography.
Pay attention to the sequence of information: identity, works, death, praise, and the story.
2
Identify scholarly achievements
Note the titles and works mentioned. What does it mean that he was 'unique in his time'?
Hilyat al-Awliya' and Tabaqat al-Asfiya' are among his most famous works.
3
Analyze the praise from al-Khatib
Consider the statement from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi. What does it tell us about Abu Nu'aym's status?
Al-Khatib was a major hadith scholar himself, so his praise is significant.
4
Understand the karama story
Examine the incident with Sultan Mahmud. Why was Abu Nu'aym spared? How does this illustrate karama?
The people's prevention of Abu Nu'aym from sitting in the mosque turned out to be a blessing.
5
Reflect on the overall lesson
Think about how this biography serves as both historical record and spiritual lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يوسف البناء الصوفى الشيخ الإمام أبو نعيم الحافظ، واحد عصره في فضله وجمعه ومعرفته صنف التصانيف المشهورة مثل حلية الأولياء وطبقة الاصفياء وغير ذلك من الكتب الكثيرة في أنواع علوم الحديث والحقائق، وشاع ذكره في الآفاق واستفاد الناس من تصانيفه لحسنها توفى باصبهان في صفر سنة ثلاثين وأربعمائة وبلغنى أنه ولد في رجب سنة ست وثلاثين وثلاثماية، وأنه توفى يوم الاثنين الحادى والعشرين من المحرم سنة ثلاثين ودفن من يومه بعد صلاة الظهر وبلغ أربعاً وتسعين سنة، سمعت من يحكي عن أبي بكر أحمد بن على بن ثابت الخطيب قال لم ألق من شيوخي أحفظ من أبي نعيم الحافظ وأبي حازم العبدوى الأعرج، وذكر لى الشيخ أبو عبد الله محمد بن محمد الأصبهاني عمن أدرك من شيوخ أصبهان أن السلطان محمود بن سكتكين لما استولى على أصبهان ولى عليها والياً من قبله ورحل عنها فوثب أهل أصبهان به فقتلوه فرجع محمود إليها وأمنهم حتى أطمأنوا ثم قصدهم يوم الجمعة في الجامع فقتل منهم مقتلة عظيمة، وكانوا قبل ذلك قد منعوا أبا نعيم الحافظ من الجلوس في الجامع فسلم مما جرى عليهم وكان يعد ذلك من كرامة أبي نعيم رحمه الله.
Yusuf al-Banna' al-Sufi, the Shaykh, the Imam, Abu Nu'aym al-Hafiz, the unique one of his time in his virtue, collection, and knowledge. He authored the famous works such as Hilyat al-Awliya' and Tabaqat al-Asfiya' and other numerous books in the various types of hadith sciences and realities. His fame spread in the horizons, and people benefited from his works due to their beauty. He died in Isfahan in Safar of the year 430 AH. It reached me that he was born in Rajab of the year 336 AH, and that he died on Monday, the twenty-first of Muharram of the year 430 AH, and was buried on the same day after Dhuhr prayer, having reached ninety-four years. I heard someone relating from Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Khatib who said: 'I did not meet among my teachers anyone with more memorization than Abu Nu'aym al-Hafiz and Abu Hazim al-'Abdawi al-A'raj.' And Shaykh Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Isfahani mentioned to me, from those he met among the teachers of Isfahan, that when Sultan Mahmud ibn Sebuktegin took control of Isfahan, he appointed a governor over it from his side and then left. The people of Isfahan revolted against him and killed him. Mahmud returned to them and granted them safety until they were reassured; then he attacked them on Friday in the mosque and inflicted a great massacre among them. Before that, they had prevented Abu Nu'aym al-Hafiz from sitting in the mosque, so he was saved from what befell them, and that was considered a miracle (karama) of Abu Nu'aym, may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for the renowned hadith scholar Abu Nu'aym al-Isfahani. It begins by identifying him fully: Yusuf al-Banna' al-Sufi, the Shaykh, the Imam, Abu Nu'aym al-Hafiz. He is described as unique in his time for his virtue, his comprehensive knowledge, and his authored works, among which are the famous Hilyat al-Awliya' and Tabaqat al-Asfiya', along with many other books covering various fields of hadith sciences and spiritual realities. The author notes that Abu Nu'aym's fame spread far and wide, and people benefited from his works due to their excellence. The death date is given as Safar 430 AH, and the author (Ibn 'Asakir) mentions that he was informed that Abu Nu'aym was born in Rajab 336 AH and died on Monday, 21 Muharram 430 AH, was buried the same day after Dhuhr, aged 94. The passage then cites a statement from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, who praised Abu Nu'aym and another scholar as the most memorizers among his teachers. Finally, a story is recounted illustrating Abu Nu'aym's karama (divine favor): when Sultan Mahmud of Ghazni massacred the people of Isfahan after a revolt, Abu Nu'aym was spared because the people had previously prevented him from sitting in the mosque, so he was not present during the massacre. This was considered a miraculous sign of his sanctity.

حلية الأولياء
كرامة
الحافظ

The Life of Abu Hamid al-Istawa'i
Biographical entry from Ibn 'Asakir's work

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and scholarly profile of Abu Hamid al-Istawa'i, a Shafi'i-Ash'ari judge and traditionist as recorded by Ibn 'Asakir.

Core Idea
A single biography reveals a scholar's lineage, teachers, school, and death.

Ibn 'Asakir continues his biographical dictionary with the entry of Abu Hamid al-Istawa'i. This passage, transmitted from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, provides a concise yet rich account of his origins, education, career, and theological orientation. As you read, notice how the biography serves both as a record of his life and as a witness to the Ash'ari presence in Baghdad.

Guided Path
1
Read the full biography
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then read the translation. Pay attention to the chain of transmission and the details about his life.
The passage is transmitted via two chains from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi.
2
Trace his scholarly lineage
Identify the teachers he heard from in Nishapur and in Baghdad. Notice that he heard from al-Daraqutni, a major hadith scholar.
3
Identify his two schools
The text explicitly states his fiqh and usul affiliations. Find that sentence and note the significance of being both Shafi'i and Ash'ari.
This shows the Ash'ari school was established among Shafi'i jurists.
4
Note his judgeship and death
He was appointed judge of 'Ukbara by Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani. His death date and burial place are recorded. Consider why such details are preserved.
The precise date and location highlight the importance of biographical continuity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم أبو حامد أحمد بن محمد بن أحمد بن محمد بن دلويه الاستوائي الدلوى، قال لنا أبو الحسن أحمد بن على بن قبيس الغساني وأبو منصور عبد الرحمن بن محمد بن زريق الشيباني قالا قال لنا أبو بكر أحمد بن على بن ثابت الخطيب فى تاريخ بغداد: أحمد بن محمد بن أحمد بن دلويه أبو حامد الاستوائي، ويعرف بالدلوى، واستوى التي نسب إليها قرية من قرى نيسابور، وسمع أبا أحمد محمد بن محمد بن إسحق الحافظ، وأبا العباس أحمد بن محمد بن إسحق الأنماطئ، وأبا سعيد عبد الله بن عبد الوهاب الرازي، ومحمد بن عبد الله الجوزقى ونحوهم، وقدم بغداد فسمع من الدارقطني وطبقته، واستوطن بغداد إلى حين وفاته، وولى القضاء بعكبرا من قبل القاضى أبى بكر محمد بن الطيب، وكان ينتحل في الفقه مذهب الشافعى وفى الأصول مذهب الأشعرى، وله حظ من معرفة الأدب والعربية، وحدث شيئاً يسيراً كتبت عنه وكان صدوقاً، ومات في ليلة الثلاثاء الثانى والعشرين من شهر ربيع الأول سنة أربع وثلاثين وأربعمائة ودفن في صبيحة تلك الليلة في مقبرة الشونيزي.
And among them is Abu Hamid Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Dilwayh al-Istawa'i al-Dilwi. Abu al-Hasan Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Qubays al-Ghassani and Abu Mansur Abd al-Rahman ibn Muhammad ibn Zurayq al-Shaybani said to us: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Khatib said to us in the History of Baghdad: Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Dilwayh, Abu Hamid al-Istawa'i, known as al-Dilwi. Istawa to which he is attributed is a village of Nishapur. He heard from Abu Ahmad Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Ishaq al-Hafiz, Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ishaq al-Anmati, Abu Sa'id Abdullah ibn Abd al-Wahhab al-Razi, and Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Jawzaqi and others. He came to Baghdad and heard from al-Daraqutni and his contemporaries. He settled in Baghdad until his death. He was appointed judge of 'Ukbara by the authority of the Qadi Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Tayyib. He adopted in fiqh the school of al-Shafi'i and in usul the school of al-Ash'ari. He had a share of knowledge of literature and Arabic. He transmitted only a little, which I wrote from him, and he was trustworthy. He died on the night of Tuesday, the twenty-second of Rabi' al-Awwal of the year 434 AH, and was buried the morning of that night in the Shawunizi cemetery.

Commentary
This is a biography of Abu Hamid al-Istawa'i, also known as al-Dilwi. The passage begins with his full lineage. It is transmitted via two chains from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi's History of Baghdad. We learn that Istawa is a village in Nishapur. He studied with several scholars, including Abu Ahmad al-Hafiz, Abu al-Abbas al-Anmati, Abu Sa'id al-Razi, and Muhammad al-Jawzaqi. He then moved to Baghdad and heard from the famous hadith scholar al-Daraqutni and his contemporaries. He settled in Baghdad until his death. He was appointed as judge of 'Ukbara by Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani (Ibn al-Tayyib). His theological stance is explicitly stated: in fiqh he followed the Shafi'i madhhab, and in usul al-din (theology) he followed the Ash'ari madhhab. He also had knowledge of literature and Arabic. He transmitted only a few hadiths, which the author (Ibn 'Asakir) wrote from him, and he was considered truthful (saduq). His death date is given: night of Tuesday, 22 Rabi' al-Awwal 434 AH, and he was buried the next morning in the Shawunizi cemetery.

Poetry can be a powerful tool for defending the honor of the Companions.

Ibn 'Asakir includes biographies of notable defenders of Ahl al-Sunnah. This passage introduces a poet who dedicated his entire Diwan to praising the Companions and refuting those who revile them. His story shows how the pen and verse can serve the cause of truth.

3

The text states almost all his poetry was in praise of the Companions and refutation of the Rafida. Ask yourself: Why would a scholar dedicate his poetry to this cause?
This reflects the sectarian tensions of his time.

فمنهم أبو الحسن السكرى البغدادي الشاعر رحمه الله، وهو قديم المولد متقدم الوفاة، أخبرنا الشيخ أبو منصور محمد بن عبد الملك بن خيرون وغيره قالا قال لنا أبو بكر أحمد بن على بن ثابت الحافظ: على بن عیسی بن سلیمان بن محمد ابن سليمان بن أبان بن أصفروخ، أبو الحسن الفارسي المعروف بالسكرى الشاعر، أصله من نفر، وهو بلد على النرس من بلاد الفرس، وكان مولد على بن عيسى ببغداد يوم الخميس لخمس خلون من صفر سنة سبع وخمسين وثلاثمائة، وصحب القاضي أبا بكر محمد بن الطيب الأشعري ودرس عليه الكلام، وكان يحفظ القرآن والقراءات، وكان متفنناً في الأدب، وله ديوان شعر كبير وكله إلا اليسير منه في مدح الصحابة والرد على الرافضة والنقض على شعرائهم، وتوفى يوم سلخ شعبان من سنة ثلاث عشرة وأربعمائة ودفن من الغد في مقبرة باب الدير التي فيها قبر معروف الکرخی رحمه الله.
Among them is Abu al-Hasan al-Sukari al-Baghdadi, the poet, may Allah have mercy on him. He was of early birth and early death. Shaykh Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik ibn Khayrun and others informed us, both saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Hafiz said to us: Ali ibn Isa ibn Sulayman ibn Muhammad ibn Sulayman ibn Aban ibn Asfarukh, Abu al-Hasan al-Farsi, known as al-Sukari, the poet. His origin is from Nafar, a town on the river Nars from the land of Persia. Ali ibn Isa was born in Baghdad on Thursday, five days before the end of Safar in the year 357 AH. He accompanied the Qadi Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Tayyib al-Ash'ari and studied kalam under him. He memorized the Qur'an and the qira'at. He was versatile in literature. He has a large diwan of poetry, all but a little of it in praise of the Companions, refutation of the Rafida, and critique of their poets. He died on the last day of Sha'ban of the year 413 AH and was buried the next day in the cemetery of Bab al-Dayr, which contains the grave of Ma'ruf al-Karkhi, may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This is a biography of the poet Abu al-Hasan al-Sukari. He is described as having an early birth and early death relative to other scholars. The chain of transmission goes through al-Khatib al-Baghdadi. His full name and lineage are given: Ali ibn Isa... al-Farsi known as al-Sukari. His origin is from a place called Nafar on the river Nars in Persia, but he was born in Baghdad. His birth date is specified: Thursday, 5 days left in Safar 357 AH (corresponding to about January 968 CE). He studied under Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani (Ibn al-Tayyib al-Ash'ari) and studied kalam (theology) with him. He memorized the entire Quran and was proficient in the various modes of Quranic recitation (qira'at). He was also well-versed in literature. His poetry collection (diwan) is large, and almost all of it is dedicated to praising the Sahaba (Companions of the Prophet), refuting the Rafida (a term for those who reject the first three caliphs, often referring to Shi'a extremists), and criticizing their poets. He died on the last day of Sha'ban 413 AH (December 1022 CE) and was buried the next day in the cemetery of Bab al-Dayr, which is the same cemetery where the famous saint Ma'ruf al-Karkhi is buried.

Key Terms
السكري
الرافضة
الشعر
مدح الصحابة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the term Rafida refers to all Shia.
Correction: In classical Sunni usage, Rafida specifically refers to those who reject the caliphates of Abu Bakr and Umar, not all Shia.

Key Takeaway
Abu al-Hasan al-Sukari was a poet who used his verse to defend the Companions and refute their detractors, showing the role of literature in Sunni theology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The source mentions that al-Sukari studied kalam under al-Baqillani and memorized the Qur'an and qira'at. He combined deep learning with poetic skill. Are you using your knowledge of Islamic sciences to actively defend the truth, or is it merely academic? Where in your life can you follow his example by applying your learning to protect the legacy of the Companions?

Al-Sukari was not just a poet; he was a polemicist who directly refuted the Rafida and critiqued their poets. Consider the people in your circle who speak ill of the Companions. Are you silent out of discomfort or fear? What would it cost you to speak up as al-Sukari did, and what is the cost of remaining silent?

Learning Objective

Core Idea

In this passage, Ibn 'Asakir introduces another scholar from the Ash'ari tradition: Abu Mansur al-Ayyubi al-Naysaburi. The entry is transmitted via a written statement from Abd al-Ghafir ibn Isma'il and is filled with high praise, listing several honorific titles that highlight the scholar's intellectual virtues. As you read, notice how the description emphasizes both his personal qualities and his association with the Ash'ari madhhab.

Note the incomplete ending

Commentary
This passage introduces Abu Mansur al-Ayyubi al-Naysaburi as a distinguished Ash'ari scholar. It begins with a phrase 'and among them' continuing the list of scholars from the third class. Ibn Asakir provides a biography of Abu al-Hasan al-Sukkari, highlighting his lineage, education, and poetic works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and scholarly profile of Abu al-Hasan al-Sukkari, a poet and mutakallim from the third generation of Ash'ari scholars.

Core Idea
Al-Sukkari used poetry to defend the Companions and refute the Rafida.

Ibn Asakir introduces the third generation of Ash'ari scholars by highlighting those who met the companions of the earlier generation. Among them is Abu al-Hasan al-Sukkari, a poet and student of al-Baqillani. His biography illustrates how one could be both a skilled poet and a serious scholar of kalam, using poetry as a tool for theological defense.

Guided Path
1

This shows the intersection of theology and literature in defending Sunni orthodoxy.

Commentary
This passage begins with an introduction to the third generation of Ash'ari scholars, indicating that they met the companions of the earlier generation and learned from them. Biography of Abu Mansur al-Ayyubi
Ibn Asakir records the biography of a prominent Ash'ari scholar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the character and struggles of the Ash'ari scholar Abu Mansur al-Ayyubi and how his piety and diligence earned him recognition despite poverty.

Core Idea
Poverty and piety can be stepping stones to scholarly greatness.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari presents the biography of Abu Mansur al-Ayyubi, a remarkable Ash'ari scholar. Despite severe poverty, he excelled in learning and earned the respect of his teacher, who married his daughter to him. His story illustrates that dedication to knowledge and piety can overcome material hardships.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the life of Abu Mansur al-Ayyubi. Note his titles and achievements.
Pay attention to the sequence of events from his studies to his marriage.
2
Identify his key titles and works
Look for phrases like 'al-Ustadh al-Imam', 'Hujjat al-Din', and the book 'Talkhis al-Dala'il'. These show his scholarly rank.
His titles reflect his mastery of evidence and reasoning.
3
Examine his hardships and response
The passage mentions his poverty, studying by moonlight, and piety. Consider how he maintained his dedication despite lack of resources.
His refusal to take suspicious money shows his scrupulousness.
4
Reflect on the teacher-student relationship
Note that his teacher Abu Bakr ibn Furak married his daughter to him. This indicates the high regard the teacher had for him.
The passage says he was 'more penetrating and braver' than his teacher.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم أبو منصور الأيوبى النيسابوري رحمه الله كتب إلى الشيخ أبو الحسن عبد الغافر بن إسماعيل قال : محمد بن الحسن بن أبي أيوب أبو منصور الأستاذ الإمام حجة الدين صاحب البيان والحجة والبرهان واللسان الفصيح والنظر الصحيح ، أنظر من كان في عصره ومن تقدمه ومن بعده على مذهب الأشعرى ، واتفق له إعداد من التصانيف المشهورة المقبولة عند أئمة الأصول مثل تلخيص الدلائل تلمذ للأستاذ أبى بكر بن فورك في صباه وتخرج به ولزم طريقته ، وجد واجتهد في فقر وقلة من ذات اليد حتى كان يعلق دروسه ويطالعها في القمر لضيق يده عن تحصيل دهن السراج ، وهو مع ذلك يكابد الفقر ويلازم الورع ولا يأخذ من مال الشبهة شيئاً إلى أن نشأ في ذلك وصار من منظورى أصحاب الإمام ، وظهرت بركة خدمته عليه فأدى الحال إلى أن زوج منه ابنته الكبرى وكان أنفذ من الأستاذ وأشجع منه ، توفي في ذي الحجة سنة إحدى وعشرين وأربعمائة ودفن بمقبرة شاهنتر
And among them is Abu Mansur al-Ayyubi al-Naysaburi, may Allah have mercy on him. He wrote to Shaykh Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Ghafir ibn Ismail, saying: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Abi Ayyub Abu Mansur, the master, the imam, the proof of the religion, the possessor of eloquence, evidence, demonstration, a fluent tongue, and sound reasoning, the most insightful of those in his time, before him, and after him, according to the Ash'ari school. He authored many famous works accepted by the leading scholars of fundamentals, such as Talkhis al-Dala'il. He studied under Master Abu Bakr ibn Furak in his youth, graduated under him, and adhered to his methodology. He strove and exerted himself in poverty and lack of means, to the extent that he would write his lessons and review them by moonlight due to his inability to afford lamp oil. Despite that, he endured poverty and adhered to piety, never taking anything from suspicious money, until he grew up in that state and became one of the distinguished companions of the Imam. The blessing of his service to him became evident, leading to the Imam marrying him to his eldest daughter. He was more penetrating and braver than his teacher. He died in Dhu al-Hijjah of the year 421 AH and was buried in the Shahantar cemetery.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage provides the biography of Abu Mansur al-Ayyubi al-Naysaburi, a prominent Ash'ari scholar. It begins with his full name and titles: 'al-Ustadh al-Imam, Hujjat al-Din' (Proof of the Religion). He was known for his eloquence, evidence, and sound reasoning. He was considered the most insightful of his time on the Ash'ari school. He authored famous works in usul al-fiqh, such as Talkhis al-Dala'il. He studied under Abu Bakr ibn Furak in his youth and stuck to his methodology. Despite severe poverty, he continued his studies by moonlight because he could not afford lamp oil. He remained pious, rejecting money of doubtful source. Because of his dedication, his teacher Ibn Furak married him to his eldest daughter. The passage notes that al-Ayyubi was more penetrating and braver than his teacher. He died in 421 AH and was buried in the Shahantar cemetery.

A Maliki judge and prolific scholar who served in Iraq and settled in Egypt.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's Tabyin presents the biography of a prominent Maliki jurist. Through two chains of transmission, we learn about his education, his judgeship, his scholarly output, and his final days in Egypt. The text offers a window into the life of a medieval scholar and the networks that sustained Islamic learning.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography

3

ومنهم القاضي أبو محمد عبد الوهاب بن علی البغدادی رحمه الله أخبرنا الشيخان أبو الحسن علي بن أحمد بن قـبـيس بدمشق وأبو منصور عبد الرحمن بن محمد بن عبد الواحد بن زريق ببغداد قالا قال لنا الشيخ الحافظ أبو بكر أحمد بن علی بن ثابت : عبد الوهاب بن على بن نصر بن أحمد بن الحسين بن هرون بن مالك ، أبو محمد الفقيه المالكي سمع أبا عبد الله بن العسكرى وعمر بن محمد بن سبنك ، وأبا حفص بن شاهين وحدث بشئ يسير كتبت عنه وكان ثقة ، ولم تلق من المالكين أفقه منه ، وكان حسن النظر جيد العبارة تولى القضاء بباذرايا وباكسايا وخرج في آخر عمره إلى مصر فمات بها في شعبان من سنة اثنتين وعشرين وأربعمائة . أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم إسماعيل بن أحمد قال ثنا الشيخ أبو إسحق إبراهيم بن على بن يوسف الفقيه لفظا قال : أبو محمد عبد الوهاب ابن على بن نصر أدركته وسمعت كلامه في النظر وكان قد رأى أبا بكر الأبهرى إلا أنه لم يسمع منه شيئاً وكان فقيهاً شاعراً متأدباً وله كتب كثيرة في كل فن من الفقه ، وخرج فى آخر عمره إلى مصر وحصل له هناك حال من الدنيا بالمغاربة ومات بمصر سنة اثنتين وعشرين وأربعمائة وأنشد في خروجه من بغداد :
And among them is Judge Abu Muhammad Abd al-Wahhab ibn Ali al-Baghdadi, may Allah have mercy on him. The two shaykhs informed us: Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Qubays in Damascus and Abu Mansur Abd al-Rahman ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Wahid ibn Zurayq in Baghdad, both said: The shaykh and hafiz Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit said to us: Abd al-Wahhab ibn Ali ibn Nasr ibn Ahmad ibn al-Husayn ibn Harun ibn Malik, Abu Muhammad the Maliki jurist. He heard from Abu Abd Allah ibn al-Askari, Umar ibn Muhammad ibn Sabank, and Abu Hafs ibn Shahin. He narrated a little, which I wrote from him, and he was trustworthy. I did not meet among the Malikis anyone more knowledgeable than him. He had good reasoning and excellent expression. He served as judge in Badharraya and Baksaya. He left at the end of his life for Egypt and died there in Sha'ban of the year 422 AH. And our shaykh Abu al-Qasim Ismail ibn Ahmad informed us, saying: Shaykh Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Ali ibn Yusuf al-Faqih narrated to us orally, saying: Abu Muhammad Abd al-Wahhab ibn Ali ibn Nasr, I met him and heard his speech in debate. He had seen Abu Bakr al-Abhari but did not hear anything from him. He was a jurist, poet, and literary man. He authored many books in every field of fiqh. He left at the end of his life for Egypt and acquired there some worldly status through the Maghribis, and died in Egypt in the year 422 AH. And he recited upon his departure from Baghdad:
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage gives the biography of Qadi Abd al-Wahhab al-Baghdadi, a Maliki jurist. It begins with his name and lineage, then provides a chain of transmission for the report about him. He was a trustworthy narrator, and the author (al-Khatib al-Baghdadi) states that he did not meet any Maliki more knowledgeable than him. He served as a judge in two locations, then left for Egypt towards the end of his life and died there in 422 AH. A second report from another chain mentions that he was a jurist, poet, literary figure, and authored many works on fiqh. He gained some worldly status in Egypt through the Maghribis (likely the Fatimid state). The passage ends with a line of poetry he recited upon leaving Baghdad, but the text cuts off.

A Devoted Student's Piety and Perseverance
Biography of a devoted student of Ibn Furak highlighting his piety and perseverance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the virtues of poverty and dedication in early Ash'ari scholarship through the biography of a student of Ibn Furak.

Core Idea
True scholarship flourishes in poverty and scrupulousness.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's Tabyīn Kadhib al-Muftarī presents a powerful example of early Ash'ari piety. It shows how a student of Imam Abu Bakr ibn Furak excelled despite extreme material hardship, earning the highest honor from his teacher. The biography invites us to reflect on the relationship between worldly means and spiritual attainment.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical sketch
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting the key details of the student's life.
The passage begins mid-sentence; the student's name is not given here.
2
Identify the virtues highlighted
The author stresses piety, perseverance, scrupulousness, and the blessing of service. List these virtues as you read.
Notice how the student's poverty is described in vivid detail.
3
Reflect on the lesson for today
Consider how this example challenges modern assumptions about resources and success. What does it teach about the relationship between material wealth and spiritual achievement?
This biography is a reminder that Allah blesses sincere effort regardless of circumstances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التصانيف المشهورة المقبولة عند أئمة الأصول مثل تلخيص الدلائل تلمذ للأستاذ أبى بكر بن فورك في صباه و تخرج به و لزم طريقته ، وجد واجتهد في فقر وقلة من ذات اليد حتى كان يعلق دروسه ويطالعها في القمر لضيق يده عن تحصيل دهن السراج ، وهو مع ذلك يكابد الفقر ويلازم الورع ولا يأخذ من مال الشبهة شيئاً إلى أن نشأ في ذلك وصار من منظورى أصحاب الإمام ، وظهرت بركة خدمته عليه فأدى الحال إلى أن زوج منه ابنته الكبرى وكان أنفذ من الأستاذ وأشجع منه ، توفي في ذي الحجة سنة إحدى وعشرين وأربعمائة ودفن بمقبرة شاهنتر
The well-known and accepted works according to the imams of the principles, such as Talkhīṣ al-Dalā'il, he studied under the master Abū Bakr ibn Fūrak in his youth, and graduated with him and adhered to his method. He exerted himself and strove in poverty and scarcity of means such that he would write down his lessons and review them by moonlight due to his inability to afford oil for a lamp. Despite that, he endured poverty and adhered to scrupulousness, taking nothing from doubtful wealth, until he grew up in that state and became one of the prominent companions of the Imam. The blessing of serving him became evident, leading to his marrying the Imam's eldest daughter. He was more penetrating and braver than the master. He died in Dhū al-Ḥijjah of the year 421 AH and was buried in the Shahantar cemetery.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch of an early Ash'ari scholar who was a student of Abu Bakr ibn Furak. The author begins by mentioning that this scholar authored well-known works accepted by the imams of usul, such as Talkhīṣ al-Dalā'il. He then notes that the scholar studied under Ibn Furak in his youth, graduated under him, and adhered to his methodology. The passage highlights the scholar's extreme poverty and asceticism: he could not afford lamp oil and studied by moonlight. Despite hardships, he maintained scrupulousness, avoiding doubtful wealth. His dedication brought him close to the Imam, who married his daughter to him. The scholar is described as 'more penetrating and braver' than his teacher. The passage concludes with his death date and burial place.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Early Ash'ari scholars were always wealthy and supported by the state.
Correction: This biography shows that early Ash'ari scholars faced extreme poverty, yet their dedication and scrupulousness earned them great honor.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Imam chose this student to marry his daughter because of his piety and perseverance. If your sincerity were measured by the same standard, what would your standing be? What change can you make in your daily routine to increase your devotion?

Biography of al-Qadi Abd al-Wahhab al-Baghdadi
Ibn Asakir records the biography of Abd al-Wahhab al-Baghdadi with two chains.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and scholarly contributions of the Maliki judge Abd al-Wahhab al-Baghdadi, as recorded by Ibn Asakir.

Core Idea
A scholar's legacy includes both knowledge and poetry.

This biographical passage from Ibn Asakir's Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari introduces us to a prominent Maliki jurist and judge, Abd al-Wahhab al-Baghdadi. Through two independent chains of transmission, we learn about his teachers, his judicial posts, his vast learning, and even his poetry. The passage shows how classical scholars integrated fiqh, literature, and personal expression.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the two chains of transmitters that Ibn Asakir provides to authenticate the information.
2
Identify key details
List the main facts about Abd al-Wahhab: his teachers, his judgeships, his move to Egypt, and his year of death.
3
Reflect on the poetry
Examine the poem at the end. What does it reveal about his feelings toward Baghdad? How does this add a personal dimension to the scholarly biography?
4
Connect to broader context
Consider how this biography exemplifies the ideal of the scholar who excelled in both religious sciences and literature. This was common among Ash'ari scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم القاضي أبو محمد عبد الوهاب بن علی البغدادی رحمه الله أخبرنا الشيخان أبو الحسن علي بن أحمد بن قـبـيس بدمشق وأبو منصور عبد الرحمن بن محمد بن عبد الواحد بن زريق ببغداد قالا قال لنا الشيخ الحافظ أبو بكر أحمد بن علی بن ثابت : عبد الوهاب بن على بن نصر بن أحمد بن الحسين بن هرون بن مالك ، أبو محمد الفقيه المالكي سمع أبا عبد الله بن العسكرى وعمر بن محمد بن سبنك ، وأبا حفص بن شاهين وحدث بشئ يسير كتبت عنه وكان ثقة ، ولم تلق من المالكين أفقه منه ، وكان حسن النظر جيد العبارة تولى القضاء بباذرايا وباكسايا وخرج في آخر عمره إلى مصر فمات بها في شعبان من سنة اثنتين وعشرين وأربعمائة . أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم إسماعيل بن أحمد قال ثنا الشيخ أبو إسحق إبراهيم بن على بن يوسف الفقيه لفظا قال : أبو محمد عبد الوهاب ابن على بن نصر أدركته وسمعت كلامه في النظر وكان قد رأى أبا بكر الأبهرى إلا أنه لم يسمع منه شيئاً وكان فقيهاً شاعراً متأدباً وله كتب كثيرة في كل فن من الفقه ، وخرج فى آخر عمره إلى مصر وحصل له هناك حال من الدنيا بالمغاربة ومات بمصر سنة اثنتين وعشرين وأربعمائة وأنشد في خروجه من بغداد : سلام على بغداد في كل موطن وحق لها على سلام مضاعف فو الله ما فارقتها عن قلا لها وأنى بشطى جانبـيـهـا لـعـارف ولكنها ضاقت على بأسرها ولم تكن الأرزاق فيها تساعف . وكانت كخل كنت أهوى دنوه وأخلاقه تنأى به وتخالف
And among them is the judge Abū Muḥammad ‘Abd al-Wahhāb ibn ‘Alī al-Baghdādī, may Allāh have mercy on him. The two shaykhs Abū al-Ḥasan ‘Alī ibn Aḥmad ibn Qubays in Damascus and Abū Manṣūr ‘Abd al-Raḥmān ibn Muḥammad ibn ‘Abd al-Wāḥid ibn Zuraik in Baghdad informed us, both saying: The ḥāfiẓ Abū Bakr Aḥmad ibn ‘Alī ibn Thābit said to us: ‘Abd al-Wahhāb ibn ‘Alī ibn Naṣr ibn Aḥmad ibn al-Ḥusayn ibn Hārūn ibn Mālik, Abū Muḥammad the Mālikī jurist, heard from Abū ‘Abd Allāh ibn al-‘Askarī, ‘Umar ibn Muḥammad ibn Subank, and Abū Ḥafṣ ibn Shāhīn, and he narrated a little, I wrote it from him, and he was trustworthy. I have not met among the Mālikīs anyone more knowledgeable in fiqh than him. He had good insight and good expression. He held judgeships in Bādharāyā and Bāksāyā, and at the end of his life he left for Egypt and died there in Sha‘bān of the year 422 AH. The shaykh Abū al-Qāsim Ismā‘īl ibn Aḥmad informed us, saying: The shaykh Abū Isḥāq Ibrāhīm ibn ‘Alī ibn Yūsuf al-Faqīh dictated to us, saying: Abū Muḥammad ‘Abd al-Wahhāb ibn ‘Alī ibn Naṣr—I met him and heard his speech in juristic reasoning. He had seen Abū Bakr al-Abharī but did not hear anything from him. He was a jurist, poet, and literary man. He had many books in every field of fiqh. At the end of his life he left for Egypt and acquired some worldly status there through the Maghribis, and died in Egypt in the year 422 AH. He recited upon his departure from Baghdad: 'Peace upon Baghdad in every station, and it deserves a double peace. By Allah, I did not leave it out of dislike, and how could I when I know its two banks? But it became too narrow for me entirely, and provisions were not abundant there. It was like a beloved whose closeness I loved, but whose morals kept him away and differed.'
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage presents the biography of al-Qadi ‘Abd al-Wahhāb al-Baghdādī, a Mālikī jurist and judge. Ibn ‘Asākir includes two chains of transmission to confirm the information. The first chain quotes al-Khaṭīb al-Baghdādī, who describes ‘Abd al-Wahhāb as trustworthy and the most knowledgeable Mālikī he met, noting his judgeships in Bādharāyā and Bāksāyā (locations in Iraq). The second chain, from Abū Isḥāq al-Fīrūzābādī, adds that he was a jurist, poet, and literary man with many books. Both chains confirm his death in Egypt in 422 AH. The passage ends with a poem by ‘Abd al-Wahhāb lamenting his departure from Baghdad, expressing his love for the city but his inability to stay due to hardship. This biographical entry exemplifies the integration of fiqh, kalam, and adab among Ash‘arī scholars.

Misconception: Judges and jurists were purely technical scholars with no interest in literature or poetry.
Correction: This biography shows Abd al-Wahhab al-Baghdadi was both a judge and a poet, integrating fiqh and adab.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

The Scholar, Poet, and Mutakallim: Abu al-Hasan al-Nu'aymi
Ibn Asakir records the biography and scholarly profile of al-Nu'aymi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Nu'aymi's biography illustrates the integration of hadith mastery, kalam, and poetic wisdom in traditional Islamic scholarship.

Core Idea
Al-Nu'aymi was both a hafiz and a mutakallim, combining textual and rational sciences.

Ibn Asakir continues his biographical entries with the life of Abu al-Hasan al-Nu'aymi al-Basri, a scholar who excelled in hadith, theology, and poetry. This brief portrait shows how a single scholar could master multiple disciplines and still remain grounded in humility and high aspiration, as reflected in his own verse.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the full Arabic passage and its English translation to get an overview of al-Nu'aymi's life, teachers, and character.
The passage includes two transmission chains and a poem.
2
Identify the two descriptions
Notice what al-Khatib al-Baghdadi and al-Shirazi each say about al-Nu'aymi's qualifications.
Both highlight different aspects: hadith mastery, figh, kalam, and poetry.
3
Reflect on the poem
Read the poem carefully. What values does it promote? How does it relate to the scholar's own life?
The poem emphasizes contentment and high aspiration.
4
Consider the integration of sciences
How does this biography demonstrate the compatibility of hadith and kalam?
This counters the misconception that kalam is opposed to traditional hadith study.

ومنهم أبو الحسن النعيمي البصري رحمه الله أخبرنا الشيخ أبو منصور محمد بن عبد الملك بن الحسن بن خيرون وأبو الحسن على بن الحسن قالا قال لنا أبو بكر أحمد بن على الحافظ : على بن أحمد ابن الحسن بن محمد بن نعيم أبو الحسن البصري المعروف بالنعيمي ، سكن بغداد وحدث بها عن أحمد بن محمد بن العباس الاسقاطى ومحمد بن أحمد بن الفيض الأصبهاني ، وعلى بن عمر السكري وأحمد بن عبيد الله النهرتيرى وعلى ابن أحمد بن موسى التمار و محمد بن عدي بن زحر المنقرى وأبى أحمد بن سعيد العسكري و محمد بن أحمد بن حماد بن سفيان الكوفى وأبى المفضل الشيباني والحسين بن أحمد بن دينار الدقاق ، وعـبـد بن محمد بن اليسع الأنطاكي وغيرهم من طبقتهم ، كتبت عنه وكان حافظاً عارفا متكلماً شاعراً . أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم ابن السمرقندى قال ثنا الشيخ أبو إسحق إبراهيم بن على الشيرازي قال : أبو الحسن على بن أحمد النعيمي درس بالاهواز وكان فقيهاً عالماً بالحديث متادباً متكلماً . أنشدنا الشيخ أبو محمد هبة الله بن أحمد بن على المنقرى إمام جامع دمشق املاء قال أنشدنا أبو الحسين عاصم بن الحسين العاصمي ببغداد قال أنشدني أبو الحسن على بن أحمد بن الحسن بن محمد بن نعيم البصري المعروف بالنعيمي لنفسه رحمه الله إذا أظمأتك أكف اللام كفتك القناعة شبعاً وريا فكن رجلا رجله في الثرى وهامة همته في الثريا أبينا لنائل ذى ثروة تراه بما في يديه أبيــــ فإن إراقة ماء الحياة دون إراقة ماء المحـ
And among them is Abū al-Ḥasan al-Nu‘aymī al-Baṣrī, may Allāh have mercy on him. The shaykh Abū Manṣūr Muḥammad ibn ‘Abd al-Malik ibn al-Ḥasan ibn Khayrūn and Abū al-Ḥasan ‘Alī ibn al-Ḥasan informed us, both saying: Abū Bakr Aḥmad ibn ‘Alī al-Ḥāfiẓ said to us: ‘Alī ibn Aḥmad ibn al-Ḥasan ibn Muḥammad ibn Nu‘aym, Abū al-Ḥasan al-Baṣrī known as al-Nu‘aymī, resided in Baghdad and narrated there from Aḥmad ibn Muḥammad ibn al-‘Abbās al-Asqāṭī, Muḥammad ibn Aḥmad ibn al-Fayḍ al-Aṣbahānī, ‘Alī ibn ‘Umar al-Sukkarī, Aḥmad ibn ‘Ubayd Allāh al-Nahrawtayrī, ‘Alī ibn Aḥmad ibn Mūsā al-Tammār, Muḥammad ibn ‘Adī ibn Zahr al-Minqarī, Abū Aḥmad ibn Sa‘īd al-‘Askarī, Muḥammad ibn Aḥmad ibn Ḥammād ibn Sufyān al-Kūfī, Abū al-Mufaḍḍal al-Shaybānī, al-Ḥusayn ibn Aḥmad ibn Dīnār al-Daqqāq, ‘Abd ibn Muḥammad ibn al-Yasa‘ al-Anṭākī, and others of their class. I wrote from him, and he was a ḥāfiẓ, knowledgeable, a mutakallim, and a poet. The shaykh Abū al-Qāsim ibn al-Samarqandī informed us, saying: The shaykh Abū Isḥāq Ibrāhīm ibn ‘Alī al-Shīrāzī said: Abū al-Ḥasan ‘Alī ibn Aḥmad al-Nu‘aymī taught in al-Ahwāz and was a jurist, knowledgeable in ḥadīth, literary, and a mutakallim. The shaykh Abū Muḥammad Hibat Allāh ibn Aḥmad ibn ‘Alī al-Minqarī, the imam of the Jāmi‘ mosque of Damascus, dictating, recited to us, saying: Abū al-Ḥusayn ‘Āṣim ibn al-Ḥusayn al-‘Āṣimī recited to us in Baghdad, saying: Abū al-Ḥasan ‘Alī ibn Aḥmad ibn al-Ḥasan ibn Muḥammad ibn Nu‘aym al-Baṣrī, known as al-Nu‘aymī, recited to me for himself, may Allāh have mercy on him: 'When the hands of the lowly make you thirsty, contentment suffices you with satiety and drink. So be a man whose foot is in the earth and whose aspiration is in the Pleiades. We disdain the gift of a wealthy man who sees what is in his hands as abundant. For the spilling of the water of life is easier than the spilling of the water of [incomplete]...'
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage provides the biography of Abū al-Ḥasan al-Nu‘aymī al-Baṣrī, an Ash‘arī scholar known for his knowledge of ḥadīth, kalām, and poetry. Ibn ‘Asākir cites two chains: first from al-Khaṭīb al-Baghdādī, who lists many of his teachers and describes him as a ḥāfiẓ, knowledgeable, a mutakallim, and a poet. The second chain from Abū Isḥāq al-Shīrāzī adds that he taught in al-Ahwāz and was a jurist and scholar of ḥadīth. The passage ends with a poem by al-Nu‘aymī praising contentment and high aspiration, though the poem is incomplete in the manuscript. This entry again emphasizes the combination of multiple disciplines in one scholar.

Key Terms
النعيمي البصري
الأهواز
حافظ
مكلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That a scholar of hadith cannot also be a theologian (mutakallim).
Correction: Al-Nu'aymi is described as both a hafiz and a mutakallim, showing that mastery of hadith and rational theology can coexist.

Checkpoint
According to al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, which of the following is NOT a description of al-Nu'aymi?
A) Ḥāfiẓ
B) Faqīh
C) Mutakallim
D) Poet

Key Takeaway
Al-Nu'aymi's biography exemplifies how a scholar can master both transmitted and rational sciences while embodying humility and high aspiration.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you, like al-Nu'aymi, content with what Allah has given you, or do you find yourself looking to the hands of others for validation and provision? Examine your heart right now: does it feel the sting of craving someone's praise or wealth? What would it take for you to truly say, 'Your contentment suffices me'?
?
Your foot may be on the earth, but where is your aspiration? Al-Nu'aymi aimed for the Pleiades while remaining humble. What is the highest goal you are currently pursuing—is it worldly recognition or something that pleases Allah? If you died today, would that goal have been worth it?
?
The spilling of water is easy, but the spilling of your dignity before a wealthy man is harder. When have you sacrificed your dignity or compromised your principles for material gain or social standing? Repent now and resolve to never let your honor be sold cheaply again.

The Multifaceted Scholar: Biography of Abu al-Hasan al-Nu'aymi
Ibn Asakir presents the biography of al-Nu'aymi, a hadith master and kalam theologian.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly profile of al-Nu'aymi as a hadith memorizer, theologian, and poet, and the key testimonies about his character and death.

Core Idea
Al-Nu'aymi combined hadith mastery, theology, and poetry with deep devotion to the Sunnah.

This biography from Ibn Asakir introduces us to a remarkable scholar of Baghdad who excelled in multiple disciplines. As you read, notice how the entry weaves together his teachers, his own poetry, and the evaluations of his peers. The passage reveals both his strengths and a reported minor flaw, showing the nuanced approach of classical biographical writing.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical data
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the chain of transmission through which Ibn Asakir received this report, and the list of al-Nu'aymi's teachers.
The chain shows careful scholarly authentication.
2
Identify his scholarly titles
The passage describes al-Nu'aymi as a hafiz, arif, mutakallim, and poet. Consider what each title implies about his learning.
These terms reflect different aspects of Islamic scholarship.
3
Reflect on the poem
Read the poem attributed to al-Nu'aymi. What message does it convey about contentment and dignity? The poem's wording has textual issues, but its theme is clear.
The poem is partially corrupted in the manuscript.
4
Consider the testimonies
Review the statements by al-Suri and al-Barqani. Note the praise and the mention of a 'blemish'. How does al-Barqani's later dream balance the criticism?
The dream indicates al-Nu'aymi's good end.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم أبو الحسن النعيمي البصري رحمه الله . أخبرنا الشيخ أبو منصور محمد بن عبد الملك بن الحسن بن خيرون وأبو الحسن على بن الحسن قالا قال لنا أبو بكر أحمد بن على الحافظ : على بن أحمد ابن الحسن بن محمد بن نعيم أبو الحسن البصري المعروف بالنعيمي ، سكن بغداد وحدث بها عن أحمد بن محمد بن العباس الاسقاطى ومحمد بن أحمد بن الفيض الأصبهاني ، وعلى بن عمر السكري وأحمد بن عبيد الله النهرتيرى وعلى ابن أحمد بن موسى التمار و محمد بن عدي بن زحر المنقرى وأبى أحمد بن سعيد العسكري و محمد بن أحمد بن حماد بن سفيان الكوفى وأبى المفضل الشيباني والحسين بن أحمد بن دينار الدقاق ، وعبد بن محمد بن اليسع الأنطاكي وغيرهم من طبقتهم ، كتبت عنه وكان حافظاً عارفا متكلماً شاعراً . أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم ابن السمرقندى قال ثنا الشيخ أبو إسحق إبراهيم بن على الشيرازي قال : أبو الحسن على بن أحمد النعيمي درس بالاهواز وكان فقيهاً عالماً بالحديث متادباً متكلماً . أنشدنا الشيخ أبو محمد هبة الله بن أحمد بن على المنقرى إمام جامع دمشق املاء قال أنشدنا أبو الحسين عاصم بن الحسين العاصمي ببغداد قال أنشدني أبو الحسن على بن أحمد بن الحسن بن محمد بن نعيم البصري المعروف بالنعيمي لنفسه رحمه الله : إذا أظمأتك أكف اللام كفتك القناعة شبعاً وريا فكن رجلا رجله في الثرى وهامة همته في الثريا أبينا لنائل ذى ثروة تراه بما في يديه أبي فإن إراقة ماء الحياة دون إراقة ماء المحـ رواها أبو بكر الخطيب عن محمد بن الصوري عن النعيمي والله أعلم . أخبرنا الشيخ أبو منصور محمد بن عبد الملك المقرى ببغداد قال أخبرنا ، وأبو الحسن بن سعيد قال ثنا أحمد بن على بن ثابت الخطيب قال سمعت محمد بن على الصورى يقول لم أر ببغداد أحداً أكمل من النعيمي كان قد جمع معرفة الحديث والكلام والأدب ، ودرس شيئا من فقه الشافعي ، قال وكان أبو بكر البرقاني يقول هو كامل في كل شئ لولا بأو فيه ، قال وأخبرنا أحمد بن على الخطيب قال حدثنا البرقاني بعد موت النعيمي قال رأيت النعيمى في منامي بهيئة جميلة وحالة صالحة ، ثم قال البرقاني قد كان شديد العصبية في السنة وكان يعرف من كل علم شيئا ، مات النعيمي في يوم الاثنين مستهل ذى القعدة سنة ثلاث وعشرين وأربعمائة رحمه الله
Among them is Abu al-Hasan al-Nu'aymi al-Basri, may Allah have mercy on him. Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik ibn al-Hasan ibn Khayrun and Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn al-Hasan informed us, both saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali al-Hafiz told us: Ali ibn Ahmad ibn al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn Nu'aym, Abu al-Hasan al-Basri, known as al-Nu'aymi, resided in Baghdad and narrated there from Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Abbas al-Isqati, Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn al-Fayd al-Isbahani, Ali ibn Umar al-Sukri, Ahmad ibn Ubayd Allah al-Nahratiri, Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Musa al-Tammar, Muhammad ibn Adi ibn Zahr al-Minqari, Abu Ahmad ibn Sa'id al-Askari, Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Hammad ibn Sufyan al-Kufi, Abu al-Mufaddal al-Shaybani, al-Husayn ibn Ahmad ibn Dinar al-Daqqaq, Abd ibn Muhammad ibn al-Yasa' al-Antaki, and others of their level. I wrote from him, and he was a memorizer, knowledgeable, a theologian (mutakallim), and a poet. Abu al-Qasim ibn al-Samarqandi informed us, saying: Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Ali al-Shirazi narrated to us, saying: Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad al-Nu'aymi studied in al-Ahwaz, and he was a jurist, knowledgeable in hadith, well-mannered, and a theologian. Abu Muhammad Hibat Allah ibn Ahmad ibn Ali al-Minqari, the imam of the Great Mosque of Damascus, dictated to us, saying: Abu al-Husayn Asim ibn al-Husayn al-Asimi in Baghdad narrated to us, saying: Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad ibn al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn Nu'aym al-Basri, known as al-Nu'aymi, recited for me his own poetry, may Allah have mercy on him: 'When the hands of [people?] make you thirsty, contentment suffices you with fullness and drink. So be a man whose foot is on the earth and whose mind's ambition is in the Pleiades. We refuse a giver of wealth whom you see stingy with what he has, for spilling the water of life is easier than spilling the water of [shame?].' Abu Bakr al-Khatib narrated it from Muhammad ibn al-Suri from al-Nu'aymi, and Allah knows best. Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Muqri' in Baghdad informed us, saying: [and] Abu al-Hasan ibn Sa'id said: Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Khatib narrated to us, saying: I heard Muhammad ibn Ali al-Suri say: 'I have not seen in Baghdad anyone more perfect than al-Nu'aymi. He had combined knowledge of hadith, theology (kalam), and literature, and studied something of Shafi'i jurisprudence.' He said: Abu Bakr al-Barqani used to say: 'He is perfect in everything except for a slight blemish (ba') in him.' He said: Ahmad ibn Ali al-Khatib informed us, saying: al-Barqani narrated to us after the death of al-Nu'aymi, saying: 'I saw al-Nu'aymi in my dream with a beautiful appearance and a righteous state.' Then al-Barqani said: 'He was intensely partisan for the Sunnah and knew something of every science.' Al-Nu'aymi died on Monday, the beginning of Dhu al-Qa'dah, the year 423 AH, may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Abu al-Hasan al-Nu'aymi al-Basri, a scholar who excelled in multiple fields. The entry begins by establishing his identity and chain of transmission: Ibn Asakir received reports about al-Nu'aymi from two teachers, who in turn heard from the famous hadith master Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali al-Khatib al-Baghdadi. The text then lists many of al-Nu'aymi's teachers from various regions, showing his wide travels and scholarly connections. Al-Khatib notes that he wrote from al-Nu'aymi and describes him as a 'hafiz' (memorizer of many hadith), 'arif' (gnostic or expert), 'mutakallim' (theologian), and 'sha'ir' (poet). Next, a report from al-Shirazi adds that al-Nu'aymi studied in al-Ahwaz and was a jurist, well-versed in hadith, well-mannered, and a theologian. The passage then includes a poem composed by al-Nu'aymi, which urges contentment and dignity. The poem's precise wording is slightly problematic in the manuscript. After the poem, the text returns to testimonies: al-Suri states he saw no one more perfect than al-Nu'aymi in Baghdad, praising his combination of hadith, kalam, and adab, and his study of Shafi'i fiqh. However, al-Barqani notes a small flaw: 'bā' fīhi' – a slight blemish. Despite this, al-Barqani later reports a dream in which he saw al-Nu'aymi in a good state, and he praises his strong partisanship for the Sunnah and his knowledge of many sciences. The biography concludes with his death date: Monday, 1 Dhu al-Qa'dah 423 AH (October 1032 CE).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The 'blemish' (بأو) mentioned by al-Barqani is a major moral fault.
Correction: In context, the 'blemish' likely refers to a minor imperfection, as al-Barqani later dreams of al-Nu'aymi in a good state and praises his partisanship for the Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Al-Nu'aymi was a multifaceted scholar whose biography illustrates the integration of hadith, theology, and poetry, and the nuanced judgment of his peers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Are you living with your head in the clouds of ambition while your feet are not firmly grounded in practice? Or are you so focused on worldly concerns that you have no aspiration for higher knowledge? Which imbalance describes you right now, and what is one small change you can make today to bring them into harmony?
?
Al-Suri said he never saw anyone more perfect than al-Nu'aymi in Baghdad. Yet al-Barqani initially said he had a blemish. This teaches that human judgment is complex. Who is someone you have dismissed due to a perceived flaw? How can you, like al-Barqani, look beyond that and see their deeper worth? What concrete action can you take to change your attitude toward them this week?

The Biography of Abu Tahir ibn Kharasha al-Dimashqi
Ibn Asakir relates the biography of the qari' Abu Tahir ibn Kharasha, noting his reliability and Ash'ari madhhab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir uses biographical entries to establish the credibility and Ash'ari affiliation of key scholars.

Core Idea
Biography as argument: trustworthy Ash'ari imams bolster the school's credibility.

In defending Ash'ari theology, Ibn Asakir provides biographical sketches of notable scholars who followed the Ash'ari school. This entry on Abu Tahir ibn Kharasha, the imam of the Great Mosque of Damascus, demonstrates that a respected Qur'an reader and teacher was both reliable (thiqa) and an adherent of the Ash'ari madhhab. The passage shows how historical documentation serves theological apologetics.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic text once to get the flow, then read the English translation. Notice the chain of transmission and the details provided about Abu Tahir.
The chain is from Ibn Asakir to al-Akfani to al-Kattani.
2
Identify the key biographical details
List the name, title, death date, teachers, and character description. Pay attention to the phrase 'يذهب إلى مذهب الأشعرى'.
This phrase explicitly states his school.
3
Reflect on the purpose of the biography
Consider why Ibn Asakir includes this biography in a work defending Ash'ari theology. How does this entry support his overall argument?
It shows that a trusted religious authority was Ash'ari.
4
Address the common misunderstanding
The term 'مذهب الأشعرى' is often misunderstood. It does not mean he was a theologian, but that he adhered to Ash'ari principles. Understand this distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم أبو طاهر بن خراشة الدمشقى المقرى رحمه الله . أخبرنا الشيخ الأمين أبو محمد هبة الله بن أحمد الأكفاني ، قال ثنا أبو محمد عبد العزيز بن أحمد بن محمد الكتاني قال توفى شيخنا أبو ظاهر الحسين ابن محمد بن عامر الإبلى المقرى إمام جامع دمشق يوم الاربعاء السابع من شهر ربيع الآخر من سنة ثمان وعشرين وأربعمائة ، حدث عن يوسف بن القسم الميانجى والحسين بن إبراهيم بن أبى الزمزام الفرائضى وغيرهما ، وكان ثقة نبيلا مأمونا يذهب إلى مذهب الأشعرى
Among them is Abu Tahir ibn Kharasha al-Dimashqi al-Muqri', may Allah have mercy on him. The trustworthy shaikh Abu Muhammad Hibat Allah ibn Ahmad al-Akfani informed us, saying: Abu Muhammad Abd al-Aziz ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Kattani narrated to us, saying: Our shaikh Abu Zahir al-Husayn ibn Muhammad ibn Amir al-Ibli al-Muqri', the imam of the Great Mosque of Damascus, died on Wednesday, the seventh of Rabi' al-Akhir of the year 428 AH. He narrated from Yusuf ibn al-Qasim al-Miyanaji, al-Husayn ibn Ibrahim ibn Abi al-Zamzam al-Fara'idi, and others. He was trustworthy, noble, reliable, and followed the Ash'ari school of thought.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Abu Tahir ibn Kharasha al-Dimashqi, a Qur'an reader (muqri') and imam of the Great Mosque of Damascus. The chain of transmission is from Ibn Asakir to al-Akfani to al-Kattani. Al-Kattani reports the death of his teacher Abu Zahir on Wednesday, 7 Rabi' al-Akhir 428 AH (January 1037 CE). The biography lists two of Abu Tahir's teachers: Yusuf ibn al-Qasim al-Miyanaji and al-Husayn ibn Ibrahim ibn Abi al-Zamzam al-Fara'idi. It then describes his character as trustworthy (thiqa), noble (nabīl), reliable (ma'mūn), and explicitly states that he followed the Ash'ari school (madhhab al-Ash'arī). This is significant because the book (Tabyin Kidhb al-Muftari) defends Ash'ari theology, so noting that a respected imam was Ash'ari is part of the overall argument.

Key Terms
أبو طاهر بن خراشة
المقرى
إمام جامع دمشق
مذهب الأشعرى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The term 'مذهب الأشعرى' implies the person was a theologian or philosopher.
Correction: It indicates adherence to the theological principles of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, which were mainstream among many Sunni scholars, especially Shafi'is. It does not mean he specialized in theology.

B) 7 Rabi' al-Awwal 428 AH

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir uses a precise biographical entry to show that a respected Qur'an reciter and imam of Damascus was an adherent of the Ash'ari school, reinforcing the legitimacy of the school.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

How does that affect your own approach to learning from historical figures in Islam? Will you now seek to understand the theological background of the scholars you study? Answer honestly.

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
intermediate

Al-Sabuni's Testimony on Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi
Ibn Asakir records al-Sabuni's praise and instruction to record the full name.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Sabuni's insistence on recording al-Baghdadi's full name matters for Sunni historiography and theology.

Core Idea
Even a critic's careful praise carries weight.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's Tabyin preserves a moment where the renowned traditionalist Abu Uthman al-Sabuni insists on a precise attribution for the Ash'ari theologian Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi. Though al-Sabuni was not an Ash'ari, his respect for al-Baghdadi's scholarship highlights a key lesson about scholarly integrity and the importance of accurate record-keeping in Islamic history.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic text once, then the translation. Notice the chain of narrators.
The chain is: Ibn Asakir ← al-Salamasi ← Abu Tahir ← Abu Ali ← al-Sabuni.
2
Identify key figures
Identify al-Sabuni (the speaker), al-Baghdadi (the subject), and the narrators. Understand their backgrounds.
Al-Sabuni was a prominent traditionalist often critical of Ash'ari theology.
3
Understand the anecdote
Why did al-Sabuni correct Abu Ali's omission? What was the potential confusion?
Abu Ali relied on al-Baghdadi's fame, but al-Sabuni wanted the full name to avoid mistaking him for another Abu Mansur.
4
Reflect on significance
Consider what this exchange tells us about al-Sabuni's attitude towards al-Baghdadi and the principle of fairness in scholarship.
Al-Sabuni's respect for accurate attribution crosses theological lines.
5
Apply the lesson
How does this story exemplify the principle of 'adl (fairness) in reporting? Reflect on its relevance today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأستاذ أبو منصور النيسابورى المعروف بالبغدادي رحمه الله . حدثنى الشيخ أبو بكر يحيى بن إبراهيم بن أحمد بن محمد السلماسى عن أبيه القاضي أبي طاهر قال قال أبو على الحسن بن نصر بن كاكا المرندى الفقيه في ذكر أبي عثمان الصابوني أنه ذكر أبا منصور المتكلم ، قال أبو على وكنت قد أهملت ذكر اسمه ونسبه اعتماداً على شهرته فقال لى أبو عثمان قيد ذكره بإثبات اسمه وأزل الشبهة عن [ر؟] أثبت فوق الكنية عبد القاهر بن طاهر لئلا يظن أنك أردت أبا منصور
The master Abu Mansur al-Naysaburi, known as al-Baghdadi, may Allah have mercy on him. The shaikh Abu Bakr Yahya ibn Ibrahim ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Salamasi narrated to me from his father, the judge Abu Tahir, who said: Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Nasr ibn Kaka al-Marandi the jurist said, in mentioning Abu Uthman al-Sabuni, that he mentioned Abu Mansur the theologian. Abu Ali said: I had neglected to mention his name and lineage, relying on his fame. So Abu Uthman said to me: 'Record his mention by writing his name, and remove the ambiguity. Write above the kunya: Abd al-Qahir ibn Tahir, lest it be thought that you meant another Abu Mansur.'
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a biographical notice for Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi, a famous Ash'ari theologian and author. The entry is a short anecdote preserving the testimony of Abu Uthman al-Sabuni, a renowned traditionalist (often associated with anti-Ash'ari sentiments). The chain: Ibn Asakir heard from al-Salamasi, who heard from his father Abu Tahir, who heard from Abu Ali al-Marandi. Abu Ali recounts that when he mentioned Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi in the presence of al-Sabuni, al-Sabuni insisted that he record the full name 'Abd al-Qahir ibn Tahir' to avoid confusion with another Abu Mansur. This story shows that al-Sabuni, despite his known opposition to Ash'ari theology, held Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi in high regard and wanted his identity clearly established. The passage thus serves to bolster al-Baghdadi's reputation by association with a respected scholar from a different theological camp.

Key Terms
الأستاذ أبو منصور البغدادي
عبد القاهر بن طاهر
أبو عثمان الصابوني
شهرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Sabuni's correction implies he agreed with al-Baghdadi's theology.
Correction: Al-Sabuni's action does not indicate theological agreement; rather it shows his respect for scholarly accuracy and al-Baghdadi's reputation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did al-Sabuni tell Abu Ali to record al-Baghdadi's full name?
A) To show his agreement with al-Baghdadi's theology
B) To avoid confusion with another Abu Mansur
C) To criticize al-Baghdadi's scholarship
D) To ensure al-Baghdadi's fame

Key Takeaway
Al-Sabuni's insistence on precise naming underscores the importance of scholarly integrity even across theological divides.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you speak about someone you disagree with theologically, do you take care to represent them accurately, or do you rely on general reputation and risk misattribution like Abu Ali initially did?
?
Al-Sabuni, despite being a critic, insisted on precise naming to avoid confusion. Is there a person or group you have mischaracterized due to carelessness? Will you commit to correcting that error today?
?
How often do you assume the worst about an opponent’s character? Would you go out of your way to ensure their name is recorded correctly, as al-Sabuni did for al-Baghdadi? What holds you back?
