Al-Nu'aymi: The Complete Scholar with a Blemish
Ibn Asakir narrates praise and a blemish of al-Nu'aymi from al-Suri and al-Barqani.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nuanced praise and criticism of a classical scholar and how a 'blemish' does not negate overall excellence.

Core Idea
A scholar can be 'complete' yet have a blemish; both praise and criticism can coexist.

This passage from Ibn Asakir presents a balanced portrait of al-Nu'aymi, a scholar praised as the most complete in Baghdad but also noted to have a blemish. Through the eyes of his contemporaries, we see how Muslim biographers recorded both strengths and weaknesses, teaching us to evaluate scholars holistically.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once through. Notice the chains of narration and the key statements about al-Nu'aymi.
2
Identify al-Nu'aymi's qualities
From the text, list the positive attributes: knowledge of hadith, kalam, adab, Shafi'i fiqh, and being 'complete'.
Also note the dream vision.
3
Understand the 'blemish'
Al-Barqani says 'lola ba'u fihi' – a blemish. Consider what this might mean contextually: possibly a minor character trait, not a doctrinal failing.
The common misunderstanding is that this was a major flaw.
4
Reflect on balanced biography
Discuss how classical biographies include both praise and criticism, and how this teaches us to avoid hagiography or blanket condemnation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رواها أبو بكر الخطيب عن محمد بن الصوري عن النعيمي والله أعلم . أخبرنا الشيخ أبو منصور محمد بن عبد الملك المقرى ببغداد قال أخبرنا ، وأبو الحسن بن سعيد قال ثنا أحمد بن على بن ثابت الخطيب قال سمعت محمد بن على الصورى يقول لم أر ببغداد أحداً أكمل من النعيمي كان قد جمع معرفة الحديث والكلام والأدب ، ودرس شيئا من فقه الشافعي ، قال وكان أبو بكر البرقاني يقول هو كامل في كل شئ لولا بأو فيه ، قال وأخبرنا أحمد بن على الخطيب قال حدثنا البرقاني بعد موت النعيمي قال رأيت النعيمى في منامي بهيئة جميلة وحالة صالحة ، ثم قال البرقاني قد كان شديد العصبية في السنة وكان يعرف من كل علم شيئا ، مات النعيمي في يوم الاثنين مستهل ذى القعدة سنة ثلاث وعشرين وأربعمائة رحمه الله ومنهم أبو طاهر بن خراشة الدمشقى المقرى رحمه الله أخبرنا الشيخ الأمين أبو محمد هبة الله بن أحمد الأكفاني ، قال ثنا أبو محمد عبد العزيز بن أحمد بن محمد الكتاني قال توفى شيخنا أبو ظاهر الحسين ابن محمد بن عامر الإبلى المقرى إمام جامع دمشق يوم الاربعاء السابع من شهر ربيع الآخر من سنة ثمان وعشرين وأربعمائة ، حدث عن يوسف بن القسم الميانجى والحسين بن إبراهيم بن أبى الزمزام الفرائضى وغيرهما ، وكان ثقة نبيلا مأمونا يذهب إلى مذهب الأشعرى الأستاذ أبو منصور النيسابورى المعروف بالبغدادي
Abu Bakr al-Khatib narrated it from Muhammad al-Suri from al-Nu'aymi, and God knows best. The Shaykh Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Muqri' informed us in Baghdad, saying: we were informed, and Abu al-Hasan ibn Sa'id said: Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Khatib narrated to us, saying: I heard Muhammad ibn Ali al-Suri say: I have not seen in Baghdad anyone more complete than al-Nu'aymi. He had gathered the knowledge of hadith, kalam, and adab, and studied some of Shafi'i fiqh. He said: And Abu Bakr al-Barqani used to say: He is complete in everything except for a blemish in him. He said: And Ahmad ibn Ali al-Khatib informed us, saying: al-Barqani narrated to us after the death of al-Nu'aymi, saying: I saw al-Nu'aymi in a dream in a beautiful appearance and a good state. Then al-Barqani said: He was intensely partisan for the Sunnah, and he knew something of every science. Al-Nu'aymi died on Monday, the beginning of Dhu al-Qi'dah, the year 423 AH, may God have mercy on him. And among them is Abu Tahir ibn Kharasha al-Dimashqi al-Muqri', may God have mercy on him. The trustworthy Shaykh Abu Muhammad Hibat Allah ibn Ahmad al-Akfani informed us, saying: Abu Muhammad Abd al-Aziz ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Kattani narrated to us, saying: Our shaykh Abu Tahir al-Husayn ibn Muhammad ibn Amir al-Abli al-Muqri', the imam of the Damascus Mosque, died on Wednesday, the 7th of Rabi' al-Akhir, the year 428 AH. He narrated from Yusuf ibn al-Qasim al-Mayanji and al-Husayn ibn Ibrahim ibn Abi al-Zimzam al-Fara'idi and others. He was trustworthy, noble, reliable, and followed the Ash'ari madhhab of the master Abu Mansur al-Naysaburi known as al-Baghdadi.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage presents two biographical entries. The first concerns al-Nu'aymi, praised by al-Suri as the most complete person in Baghdad, having knowledge of hadith, kalam, and adab, and some Shafi'i fiqh. Al-Barqani qualifies this praise by noting a 'blemish' in him, though he later sees him in a good dream and describes him as intensely partisan for the Sunnah. The second entry is about Abu Tahir ibn Kharasha al-Muqri', the imam of the Damascus Mosque, who died in 428 AH. The narrators testify to his trustworthiness and note that he followed the Ash'ari school (madhhab) of Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi. This explicitly links a scholar of this period to the Ash'ari theological tradition.

Key Terms
النعيمي
البرقاني
بأو

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that a scholar with a 'blemish' is unreliable or of low status.
Correction: The text shows al-Nu'aymi was considered the most complete scholar in Baghdad despite a minor blemish, and his dream vision affirms his good state. Biographers recorded such nuances without dismissing his overall excellence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did al-Barqani say about al-Nu'aymi after his death?
A) He was a complete scholar in every respect.
B) He saw him in a dream in a beautiful state and said he was intensely partisan for the Sunnah.
C) He said he was untrustworthy.
D) He said he rejected the Ash'ari madhhab.

Key Takeaway
Classical biographies balance praise and criticism, teaching us to evaluate scholars holistically without hagiography or blanket condemnation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of someone you know—a teacher, a friend, or a public figure—who has both strengths and a clear flaw. How do you habitually treat that person? Do you magnify the flaw or acknowledge the good? What would it take for you to see them as al-Suri and al-Barqani saw al-Nu'aymi: complete except for a blemish? Write down one step you can take this week to correct your imbalance.
?
Al-Barqani saw al-Nu'aymi in a beautiful dream after death, confirming his good state despite the blemish. If your life were to end today, what would the people who know your weaknesses say about you in a dream? Are there 'blemishes' in your own character that you have dismissed as minor but that might prevent others from seeing you as complete? Name one and commit to addressing it this month.
?
The source says al-Nu'aymi was 'intensely partisan for the Sunnah.' What are you intensely partisan for? Is your partisanship for truth, or for your own opinions and habits? Examine your loyalties: do they align with the Sunnah as you understand it, or with something else? What would it cost you to realign them, and are you willing to pay that price?

Abu Tahir ibn Kharasha: A Trustworthy Ash'ari Imam
Ibn Asakir narrates the death and praise of Abu Tahir ibn Kharasha, noting his Ash'ari affiliation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how this biographical entry explicitly associates a scholar with the Ash'ari madhhab and confirms his trustworthiness.

Core Idea
Abu Tahir ibn Kharasha was a trustworthy imam who followed the Ash'ari school.

This second part of the passage presents the biography of Abu Tahir ibn Kharasha, the imam of the Damascus Mosque. Through a chain of narrators, we learn of his death date, his teachers, and his reputation for trustworthiness. Significantly, the text explicitly states he followed the Ash'ari madhhab of Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi, providing a clear link to the Ash'ari theological tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage

2
Identify biographical details
List the facts: name, death date, teachers, and that he was imam of Damascus Mosque.
3
Note the Ash'ari affiliation
The text explicitly says 'yadhhabu ila madhhab al-Ash'ari'. This is a direct statement of his theological school.
The master is Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi, a key Ash'ari theologian.
4
Reflect on historical significance
Consider how such entries help us trace the spread of Ash'ari theology among scholars of the period.

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
5 min
Identifying Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi
al-Sabuni insists on specifying the full name to avoid confusion with another theologian.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why early Ash'ari scholars insisted on precise naming to avoid confusion with the Maturidi theologian.

Core Idea
Precision in names preserves doctrinal boundaries.

This passage from Ibn Asakir shows how Abu Uthman al-Sabuni corrected a narrator to write the full name of Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi. The concern was that simply saying 'Abu Mansur' could refer to the Maturidi scholar. This lesson highlights the importance of scholarly exactness.

Guided Path
1
Read the identification narrative
Read how al-Marandi initially omitted the name and how al-Sabuni insisted on adding 'Abd al-Qahir ibn Tahir' to avoid ambiguity.
Note the phrase 'لئلا يظن أنك أردت أبا منصور الآخر'.
2
Consider the doctrinal context
Reflect on why confusion between Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi (Ash'ari) and another Abu Mansur (likely al-Maturidi) was problematic. The lesson points to a 'خلاف في الاعتقاد' (difference in belief).
3
Read al-Sabuni's praise
After the identification, al-Sabuni praises al-Baghdadi as a leading imam. This shows the high regard despite the need for precision.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حدثنى الشيخ أبو بكر يحيى بن إبراهيم بن أحمد بن محمد السلماسى عن أبيه القاضي أبي طاهر قال قال أبو على الحسن بن نصر بن كاكا المرندى الفقيه في ذكر أبي عثمان الصابوني أنه ذكر أبا منصور المتكلم ، قال أبو على وكنت قد أهملت ذكر اسمه ونسبه اعتماداً على شهرته فقال لى أبو عثمان قيد ذكره بإثبات اسمه وأزل الشبهة عن فأثبت فوق الكنية عبد القاهر بن طاهر لئلا يظن أنك أردت أبا منصور الآخر ، فكأنه أشار إلى خلاف في الاعتقاد كان بينهما ومهما نفيت الاحتمال والشركة ورفعت الظن والشبهة بان أنى أردت ببياني أبا منصور البغدادي ثم قال أبو عثمان كان من أئمة الأصول وصدور الإسلام بإجماع أهل الفضل والتحصيل ، بديع الترتيب غريب التأليف في التهذيب يراه الجلة صدرا مقدما ويدعوه الأئمة إماما مفخما ومن خراب نيسابور أن اضطر مثله إلى مفارقتها إلى حيث خلق منه وتوفی باسفراین وبها قبره رحمه الله
وقال أبو على المرندى وحدثني أبو عبد قال لما حصل أبو منصور باسفراين ابتهج الناس بمقدمه إلى الحد الذي لا يوصف، فلم يبق إلا يسيرا حتى مات واتفق أهل العلم على دفنه يجنب أبى إسحق إبراهيم بن محمد المتكلم الاسفراينى فقبراهما متجاوران تجاور تلاصق كأنهما نجمان جمعهما مطلع وكوكبان ضمهما برج مرتفع قال : وإنما انتقل إلى أسفراين لأن حالها كان بعد متماسكاً بعض التماسك
كتب إلى الشيخ أبو الحسن عبد الغافر بن إسماعيل النيسابوري قال فی ذیل تاریخ نيسابور : عبد القاهر بن طاهر بن محمد البغدادى أبو الأستاذ الإمام الكامل ذو الفنون الفقيه الأصولي الأديب الشاعر النحوى الماهر في علم الحساب ، العارف بالعروض ورد نيسابور مع أبيه أبي طاهر وكان ذا مال وثروة ومروءة وتفقه على أهل العلم والحديث وأنفق ماله على أهل العلم حتى افتقر صنف في العلوم وأربى على أقرانه في الفنون ودرس فى سبعة عشر نوعاً من العلوم وكان قد درس على الاستاذ أبي إسحاق الاسفراينى وأقعده بعده في مسجد عقيل للاملاء مكانه وأملى سنين واختلف إليه الأئمة فقروا عليه مثل الإمام ناصر المروزي وأبى القسم القشيري وغيرهما وحدث عن الإسماعيلي وأبي أحمد بن عبدی خرج من نيسابور في أيام التركمانية وفتنتهم إلى أسفراين فمات بها سنة تسع وعشرين وأربعماية .
Shaykh Abu Bakr Yahya ibn Ibrahim ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Salamasi narrated to me from his father, the judge Abu Tahir, who said: Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Nasr ibn Kaka al-Marandi the faqih said, in mentioning Abu Uthman al-Sabuni, that he mentioned Abu Mansur the mutakallim (theologian). Abu Ali said: I had neglected to mention his name and lineage, relying on his fame. So Abu Uthman said to me: 'Restrict his mention by setting down his name and remove ambiguity.' So I set down above the kunyah (patronymic) 'Abd al-Qahir ibn Tahir, lest it be thought that you meant the other Abu Mansur. It was as if he pointed to a disagreement in belief that was between them. And whenever you negate the possibility and association and raise the suspicion and ambiguity, it becomes clear that I intended by my statement Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi. Then Abu Uthman said: 'He was among the imams of usul (principles of religion) and the foremost of Islam by consensus of the people of virtue and attainment. Wonderful in arrangement, unique in composition in refinement. The great ones see him as a foremost leader, and the imams call him a magnified imam. And from the ruin of Nishapur is that one like him was compelled to leave it to where he was created, and he died in Isfarayin, and there is his grave, may God have mercy on him.' And Abu Ali al-Marandi said: Abu Abdullah narrated to me, saying: When Abu Mansur arrived in Isfarayin, the people rejoiced at his arrival to an extent that cannot be described. He remained only a short time until he died. The people of knowledge agreed to bury him next to Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Muhammad the mutakallim al-Isfarayini. Their two graves are adjacent, attached, as if they are two stars joined by a rising point, and two planets gathered by a lofty tower. He said: He only moved to Isfarayin because its condition was still somewhat stable. The Shaykh Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Ghafir ibn Ismail al-Naysaburi wrote to me, saying in the supplement to the History of Nishapur: 'Abd al-Qahir ibn Tahir ibn Muhammad al-Baghdadi, Abu al-Ustadh (father of the master), the complete imam, possessor of many arts, the faqih, the usuli, the adib, the poet, the grammarian, the skilled in arithmetic, the knower of prosody. He came to Nishapur with his father Abu Tahir, and he had wealth, riches, and chivalry. He studied fiqh with the people of knowledge and hadith. He spent his wealth on the people of knowledge until he became poor. He authored works in the sciences and excelled his peers in the arts. He taught in seventeen types of sciences. He had studied under Ustadh Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini, and after him he appointed him in the Mosque of 'Uqayl for dictation in his place, and he dictated for years. The imams would frequent him and read to him, such as Imam Nasir al-Marwazi and Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri and others. He narrated from al-Isma'ili and Abu Ahmad ibn 'Abd [something]. He left Nishapur during the days of the Turkomans and their strife to Isfarayin, and he died there in the year 429 AH.'
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part biographical entry for Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi (Abd al-Qahir ibn Tahir). It begins with a narrative from al-Marandi and al-Sabuni, emphasizing the need to precisely identify Abu Mansur by his full name and kunyah to avoid confusion with another scholar of similar name. Al-Sabuni describes him as an imam of usul and a foremost scholar of Islam, praising his works and lamenting the necessity of his departure from Nishapur. The second part describes his warm reception in Isfarayin and his burial next to Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini, symbolically comparing their graves to stars. The third part is a formal biographical notice from Abd al-Ghafir al-Naysaburi, detailing his vast knowledge across seventeen sciences, his teachers, his students (including Nasir al-Marwazi and al-Qushayri), his generosity, and his eventual death in Isfarayin in 429 AH due to Turkoman strife.

Key Terms
أبو منصور البغدادي
عبد القاهر بن طاهر
أبو عثمان الصابوني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think there is only one famous Abu Mansur in Islamic theology.
Correction: This passage shows there were at least two: Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi (Ash'ari) and another Abu Mansur (likely al-Maturidi). Careful identification is needed to avoid confusing distinct theological schools.

Checkpoint
Why did Abu Uthman al-Sabuni instruct the narrator to specify 'Abd al-Qahir ibn Tahir'?
A) To honor his lineage
B) To avoid confusion with another Abu Mansur
C) Because he had forgotten his name
D) To assert his Ash'ari affiliation

Key Takeaway
This lesson shows how early Ash'ari scholars carefully identified Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi to prevent confusion with the Maturidi theologian, highlighting the importance of precision in scholarly transmission.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you refer to a scholar's opinion in your own discussions, do you ensure you have the correct person in mind, or do you rely on general reputation? How can you verify accuracy starting today?
?
The great imam Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi was forced to leave Nishapur due to its ruin. Have you ever neglected or undervalued a scholar because of circumstances? What can you do to seek knowledge from those who are overlooked?
?
This lesson shows a small act of precision that prevented a major confusion. What vague attribution in your own understanding needs to be clarified right now—and what step will you take by the end of this week to resolve it?
